Admission of Receiving Counterfeit Dirhams
Ruling that one who admits receiving dirhams and claims they are counterfeit is believed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a party who admits receiving dirhams but then claims they were counterfeit, and explain the reasoning (talil) based on the genus of counterfeit dirhams and the scope of receipt.

Core Idea
A person who admits receiving dirhams but claims they were counterfeit is believed, because counterfeit dirhams are still dirhams and receipt is not limited to good quality.

This lesson examines a specific situation in judicial proceedings: when someone admits to receiving a sum of dirhams but later asserts they were counterfeit. The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on the nature of counterfeit dirhams and the concept of receipt (qabd). Understanding this ruling is important for judges and parties involved in financial claims.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the ruling
Read the passage: a person admits receiving ten dirhams, then claims they were counterfeit. The ruling is: he is believed (saddaq).
2
Identify the legal issue
The issue is whether his claim is credible after admitting receipt. Does admission imply the dirhams were good?
The answer hinges on the definition of dirhams and receipt.
3
Analyze the reasoning
The text gives the reason (talil): counterfeit dirhams (zuyuf) are from the genus of dirhams (jins al-darahim), just defective. They are still dirhams, and receipt (qabd) does not require good quality.
An analogy is made: transactions with counterfeit dirhams in sarf and salam are valid, showing they are treated as dirhams.
4
Apply the principle
Since receipt is not specific to good dirhams, the person's claim that he received defective ones is plausible. He is believed because he is denying that he received his due (good dirhams).
5
Note the exception
If he admitted receiving 'good dirhams' (jiyad) or 'his due' (haqq), he would not be believed if he later claims they were counterfeit, because that contradicts the earlier admission.
This distinction is crucial for understanding the boundaries of the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایک شخص نے اقرار کیا کہ میں نے فلاں شخص سے دس درہم قبضہ کیا پھر اس نے کہا کہ
کھوٹے ہیں۔ اس کی تصدیق کی جائے گی یا نہیں
قال ومن اقرانه قبض من فلان عشرة دراهم ثم ادعى انه زيوف صدق و في بعض النسخ اقتضى وهو عبارة عن القبص ايضاً ووجهه ان الزيوف من جنس الدراهم الا انها معيبة ولهذا لو تجوز بها في الصرف والسلم جاز والقبض لا يختص بالجياد فيصدق لانه انكر قبض حقه بخلاف ما اذا اقرانه قبض الجياد أو حقه أو
A person admitted: I received ten dirhams from so-and-so, then he said: They are counterfeit. Will he be believed or not? He said: And whoever admits that he received from so-and-so ten dirhams, then claims they are counterfeit, he is believed. In some copies, 'iqtada' which is also an expression for receipt. And the reason is that counterfeit dirhams are of the genus of dirhams, except that they are defective; for this reason, if one transacts with them in currency exchange or salam, it is valid. And receipt is not specific to good dirhams, so he is believed because he denied receiving his due. Unlike if he admitted receiving good dirhams or his due, or...
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage is a brief ruling with proof regarding the credibility of a person who admits receiving a sum of dirhams but then claims they were counterfeit. The ruling is that he is believed (saddaq). The proof is that counterfeit dirhams (zuyuf) are still a type of dirham, albeit defective; thus, receiving them is still receiving dirhams. Since receipt is not restricted to good (jiyad) dirhams, the person's claim that he received counterfeit ones is plausible and accepted. The text distinguishes the case where he admits receiving good dirhams or his due (haqq), where he would not be believed if he later claims they were counterfeit, because that would contradict his earlier admission. The Hanafi position is that the claimant's statement is taken as true because he is denying that he received what was actually his due (i.e., good dirhams), so he is effectively denying the receipt of the correct quality.

Key Terms
زيوف (zuyuf): Counterfeit or defective dirhams that are not pure silver or not of full weight, but still considered dirhams.
قبض (qabd): Taking possession or receipt, not limited to good quality items.
تصدیق (tasdiq): Giving credence or believing the claim in the absence of evidence to the contrary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, why is a person who admits receiving dirhams believed when he later claims they were counterfeit?
A) Because he is the defendant.
B) Because counterfeit dirhams are of the genus of dirhams and receipt is not specific to good ones.
C) Because he swore an oath.
D) Because the other party admitted.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a person who admits receiving dirhams but claims they were counterfeit is believed because counterfeit dirhams are still dirhams and receipt does not require good quality.

Claim of Defective Dirhams After Qabd: General vs Specific Acknowledgment
Expansion of a Hanafi ruling on claim of defective dirhams after qabd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the admissibility of a claim of defective dirhams after acknowledging possession and distinguish the cases based on the wording of the acknowledgment.

Core Idea
Acknowledging possession of dirhams does not imply they were good; later claiming defect is not contradictory unless the acknowledgment specified quality.

In Hanafi court procedure, a common issue arises when a person acknowledges taking possession of dirhams but later claims those dirhams were defective. The opposing party may argue that acknowledging possession of dirhams necessarily implies acknowledging good dirhams, making the later claim a contradiction. This passage from al-Hidayah explains the Hanafi response: possession (qabd) applies to both good and bad dirhams, so general acknowledgment does not preclude a later claim of defect—unless the acknowledgment explicitly or implicitly specified the dirhams were good. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the rules of evidence in financial disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The central issue: after acknowledging possession of dirhams, can a person later claim those dirhams were defective? The immediate objection is that such a claim contradicts the earlier acknowledgment. Your task is to recognise this conflict and understand why the Hanafi school finds it resolvable.
The objection rests on the assumption that a person's right is to receive good dirhams, so acknowledging possession implies receiving good dirhams.
2
Understand the Hanafi principle on qabd
The key principle: possession (qabd) is not specific to good dirhams. It literally applies to both good and bad dirhams. Therefore, a general acknowledgment 'I took possession of ten dirhams' does not by itself indicate the quality of those dirhams. This is the foundational premise for accepting the later claim.
Qabd is a physical act; it does not describe the quality of what is possessed.
3
Distinguish general vs specific acknowledgment
The passage details scenarios where the acknowledgment is general (e.g., 'I took possession of dirhams') versus specific (e.g., 'I took possession of pure dirhams', 'my right', 'the price', 'fully received'). When the wording indicates goodness, the later claim of defect becomes contradictory and is rejected. Otherwise, the claim is accepted with an oath.
Specific wording can be explicit (pure dirhams) or implicit (my right, the price) because those terms imply good dirhams in context.
4
Apply the types of defective dirhams
Not all defective dirhams are treated alike. Ziyuf (bad but accepted by merchants) and naqira (rejected by merchants but still dirhams) are considered dirhams, so claiming them after general acknowledgment is acceptable. SatUqa (where silver is overcome by alloy) are not dirhams, so claiming them contradicts the acknowledgment of possessing dirhams.
The critical factor is whether the defective coin still belongs to the genus (jins) of dirhams.

Source Text

ستلزم ہوتا ہے۔ اور اس کا حق دراہم جیاد میں تھا تو مقر کا مطلقا درا ہم پر قبضہ کے اقرار لوستلزم ہوا ۔ یعنی گو یا مقر نے دراہم جیاد پر قبضہ کا اقرار کیا ہے اور جب مقر دراہم جیاد پر قبضہ کا اقرار کر چکا اقرار کرنا ہے۔ اور اسی طرح جب اس نے یہ کہا کہ میں نے اپنا ثمن وصول کر لیا ہے کیونکہ یمن بھی درا ہم جیاد ہوتے ہیں نہ کہ درا ہم زیوف ۔ پس شمن پر قبضہ کا اقرار کرنا ایسا ہے جیسے دراہم جیاد پر قبضہ کا اقرار کیا ہو۔ اسی طرح جب اس نے لفظ استونی کہا یعنی میں پورے طور پر وصول کر چکا تو بھی دراہم جیاد پر قبضہ کا اقرار ہوگا۔ کیونکہ پورے طور پر وصول کرنا اسی وقت ہوتا ہے جب وصف نام کے ساتھ قبضہ کیا گیا ہو۔ اور وصف تام جودت ہے نہ کہ زیافت ۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ اس صورت میں بھی مقر نے دراہم جیاد پر قبضہ کا اقرار کیا ہے۔ پس جب مذکورہ صورتوں میں صراحۃ یا دلالہ دراہم جیاد پر قبضہ کا اقرار کر چکا تو اب اس کے بعد زیوف ہونے کا دعویٰ کرنا اس کے قول میں تناقض پیدا کرے گا۔ اور تناقض کی صورت میں چونکہ دعوی قابل سماعت نہیں ہوتا۔ اس لئے مذکورہ صورتوں میں بھی مقر کا دعوی زیوف قابل سماعت اور معتبر نہ ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ نہرہ درہم، دراہم کے مانند ہیں یعنی کسی نے کہا کہ میں نے فلاں سے دس درہم پر قبضہ کیا ہے اور پھر دعوی کیا کہ وہ در اہم شہرہ ہیں تو اس کی تصدیق کی جائے گی ۔ جیسا کہ زیوف کا دعوی کرنے کی صورت میں تصدیق کی جاتی ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ جس طرح درا ہم زیوف، دراہم کی جنس سے ہیں اسی طرح دراہم نہرہ بھی دراہم کی جنس سے ہیں۔ لیکن اگر درا ہم پر قبضہ کے اقرار کے بعد ان کے ستوقہ ہونے کا دعویٰ کیا تو یہ دعوی مقبول نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ستوقہ دراہم ، دراہم کی جنس سے نہیں ہیں۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر قبضہ سے پہلے ان دراہم کے بدلے جو بدل صرف یا راس المال ہیں دراہم ستوقہ دیدئیے تو جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ دراہم ستوقہ چونکہ دراہم کی جنس سے نہیں ہیں اس لئے قبضہ سے پہلے بدل صرف اور راس المال کے عوض دراہم ستوقہ کا لینا نا جائز ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے زیوف وغیرہ کی تفسیر کرتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ زیوف وہ دراہم ہیں جن کو بیت المال کھوٹا قرار دیکر رد کر دے مگر تاجر لوگ اپنے معاملات میں ان کو لے لیتے ہیں۔ اور نہر جہ (نہرہ ) وہ دراہم ہیں جن کو تاجر لوگ بھی رد کر دیتے ہیں ۔ گویا نہ جہ، زیوف سے گھٹیا ہوتے ہیں مگر ہوتے در اہم ہی ہیں۔ اور ستوقہ وہ دراہم کہلاتے ہیں جن میں کھوٹ غالب اور چاندی مغلوب ہو۔ گویا وہ درہم ہی نہیں ہیں۔
From the statement 'Possession is not specific to good dirhams' and so forth, it is an answer to a question. The question is: When the acknowledging person acknowledged possession of ten dirhams, it is as if he acknowledged possession of his right. Because acknowledgment of possession necessitates acknowledgment of possession of his right. And his right was in good dirhams, so the acknowledging person's absolute acknowledgment of possession of dirhams necessitated that he acknowledged possession of good dirhams. And when he has already acknowledged possession of good dirhams, then afterwards claiming that these dirhams are bad would be a contradiction in his statement. And in case of contradiction, the claim is not admissible. Therefore, his claim that these dirhams are bad should not be admissible. The answer to this is that possession is not specific to good dirhams; rather, it occurs in both good dirhams and bad dirhams. So if someone says 'I took possession of ten dirhams', this possession applies to both good dirhams and bad dirhams. Meaning, it could be that those ten dirhams are good, or it could be that they are bad. Since possession is not specific to good dirhams, acknowledging possession of ten dirhams does not necessitate acknowledging possession of good dirhams. And if acknowledging possession of ten dirhams does not necessitate acknowledging possession of good dirhams, then claiming after possession that they are bad does not create a contradiction in the acknowledging person's statement. Rather, the acknowledging person is a denier of having possessed his right, and the statement of a denier is accepted with an oath. Therefore, the one who acknowledged possession of ten dirhams, since he is a denier of possession of his right, his statement is accepted and he is believed. However, if someone acknowledged 'I took possession of ten pure dirhams' or 'I took possession of my right' or 'I took possession of the price' or 'I fully received', then if he afterwards claims that these dirhams are bad, he will not be believed. That is, his claim of defect is not admissible. Because he has explicitly or implicitly acknowledged possession of good dirhams. In the first case, the acknowledgment is explicit; in the second, because he said 'I took possession of my right' and his right is in good dirhams. So acknowledging possession of his right is acknowledging possession of good dirhams. Similarly, when he said 'I received my price' because the price is also good dirhams, not bad dirhams. So acknowledging possession of the price is like acknowledging possession of good dirhams. Similarly, when he said the word 'istawfaytu' (I fully received), then also it is an acknowledgment of possession of good dirhams. Because full receipt only occurs when possession is taken with the complete quality, and the complete quality is goodness, not defect. So it becomes clear that in this case as well, the acknowledging person has acknowledged possession of good dirhams. When in the mentioned cases he explicitly or implicitly acknowledged possession of good dirhams, then after that claiming badness would create a contradiction in his statement, and in case of contradiction, the claim is not admissible. Therefore, in those cases, the claim of badness is not admissible or accepted. The author of al-Hidayah says: 'Naqira dirhams are like dirhams' i.e., if someone says 'I took possession of ten dirhams from so-and-so' and then claims that they are naqira, he will be believed, just as he is believed in the case of claiming they are ziyuf. The conclusion is that just as ziyuf dirhams are of the category of dirhams, so too naqira dirhams are of the category of dirhams. But if after acknowledging possession of dirhams, he claims that they are satuqa, this claim will not be accepted. Because satuqa dirhams are not of the category of dirhams. For this reason, if before possession, in exchange for those dirhams which are the price in exchange or capital, satuqa dirhams are given, it is not permissible. Because satuqa dirhams are not of the category of dirhams, so accepting satuqa dirhams before possession for the price in exchange or capital is impermissible. The author of al-Hidayah, interpreting ziyuf and others, said: Ziyuf are dirhams which the treasury rejects as defective, but merchants accept them in their transactions. Naqira (or nahra) are dirhams which even merchants reject. So naqira are inferior to ziyuf, but they are still dirhams. SatUqa are dirhams in which the defect is predominant and silver is overcome; they are not dirhams at all.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of a ruling from al-Hidayah regarding the claim of defective dirhams after acknowledging possession. The issue arises when a person acknowledges that he took possession of ten dirhams from someone, but later claims those dirhams were actually bad (ziyuf). The potential objection is that acknowledging possession of dirhams implies possessing one's right, which is in good dirhams, so later claiming badness would be contradictory. The response, based on Hanafi reasoning, is that possession (qabd) is not specific to good dirhams; it applies to both good and bad dirhams. Therefore, mere acknowledgment of possession of dirhams does not necessitate that they were good. Thus, the later claim of badness is not a contradiction; rather, the person is effectively denying that he received his right (which is good dirhams), so his statement is accepted with an oath. However, if the acknowledgment explicitly or implicitly specified good dirhams (e.g., by saying 'pure dirhams', 'my right', 'the price', or 'fully received'), then the claim of badness is contradictory and inadmissible. The passage then distinguishes three types of defective dirhams: ziyuf (bad but accepted by merchants), naqira (even merchants reject, but still dirhams), and satuqa (where defect overwhelms silver, effectively not dirhams). Claiming satuqa after acknowledging possession of dirhams is not accepted because satuqa are not considered dirhams. This distinction has practical implications in contracts like sarf and mudarabah.

Key Terms
قبض (qabd): Possession; taking physical control of the dirhams.
زیوف (ziyuf): Bad dirhams that the treasury rejects but merchants accept in transactions.
نہرہ (naqira (or nahra)): Dirhams that even merchants reject, but still fall under the category of dirhams.
ستوقہ (satuqa): Dirhams where defect predominates and silver is overcome; they are not considered dirhams.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person acknowledges 'I took possession of ten dirhams from Zaid' and later claims they were satuqa, is his claim accepted?
A) Yes, because possession does not specify quality.
B) Yes, because satuqa are still dirhams.
C) No, because satuqa are not dirhams, so claiming them contradicts the acknowledgment.
D) No, because he already acknowledged possession of good dirhams.

Key Takeaway
The admissibility of a claim of defective dirhams after acknowledging possession depends on whether the acknowledgment was general or specified quality, and whether the defect type is still considered dirhams.

Ruling on Acknowledgment of Debt Rejected by Muqarr Lahu
Explaining that rejection nullifies iqrar bil-dayn but not iqrar bil-bay'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a muqarr lahu rejects an iqrar bil-dayn and distinguish it from iqrar bil-bay'.

Core Idea
An acknowledgment of debt is nullified if the recipient rejects it; but a sale acknowledgment is not so easily undone.

The Hanafi school recognises that a person may acknowledge a debt, but the creditor has the right to reject that acknowledgment, effectively nullifying it. This may seem counterintuitive—why would a creditor refuse money? But it prevents manipulation and preserves the integrity of claims. In contrast, an acknowledgment of a sale contract cannot be nullified by one party, because a contract requires mutual consent to rescind.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon: an acknowledgment of debt (iqrar bil-dayn) that is rejected by the muqarr lahu. The ruling is that after rejection, the iqrar is nullified, and the muqir is not liable for the debt.
The rejection (radd) is a unilateral act of the muqarr lahu.
2
Understand the effect of rejection
In Hanafi law, the muqarr lahu can unilaterally reject an iqrar bil-dayn. Once rejected, the iqrar is void ab initio. Any subsequent statement by the muqir is treated as a new claim (da'wa), not an acknowledgment.
If the muqarr lahu later changes his mind and attests, it is ineffective because the iqrar no longer exists.
3
Contrast with iqrar bil-bay'
If a person acknowledges a sale (e.g., 'You bought from me'), and the other party denies it, the acknowledgment is not nullified by rejection. The sale contract is a bilateral agreement, so rescission requires mutual consent. Therefore, the denying party can later attest to the sale, and his attestation is valid.
The difference hinges on the nature of the right: debt is a right of the creditor alone; contract rescission is a joint right.
4
Apply the ruling to the given scenario
In the scenario: Khalid says to Hamid, 'I owe you 1000 dirhams.' Hamid says, 'You owe me nothing.' Then Khalid says, 'Rather, you owe me 1000 dirhams.' The first statement (iqrar) is nullified by Hamid's rejection. The second statement is a claim, requiring proof or Hamid's admission. Since neither is present, Khalid is not liable.
Even if Hamid later admits, the admission would not revive the iqrar because it was already void.
5
Explain the underlying rationale (ta'lil)
The Hanafi position is based on the principle that the muqarr lahu has exclusive authority over the iqrar bil-dayn because it is his right. In a contract, rights are shared, so one party cannot unilaterally nullify it.
This reasoning is consistent with the maxim: 'Al-umur bi-maqasidiha' – acts are judged by intentions. The muqarr lahu's rejection indicates he does not want the debt, so the iqrar has no effect.

دونوں مسئلوں کے درمیان فرق ظاہر ہو گیا ہے۔
A person said to another: 'You have one thousand dirhams on me.' He said: 'I have nothing on you.' Then the first said: 'Rather, you have one thousand dirhams on me.' Then nothing is due from him. Because his first acknowledgment was rejected by the muqarr lahu, and the second is a claim, so a proof or the opponent's attestation is required. Contrary to if one said to another: 'You bought (from me),' and the other denied; still he may attest to it because one of the two contracting parties cannot unilaterally rescind, just as he cannot unilaterally conclude the contract. The meaning is that it is the right of both, so the contract remains and the attestation takes effect. As for the muqarr lahu, he can unilaterally reject the acknowledgment, so they differ. The translation explains: If one person said to another: 'You have 1000 dirhams on me,' and the other said: 'I have nothing on you,' then the first said in the same place: 'Rather, you have 1000 dirhams on me,' then nothing is due from him. Because his first acknowledgment was nullified by the rejection of the muqarr lahu, and the second is a claim requiring proof or attestation. Contrary to if one said: 'You bought,' and the other denied; the first may still attest because one contracting party cannot unilaterally rescind, just as he cannot conclude the contract alone; rescission is a right of both. So the contract remains and attestation is effective. But the muqarr lahu can unilaterally reject the acknowledgment, so they differ. The commentary elaborates: The scenario is that Khalid says to Hamid: 'I owe you 1000 dirhams.' Hamid responds: 'You owe me nothing.' Then Khalid says: 'Rather, you owe me 1000 dirhams.' Khalid is not liable. The reason: Khalid's first statement is an acknowledgment, which is nullified by Hamid's rejection. The second is a claim, which requires proof or Hamid's admission. If after rejection Hamid were to attest, it would not be accepted. However, if Hamid first attested and then rejected, it would not be accepted. For the claim, Khalid must either present proof or Hamid must attest. In contrast, if Khalid said 'You bought this slave from me' and Hamid denied, Hamid's later attestation would be valid because one party cannot unilaterally rescind a sale contract; rescission requires both parties. Thus the difference between iqrar bil-dayn and iqrar bil-bay' is that the former is nullified by the muqarr lahu's rejection, while the latter is not. The reason is that rescission of a contract is a right of both parties, so rejection by one does not nullify it. Our discussion has clarified the difference between the two issues.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_statement with detailed reasoning. It begins with a scenario: Person A (Khalid) says to Person B (Hamid): 'I owe you 1000 dirhams.' Hamid denies: 'You owe me nothing.' Khalid then says: 'Rather, you owe me 1000 dirhams.' The ruling: Khalid is not liable for anything. The reasoning is that Khalid's first statement was an acknowledgment (iqrar) of debt. That acknowledgment was rejected (radd) by Hamid (the muqarr lahu). In Hanafi law, an acknowledgment of debt (iqrar bil-dayn) can be unilaterally rejected by the person in whose favor it is made, thereby nullifying it. So Khalid's acknowledgment is gone. His second statement is a claim (da'wa) against Hamid, which requires proof (bayyinah) or Hamid's admission to be established. Since neither is present, Khalid is not liable. The text then contrasts this with an acknowledgment of sale (iqrar bil-bay'). If Khalid says 'You bought this slave from me' and Hamid denies, the acknowledgment is not nullified by rejection. Because a sale contract cannot be unilaterally rescinded; rescission is a joint right. So if Hamid later attests to the sale, his attestation is valid and effective. The key difference is that in iqrar bil-dayn, the muqarr lahu has the exclusive right to reject, while in iqrar bil-bay', both parties have rights, so one party's rejection does not nullify the contract. The passage emphasizes that the muqarr lahu's rejection makes the iqrar invalid, and any subsequent attestation by him is ineffective.

Key Terms
اقرار (iqrar): A declaration by a person (muqir) that another person (muqarr lahu) has a right (like a debt) on him.
مقرلہ (muqarr lahu): The person in whose favor the acknowledgment is made; he has the right to reject it.
رد (radd): Rejection; the act of the muqarr lahu in refusing the acknowledgment.
دعوی (da'wa): A claim made by one party against another, requiring proof or admission to be established.

Key Terms from Source Passage

In the scenario where Khalid first acknowledges a debt to Hamid, and Hamid rejects it, then Khalid claims Hamid owes him 1000 dirhams, why is Khalid not liable for the debt?
A) Because Khalid retracted his acknowledgment, which is allowed only before rejection.
B) Because Hamid's rejection nullified the first acknowledgment, and the second statement is a claim without proof or admission.
C) Because the amount is unclear and must be witnessed.
D) Because acknowledgment of debt requires the presence of a judge.

Key Takeaway
Rejection by the muqarr lahu nullifies an iqrar bil-dayn, rendering it as if it never existed, but does not nullify an iqrar bil-bay'.

Acceptance of Evidence of Payment Despite Denial of Original Debt
Resolving conflicting evidence in a debt claim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on accepting evidence of payment despite prior denial, and evaluate Zufar's opposing argument using the principle of tawfiq (reconciliation).

Core Idea
Evidence of payment is accepted even after denial of debt because payment can be made to avoid litigation, reconciling the apparent contradiction.

In this passage from Al-Hidayah, we encounter a nuanced evidentiary scenario: a plaintiff claims a debt, the defendant denies any debt ever existed, yet the plaintiff proves the debt and the defendant proves payment. At first glance, the defendant's statements seem contradictory. The Hanafi school resolves this through the principle of tawfiq (reconciliation), while Imam Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) rejects the evidence. This lesson dissects the arguments and the governing legal maxim.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
Plaintiff claims wealth from defendant. Defendant says: 'You never had anything on me.' Plaintiff brings evidence (bayyinah) of a 1000 dirham debt. Defendant then brings evidence that he paid (qada') or was discharged (ibra') from that same debt.
Note the timing: the defendant first denies any obligation, then shows proof of fulfilling it.
2
Identify the Hanafi ruling
According to the matn (attributed to Imam Muhammad), the defendant's evidence of payment is accepted, and the plaintiff's evidence of the debt is effectively superseded.
The same applies for evidence of discharge (ibra').
3
Understand Zufar's objection
Imam Zufar argues that payment (qada') logically follows a valid obligation (wujub). Since the defendant denied any obligation ever existed, his subsequent claim of payment is contradictory (munaqid), and thus his evidence should be rejected.
Zufar's reasoning is based on the logical sequence: payment presupposes a debt.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond that reconciliation (tawfiq) between the two statements is possible. A person may pay something that was not rightfully due solely to avoid litigation (دَفعاً للخصومة). This is evidenced by the common expression 'He paid a false debt' (قضى بباطل). Thus, the defendant's denial of a genuine debt does not preclude his later payment for other reasons.
The text emphasizes 'التوفيق ممكن' (reconciliation is possible) and 'التوفيق أظهر' (reconciliation is more apparent).
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah)
If the defendant's evidence is accepted, he avoids double payment. If Zufar's view were followed, the plaintiff would win despite the defendant having actually paid. The matn adopts the Hanafi position, and it is the mufta bihi.
This highlights the importance of procedural fairness: evidence is evaluated holistically, not in isolation.

ایک نے دوسرے پر مال کا دعوی کیا مدعی علیہ نے کہا تیرا مجھ پر کچھ نہیں تھا، مدعی نے ایک ہزار درہم پر مبینہ قائم کر دیئے، مدعی علی نے ادا کرنے پر بینہ قائم کر دیئے تو کس کے بینہ قبول ہوں گے
قال ومن ادعى على اخر مالاً فقال ماكان لك على شئ قط فاقام المدعى البينة على الف واقام هو البينة على القضأ قبلت بينته وكذلك على الابراء و قال زفر لا تقبل لان القضاء يتلوا لوجوب و قد انكره فيكون مناقضاً ولنا ان التوفيق ممكن لان غير الحق قد يُقضى ويبرأ منه دفعاً للخصومة الاترى انه يقال قضى بباطل وقد يصالح على شئ فيثبت ثم يقضى وكذا اذا قال ليس لك على شئ قط لان التوفيق اظهر ترجمہ اگر ایک شخص نے دوسرے پر مال کا دعوی کیا۔ پس مدعی علیہ نے کہا کہ تیر مجھ پر بھی کچھ نہیں تھا۔ پس مدعیان ایک ہزار پر پینہ قائم کر دیا۔ اور مدعی علیہ نے ادا کرنے پر مبینہ قائم کیا تو مدعی علیہ کا بینہ قبول ہوگا۔ اور اسی طرح بری کرنے پر ۔ اور امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ مدعی علیہ کامہینہ قبول نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ادا کرنا وجوب کے بعد ہوتا ہے۔ حالانکہ اس نے وجوب کا انکار کیا ہے۔ تو وہ مناقض ہوگا۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ توفیق ممکن ہے اس لئے کہ کبھی خصومت دفع کرنے کے لئے غیر حق کو بھی ادا کر دیا جاتا ہے۔ اور اس سے برأت کر لی جاتی ہے۔ کیا ہیں دیکھتے ہو کہ یہ کہا جاتا ہے اس نے ناحق ادا کیا اور کبھی ایک چیز پر صلح کی جاتی ہے۔ پس یہ چیز ثابت ہوکر ادا کی جاتی ہے۔ اور ایسے ہی جب کہا تیرا مجھ پر ہر گز کچھ نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ تو فیق اظہر - تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے دوسرے پر مال کا دعوی کیا۔ پس مدعی علیہ نے کہا کہ تیرا مجھ پر کبھی کچھ نہیں تھا۔ یعنی مدعی
One person claimed wealth from another; the defendant said: 'You never had anything on me.' The plaintiff brought evidence of 1000, and the defendant brought evidence of payment. So which evidence is accepted? He said: 'If one claims wealth from another, and he says: 'You never had anything on me,' and the plaintiff brings evidence of 1000, and he brings evidence of payment, then his evidence is accepted. Similarly on discharge. Zufar said: It is not accepted, because payment follows the obligation, and he denied the obligation, so he is contradictory. Our evidence is that reconciliation is possible, because sometimes a person pays and is discharged from something that is not right, to avoid litigation. Do you not see that it is said, 'He paid a false debt'? And sometimes a person settles for something, then it is established and then paid. Likewise when he says 'You never had anything on me' because reconciliation is more apparent. Translation: If one person claimed wealth from another, and the defendant said: 'You never had anything on me,' and the plaintiff brought evidence of 1000, and the defendant brought evidence of payment, then the defendant's evidence is accepted. Similarly on discharge. Imam Zufar said that the defendant's evidence is not accepted because payment follows the obligation, and he denied the obligation, so it is contradictory. Our evidence is that reconciliation is possible, because sometimes a person pays what is not right to avoid litigation, and he is discharged from it. Do you not see that it is said, 'He paid a false debt'? And sometimes a person settles for something, then it is established and then paid. Likewise when he said 'You never had anything on me' because reconciliation is more apparent. Commentary: The scenario is that one person claimed wealth from another; the defendant said: 'You never had anything on me.' ...

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The scenario: plaintiff claims money from defendant; defendant says 'you never had anything on me.' Plaintiff brings evidence of a 1000 dirham debt. Defendant then brings evidence that he already paid that 1000 dirhams. The question: whose evidence is accepted? The ruling (from the matn, attributed to Imam Muhammad) is that the defendant's evidence of payment (qada') is accepted. The same applies for evidence of discharge (ibra'). Imam Zufar disagreed: he argued that payment logically presupposes an obligation (wujub), but the defendant denied any obligation ever existed. Thus, his evidence of payment contradicts his earlier denial, so it should not be accepted. The Hanafi response (from the matn) is that reconciliation (tawfiq) between the two statements is possible. A person might pay a debt that was not actually due just to avoid litigation (دفعاً للخصومة). There is even a common saying: 'He paid a false debt.' Similarly, one might settle a dispute and then pay. So the defendant's evidence of payment is not necessarily contradictory to his denial; it can be explained as a payment made despite the absence of a genuine debt. Therefore, his evidence is accepted. The principle is that if two pieces of evidence can be reconciled, they should be. The passage emphasizes that this reconciliation is more apparent (اظہر). The commentary elaborates the scenario but the window cuts off.

Key Terms
بینہ (bayyinah): Evidence, usually consisting of two witnesses or equivalent proof.
قضاء (qada'): Payment or execution of a debt.
ابراء (ibra'): Discharge or release from a debt; evidence that the creditor absolved the debtor.
توفیق (tawfiq): Reconciliation or harmonization of apparently conflicting statements or evidence.
مناقض (munaqid): Contradictory; a statement that conflicts with another statement made by the same person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because payment does not require a valid debt; it can be made to avoid litigation.
B) Because the plaintiff's evidence is weaker.
C) Because the defendant can change his statement.
D) Because the court presumes payment in doubtful cases.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts evidence of payment despite a prior denial of debt, reconciling the two statements through the possibility of paying to avoid litigation.

Effect of Rejection on Acknowledgment of Debt vs. Sale
Explains the legal difference between iqrar of debt and iqrar of sale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi ruling on acknowledgment of debt and acknowledgment of sale regarding the addressee's rejection, and explain the underlying reasoning based on the bilateral nature of sale.

Core Idea
Debt acknowledgment is undone by rejection; sale acknowledgment survives because one party cannot rescind a bilateral contract alone.

In this lesson, we examine a nuanced Hanafi rule concerning the effect of the addressee's rejection on an acknowledgment (iqrar). The ruling differs dramatically based on whether the acknowledgment concerns a debt (dayn) or a sale (bay'). By understanding the legal reasoning (ta'lil) rooted in contract law, you will see how the Hanafi school maintains coherence across the law of evidence and obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two cases: iqrar bi al-dayn (acknowledgment of a debt) and iqrar bi al-bay' (acknowledgment of a sale). In each, the addressee (muqarr lahu) rejects the acknowledgment. Note the different outcomes.
The same pattern applies to any unilateral vs. bilateral obligation.
2
State the effect of rejection
Acknowledge that rejection nullifies the debt acknowledgment entirely, but leaves the sale acknowledgment intact. After rejection, any later confirmation by the addressee is invalid for debt but valid for sale.
This is the core ruling.
3
Analyze the legal reasoning (ta'lil)
The passage analogizes the sale contract: just as one party cannot unilaterally conclude a sale, one party cannot unilaterally rescind it. Rescission is a bilateral right. Therefore, the addressee's rejection does not rescind the sale, so the acknowledgment stands and later confirmation is effective. In contrast, debt acknowledgment is unilateral, so the addressee can nullify it alone.
This reasoning (talil) is what distinguishes the two cases.
4
Apply the principle to a new situation
Test your understanding: if Zayd acknowledges to Amr that he gifted a house to Amr, and Amr rejects the gift, does the rejection nullify the acknowledgment? Use the reasoning: a gift (hiba) is not a bilateral contract? Actually, hiba is a contract that can be completed by delivery, but is it bilateral? Consider the Hanafi classification.
This step prepares you for the practice tasks.

اقرار حامد کے رد کرنے سے رد ہو گیا تو مقر یعنی خالد پر کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ چنانچہ اگر رد کرنے کے بعد مقرلہ نے مقر کی تصدیق کی تو اس کی تصدیق معتبر نہ ہوگی ۔ لیکن اگر مقرلہ مقر کے اقرار کی تصدیق کر دے اور پھر اس اقرار کو رد کرے تو اب یہ اقرار نہ ہوگا۔ اور رہا دوم یعنی خالد کا حامد پر ایک ہزار درہم کا دعویٰ تو اس کو ثابت کرنے کے لئے یا تو خالد بینہ پیش کرے یا خصم یعنی حامد اس کی تصدیق کرے۔ اس کے برخلاف اگر خالد نے حامد سے کہا کہ تو نے مجھ سے یہ غلام خریدا ہے۔ اور حامد نے انکار کر دیا تو انکار کے بعد بھی حامد اگر خالد کے قول کی تصدیق کر دے تو یہ تصدیق کرنا درست اور معتبر ہوگا۔ پس اقرار بالدین اور اقرار بالبیع کے مسئلہ کے درمیان فرق یہ ہوا کہ اقرار بالدین، مقرلہ کے رد کرنے سے رد ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور اقرار بالبیع مقرلہ کے رد کرنے سے رد نہیں ہوتا۔ اور وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ احد العاقدین جس طرح تنہا عقد بیع کو منعقد نہیں کر سکتا۔ اسی طرح تنہا اس کو فسخ بھی نہیں کر سکتا۔ کیونکہ فسخ دونوں عاقدوں کا حق ہے تو مقرلہ یعنی حامد کے رد کرنے سے عقد بیع فسخ نہ ہوگا ۔ اور جب حامد کے رد کرنے کے باوجود عقد بیع باقی رہا تو رد کرنے کے بعد حامد کا تصدیق کرنا کار آمد اور مفید ہوگا۔ اور جب حامد کا تصدیق کرنا مفید اور کارآمد ہے تو اس کی تصدیق کا اعتبار بھی ہوگا۔ اور رہا اقرار بالدین کا مسئلہ تو اقرار بالدین کو مقرلہ تنہا رد کر سکتا ہے۔ اور جب مقرلہ تنہا اقرار بالدین کو رد کر سکتا تو اس کے رد کرنے کے بعد اقرار بالدین باقی نہیں رہتا۔ اور جب اقرار بالدین باقی نہ رہا تو رد کرنے کے بعد مقرلہ کا تصدیق کرنا بھی معتبر نہ ہوگا۔ ہماری مذکورہ تقریر سے اقرار بالدین اور اقرار بالبیع دونوں مسئلوں کے درمیان فرق ظاہر ہو گیا ہے۔
When Hammad's rejection caused the acknowledgment to be rejected, then no obligation falls on the acknowledger, Khalid. So if after rejection the addressee confirms the acknowledger's statement, that confirmation will not be valid. But if the addressee first confirms the acknowledgment and then rejects it, then this acknowledgment will not be (valid). As for the second, that is Khalid's claim of one thousand dirhams against Hammad, to prove it either Khalid presents evidence or the opponent, Hammad, confirms it. In contrast, if Khalid said to Hammad, 'You bought this slave from me,' and Hammad denied, then even after denial if Hammad confirms Khalid's statement, this confirmation is valid and acceptable. So the difference between acknowledgment of debt and acknowledgment of sale is that acknowledgment of debt is nullified by the addressee's rejection, while acknowledgment of sale is not nullified by the addressee's rejection. And the reason for the difference is that just as one party to a contract cannot conclude a sale contract alone, similarly one party cannot rescind it alone, because rescission is the right of both parties. So the sale contract is not rescinded by the addressee Hammad's rejection. And when the sale contract remains despite Hammad's rejection, then Hammad's confirmation after rejection is effective and beneficial. And when Hammad's confirmation is beneficial, it is also considered valid. As for the case of acknowledgment of debt, the addressee alone can nullify the acknowledgment of debt. And when the addressee alone can nullify it, then after his rejection the acknowledgment of debt does not remain. And when the acknowledgment of debt does not remain, then the addressee's confirmation after rejection is not valid. From our above discussion, the difference between acknowledgment of debt and acknowledgment of sale is clear.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage, from the commentary on Al-Hidayah, discusses a crucial distinction in Hanafi fiqh regarding the effect of the addressee's rejection on two types of acknowledgment (iqrar). The ruling is that an acknowledgment of debt (iqrar bi al-dayn) is nullified if the addressee (muqarr lahu) rejects it. However, an acknowledgment of a sale (iqrar bi al-bay') is not nullified by the addressee's rejection. The reasoning (ta'lil) is based on the nature of the transaction: a sale is a bilateral contract (aqd), so one party cannot unilaterally rescind it. Thus, even if the addressee rejects the acknowledgment of sale, the underlying contract remains, and a later confirmation by the addressee is valid. In contrast, an acknowledgment of debt is a unilateral act, so the addressee can reject and nullify it; thereafter, any confirmation is ineffective. This distinction is practical in court: a defendant who initially denies a sale can later be held to his acknowledgment if he confirms it, whereas for a debt, denial is final. The author follows the order: first, the ruling for debt, then for sale, then the difference and its cause.

Key Terms
اقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment or confession of a right or debt.
مقر (muqir): The person who makes the acknowledgment.
مقرلہ (muqarr lahu): The person in whose favor the acknowledgment is made; the addressee.
دین (dayn): Debt; a financial obligation.
بیع (bay'): Sale; a contract transferring ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is an acknowledgment of sale not nullified by the addressee's rejection according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because a sale contract requires witnesses.
B) Because a sale is a bilateral contract that cannot be rescinded by one party.
C) Because the addressee's rejection is considered invalid in sale cases.
D) Because the acknowledgment of sale is stronger than debt.

Key Takeaway
The effect of rejection on an acknowledgment depends on whether the underlying transaction is unilateral (debt) or bilateral (sale); only unilateral acknowledgments are nullified by the addressee's rejection.

Accepting Defendant's Evidence of Payment After Denial
Ruling on whose evidence (claimant or defendant) is accepted when both present proof in a debt claim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on accepting defendant's evidence of payment after denial, and evaluate the opposing view of Zufar and Ibn Abi Layla using the concept of tawfiq.

Core Idea
Evidence of payment after denying debt is accepted because payment may be without obligation (tawfiq resolves contradiction).

In a financial dispute, a defendant first denies any debt, then brings evidence that he paid. The Hanafi school, led by Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, accepts this evidence. However, Imam Zufar and Ibn Abi Layla argue that payment presupposes obligation, so the denial contradicts the claim of payment, making the evidence invalid. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind the Hanafi position, focusing on the principle of tawfiq (reconciliation) and its application in court.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: the defendant's evidence of payment (or discharge) is accepted even after he has denied any obligation. Note that this is the view of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani (Zahir al-Riwayah).
This is the mufta bihi (operative) position.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Name the opposing scholars: Imam Zufar and Ibn Abi Layla. They reject the defendant's evidence because they see a contradiction: payment implies a prior obligation, which the defendant denied.
This is an inter-madhhab ikhtilaf within the broader Hanafi tradition (Zufar and Ibn Abi Layla are early Hanafi authorities).
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the opponent's dalil: payment (ada') necessarily follows obligation (wujub). If the defendant denies any obligation, then claiming payment is logically contradictory (munaqadah). A contradictory claim is invalid, so evidence on an invalid claim is rejected.
This is a strict qiyas reasoning.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response uses tawfiq (reconciliation): payment can occur without a legal obligation, e.g., a false payment to settle a dispute or a settlement where a right is established then paid. Thus, the defendant's statements can be harmonized: 'You had nothing rightful against me, but I paid to avoid litigation.' No contradiction remains.
This is an example of istihsan (juristic preference) overriding strict qiyas.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: In a Hanafi court, the defendant's evidence is accepted and the case is dismissed; under Zufar's view, the defendant's evidence is rejected and the claimant's evidence prevails, so the debt is enforced.
The Hanafi position is considered more equitable as it prevents a potential injustice where a defendant who paid informally is forced to pay again.

Source Text

قال ومن ادعى على اخر مالاً فقال ماكان لك على شئ قط فاقام المدعى البينة على الف واقام هو البينة على القضأ قبلت بينته وكذلك على الابراء و قال زفر لا تقبل لان القضاء يتلوا لوجوب و قد انكره فيكون مناقضاً ولنا ان التوفيق ممكن لان غير الحق قد يُقضى ويبرأ منه دفعاً للخصومة الاترى انه يقال قضى بباطل وقد يصالح على شئ فيثبت ثم يقضى وكذا اذا قال ليس لك على شئ قط لان التوفيق اظهر
ترجمہ اگر ایک شخص نے دوسرے پر مال کا دعوی کیا۔ پس مدعی علیہ نے کہا کہ تیرا مجھ پر بھی کچھ نہیں تھا۔ پس مدعی نے ایک ہزار پر بینہ قائم کر دیا۔ اور مدعی علیہ نے ادا کرنے پر بینہ قائم کیا تو مدعی علیہ کا بینہ قبول ہوگا۔ اور اسی طرح بری کرنے پر ۔ اور امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ مدعی علیہ کا بینہ قبول نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ادا کرنا وجوب کے بعد ہوتا ہے۔ حالانکہ اس نے وجوب کا انکار کیا ہے۔ تو وہ مناقض ہوگا۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ توفیق ممکن ہے اس لئے کہ کبھی خصومت دفع کرنے کے لئے غیر حق کو بھی ادا کر دیا جاتا ہے۔ اور اس سے برأت کر لی جاتی ہے۔ کیا تم نہیں دیکھتے کہ یہ کہا جاتا ہے اس نے ناحق ادا کیا اور کبھی ایک چیز پر صلح کی جاتی ہے۔ پس یہ چیز ثابت ہوکر ادا کی جاتی ہے۔ اور ایسے ہی جب کہا تیرا مجھ پر ہر گز کچھ نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ تو فیق اظہر - تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے دوسرے پر مال کا دعوی کیا۔ پس مدعی علیہ نے کہا کہ تیرا مجھ پر کبھی کچھ نہیں تھا۔ یعنی مدعی علیہ نے زمانہ ماضی میں علی سبیل الاستغراق وجوب مال کی نفی کی ہے۔ پس مدعی نے اپنے دعوی پر بینہ پیش کیا اور مدعی علیہ نے اس بات پر بینہ پیش کیا کہ میں ادا کر چکا ہوں یا مدعی مجھ کو بری کر چکا ہے تو مدعی علیہ کا بینہ قبول ہوگا۔ اور امام زفر اور ابن ابی لیلی نے فرمایا کہ مدعی علیہ کا بینہ قبول نہ ہو گا۔
امام زفر اور ابن ابی لیلی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ادائیگی وجوب کے بعد ہوتی ہے۔ پس ادائیگی دین یا بری کرنے پر بینہ پیش کرنا اس بات کی علامت ہے کہ مدعی علیہ وجوب مال کا اقرار کرتا ہے حالانکہ وہ اس سے پہلے وجوب مال کا انکار کر چکا ہے۔ پس مدعی علیہ کے دعوی میں تناقض ہو گیا اور دعوی میں تناقض چونکہ دعوی کو فاسد کر دیتا ہے۔ اس لئے مدعی علیہ کا دین ادا کرنے یا مدعی کے بری کرنے کا دعوی فاسد ہوگا۔ اور بینہ چونکہ وہی قبول ہوتا ہے جو دعوی صحیحہ پر ہو۔ دعوی فاسدہ پر جو بینہ پیش کیا گیا ہو اس کو قبول نہیں کیا جاتا۔ اس لئے ادائے دین یا ابراء پر مدعی علیہ کا بینہ قبول نہ ہوگا۔ اور جب مدعی علیہ کا بینہ قبول نہ ہو تو وجوب دین پر مدعی کا بینہ قبول ہوگا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ مدعی علیہ کے وجوب مال کے انکار اور ادائے مال کے دعووں میں توفیق دینا ممکن ہے۔ اس لئے کوئی تناقض نہ ہوگا۔ اور توفیق اس لئے ممکن ہے کہ کبھی کبھی جھگڑا دور کرنے کے لئے ناحق مال کو بھی ادا کر دیا جاتا ہے اور اس سے برأت حاصل کر لی جاتی ہے۔ حتی کہ کہا جاتا ہے قضی باطل ، جیسا کہ قضی بحق کہا جاتا ہے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ ادائیگی جس طرح بجا اور حق طریقہ پر ہوتی ہے اسی طرح بیجا اور ناحق طور پر بھی ہوتی ہے، اسی طرح اگر مدعی علیہ کسی کے حق کا انکار کر دے پھر مدعی سے کچھ لے دے کر صلح کر لے تو وہ حق ثابت ہو کر ادا ہو گا۔ یعنی وہ حق پہلے ناحق طریقہ پر ثابت ہوا اور پھر اس کو ادا کیا گیا اس سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ اداء مال ناحق طور پر بھی ہوتا ہے۔ پس مدعی علیہ کا یہ کہنا کہ تیرا مجھ پر کبھی کچھ نہیں تھا اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ بجا اور حق طور سے مجھ پر کبھی کچھ واجب نہیں ہوا۔ اور مدعی علیہ کے ادا کرنے کے دعوی کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ تیرا مجھ پر گرچہ حق طور پر واجب نہیں تھا مگر میں نے جھگڑے سے بچنے کے لئے بغیر وجوب کے ناحق طور پر اتنامال ادا کر دیا ہے جس کا تو مدعی ہے۔ آپ ملاحظہ فرمائیے مدعی علیہ کے اس دعوی میں کتنا تناقض ہے۔ یعنی کوئی تناقض نہیں ہے۔ پس جب مدعی علیہ کے دعوی میں کوئی تناقض نہیں ہے تو مدعی علیہ کی طرف سے مال ادا کرنے یا بری کر دینے کا دعوی بھی درست ہوگا۔ اور جب مدعی علیہ کا دعوی درست ہے تو اس پر قائم کردہ بینہ بھی قبول کر لیا جائے گا۔
اسی طرح اگر ایک آدمی نے دوسرے پر مال کا دعوی کیا اور مدعی علیہ نے انکار کر دیا یعنی یہ کہا کہ تیرا مجھ پر ہرگز کچھ نہیں ہے پھر مدعی نے اپنے دعوی پر اور مدعی علیہ نے ادائے مال پر بینہ پیش کر دیا تو بھی مدعی علیہ کا بینہ قبول ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں مدعی علیہ کے قول میں توفیق زیادہ ظاہر ہے۔ اس طور پر کہا "لیس لک علی شیء قط" میں لفظ "لیس" حال کی نفی کے لئے ہے۔ یعنی مدعی علیہ کہتا ہے کہ زمانہ حال میں مدعی کا مجھ پر ہرگز کچھ واجب نہیں ہے اور اس نے بینہ اس بات پر قائم کیا کہ مدعی علیہ زمانہ حال سے پہلے ادا کر چکا یا مدعی زمانہ حال سے پہلے اس کو بری کر چکا ہے۔ پس جب ادائیگی یا ابراء کا دعوی زمانہ حال سے پہلے ہے اور وجوب مال کی نفی زمانہ حال میں ہے تو مدعی علیہ کے قول میں تناقض نہ ہوگا۔ اور جب تناقض نہیں ہے تو مدعی علیہ کی طرف سے مال پر پیش کردہ بینہ بھی قبول کر لیا جائے گا۔
He said: And whoever claims property from another and he says, 'You never had any right against me,' then the claimant presents evidence of one thousand, and he (the defendant) presents evidence of payment, his evidence is accepted, and similarly for discharge. Zufar said: It is not accepted because payment follows obligation, and he has denied it, so it is contradictory. And our evidence is that reconciliation is possible because sometimes non-right is paid and one is discharged from it to avoid litigation. Don't you see that it is said 'he paid falsely'? And sometimes a settlement is made on something, then it is established then paid. And likewise when he says 'You have nothing against me at all' because reconciliation is more apparent.
Translation: If a person claims property from another, then the defendant says, 'You had nothing against me,' then the claimant presents evidence of one thousand, and the defendant presents evidence of payment, then the defendant's evidence will be accepted, and similarly for discharge. Imam Zufar said that the defendant's evidence will not be accepted because payment occurs after obligation, yet he has denied obligation, so it is contradictory. Our evidence is that reconciliation is possible because sometimes non-right is paid and discharge is obtained to avoid litigation. Don't you see that it is said 'he paid falsely'? And sometimes a settlement is made on something, so it is established then paid. And likewise when he says 'You have nothing against me at all' because reconciliation is more apparent.
Explanation: The case is that a person claims property from another. The defendant says, 'You never had anything against me,' meaning the defendant has denied obligation in the past comprehensively. Then the claimant presents evidence on his claim, and the defendant presents evidence that he has paid or the claimant has discharged him. Then the defendant's evidence will be accepted. Imam Zufar and Ibn Abi Layla said that the defendant's evidence will not be accepted.
The evidence of Zufar and Ibn Abi Layla is that payment occurs after obligation. So presenting evidence of payment or discharge indicates that the defendant acknowledges the obligation, whereas he had previously denied it. So there is a contradiction in the defendant's claim, and since contradiction invalidates a claim, the defendant's claim of payment or discharge is invalid. And since evidence is only accepted for a valid claim, evidence presented on an invalid claim is not accepted. Therefore, the defendant's evidence for payment or discharge will not be accepted. And when the defendant's evidence is not accepted, the claimant's evidence for obligation will be accepted. Our evidence is that reconciliation between the defendant's denial of obligation and his claim of payment is possible, so there is no contradiction. Reconciliation is possible because sometimes false payment is made to avoid litigation, and discharge is obtained. So much so that it is said 'he paid falsely,' just as 'he paid rightly' is said. This shows that payment can occur both rightly and wrongly. Similarly, if a defendant denies someone's right, then settles with the claimant by giving something, that right becomes established and then paid. So the right first becomes established in a non-right way and then paid. This also shows that payment of property can occur wrongly. So the defendant's saying 'You never had anything against me' means that justly and rightly nothing was ever obligatory on me. And his claim of payment means that even though it was not obligatory on me rightly, I paid that amount to avoid dispute without obligation. See how much contradiction there is in the defendant's claim? That is, there is no contradiction. So when there is no contradiction in the defendant's claim, his claim of payment or discharge is valid. And when his claim is valid, the evidence presented on it will be accepted.
Similarly, if a person claims property from another, and the defendant denies, i.e., says 'You have nothing against me at all,' then the claimant presents evidence on his claim and the defendant presents evidence of payment, then also the defendant's evidence will be accepted because in this case reconciliation in the defendant's statement is more apparent. In this way, the word 'lis' in 'Laysa laka 'alayya shay'un qattu' is for negation of the present, i.e., the defendant says that in the present time there is no obligation upon him from the claimant, and he presents evidence that the defendant paid before the present time or the claimant discharged him before the present time. So when the claim of payment or discharge is from before the present time and the negation of obligation is in the present time, there is no contradiction in the defendant's statement. And when there is no contradiction, the evidence presented by the defendant on payment will be accepted.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents a classical Hanafi ruling on evidence in financial claims. The case: a claimant (mudda'i) alleges a debt, the defendant (mudda'a 'alayh) denies any obligation, then both bring evidence: claimant for the debt, defendant for payment or discharge. The Hanafi position, attributed to Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, is that the defendant's evidence is accepted, and the claimant's is rejected. Imam Zufar and Ibn Abi Layla disagree, arguing the defendant contradicts himself by denying obligation then claiming payment. The Hanafi response uses tawfiq (reconciliation): it is possible that the defendant paid the money without legal obligation, e.g., to settle a dispute ('paid falsely'). Thus no contradiction. The commentary further explains that if the denial uses the present tense ('You have nothing against me now'), reconciliation is even clearer because payment could have been made earlier. This is a classic example of istihsan (juristic preference) over qiyas (analogy). The passage is a ruling with proof (dalil) and an inter-madhhab dispute (Hanafi vs. Zufar/Ibn Abi Layla).

Key Terms
بینہ (bayyinah): Legal evidence, usually two male witnesses or one male and two females.
مدعی (mudda'i): The claimant or plaintiff who brings a claim.
مدعی علیہ (mudda'a 'alayh): The defendant against whom the claim is made.
توفیق (tawfiq): Reconciliation or harmonization between apparently contradictory statements.
مناقضہ (munaqadah): Contradiction in legal statements, rendering a claim invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position, why is the defendant's evidence of payment accepted even after he has denied any obligation?
A) Because the defendant's denial is considered false.
B) Because reconciliation (tawfiq) is possible—payment may have been made without legal obligation.
C) Because the claimant's evidence is automatically weaker.
D) Because the defendant always has the right to change his statement.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts a defendant's evidence of payment after denying debt because tawfiq (reconciliation) allows for the possibility of non-obligatory payment, avoiding strict logical contradiction.

8 min
Defendant's Evidence After Denial: Tawfiq vs. Tanazuq
Hanafi vs Zufar/Ibn Abi Layla on defendant's evidence after denial

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of tawfiq (reconciliation) to resolve apparent contradiction in a defendant's statements and determine when his evidence of payment or discharge is accepted.

Core Idea
Tawfiq over tanazuq: reconcile statements before declaring contradiction.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute on a practical court scenario: a defendant first denies any debt, then presents evidence that he paid or was discharged. How should the court treat his evidence? The Hanafi school, led by Abu Hanifa, applies the principle of tawfiq (reconciliation) to accept the evidence, while Zufar and Ibn Abi Layla see contradiction (tanazuq) and reject it. Understanding this distinction is crucial for legal practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defendant's two statements
The defendant first denies the debt (e.g., 'you have nothing on me ever'), then claims he paid or was discharged. What is the apparent conflict?
2
Apply the Hanafi rule of tawfiq
Can these statements be reconciled? Consider that denial of a just obligation does not preclude an unjust payment. Explore possibility of tawfiq.
The text gives examples like 'qada' batil'.
3
Analyze the opposing view (tanazuq)
Why do Zufar and Ibn Abi Layla see contradiction? They argue payment presupposes obligation, making denial and payment mutually exclusive.
Their proof: 'payment occurs after obligation.'
4
Evaluate the linguistic argument
The word 'laysa' (is not) negates the present state. How does this help reconcile? The denial refers to present, while payment is in the past.
Example: 'laysa laka 'alayya shay' qattu'.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical consequence? If defendant's evidence is accepted, he is free; if not, plaintiff's evidence prevails.
The ruling directly affects the outcome of the case.

جاتی ہے۔ حتی کہ کہا جاتا ہے قضی باطل ، جیسا کہ قضی بحق کہا جاتا ہے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ ادا ئیگی جس طرح بجا اور حق طریقہ پر ہوتی ہے اسی طرح بیجا اور ناحق طور پر بھی ہوتی ہے، اسی طرح اگر مدعی علیہ کسی بھی ہوتا ہے۔ پس مدعی علیہ کا یہ کہنا کہ تیرا مجھ پر بھی کچھ نہیں تھا اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ بجا اور حق طور سے مجھ پر کبھی کچھ واجب نہیں ہوا۔ اور مدعی علیہ کے ادا کرنے کے دعوی کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ تیرا مجھ پر گر چہ بھی واجب نہیں تھا۔ مگر میں نے جھگڑے سے بچنے کے لئے بغیر وجوب کے ناحق طور پر اتنامال ادا کر دیا ہے جس کا تو مدعی ہے۔ آپ ملاحظہ فرمائیے مدعی علیہ کے اس دعوی میں کتنا تناقض ہے۔ یعنی کوئی تناقض نہیں ہے۔ پس جب مدعی علیہ کے دعوئی میں کوئی تناقض نہیں ہے تو مدعی علیہ کی طرف سے مال ادا کرنے یا بری کر دینے کا دعوئی بھی درست ہوگا۔ اور جب مدعی علیہ کا دعوئی درست ہے تو اس پر قائم کر دہ مینہ بھی قبول کر لیا جائے گا۔ اسی طرح اگر ایک آدمی نے دوسرے پر مال کا دعوی کیا اور مدعی علیہ نے انکار کر دیا یعنی یہ کہا کہ تیرا مجھ پر ہرگز کچھ نہیں ہے پھر مدعی نے اپنے دعوئی پر اور مدعی علیہ نے ادائے مال پر بینہ پیش کر دیا تو بھی مدعی علیہ کا بینہ قبول ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں مدنی علیہ کے قول میں تو فیق زیادہ ظاہر ہے۔ اس طور پر کہا "لیس لک علی شنی قط" میں لفظ لیس" حال کی نفی کے لئے ہے۔ یعنی مدعی علیہ کہتا ہے کہ زمانہ حال میں مدعی کا مجھ پر ہرگز کچھ واجب نہیں ہے اور اس نے بینہ اس بات پر قائم کیا کہ مدعی علیہ زمانہ حال سے پہلے ادا کر چکا یا مدعی زمانہ حال سے پہلے اس کو بری کر چکا ہے۔ پس جب ادائیگی یا ابراء کا دعوئی زمانہ حال سے پہلے ہے اور وجوب مال کی نفی زمانہ حال میں ہے تو مد علی علیہ کے قول میں تناقض نہ ہوگا۔ اور جب تناقض نہیں ہے تو مدعی علیہ کی طرف سے مال پر پیش کردہ ہینہ بھی قبول کر لیا جائے گا۔
He denied the obligation of wealth in the past tense in a comprehensive manner. Then the plaintiff presented evidence (bayyinah) for his claim, and the defendant presented evidence (bayyinah) that he had paid or that the plaintiff had discharged him, so the defendant's evidence will be accepted. Imam Zufar and Ibn Abi Layla said that the defendant's evidence will not be accepted. The proof of Imam Zufar and Ibn Abi Layla is that payment occurs after obligation. Thus, presenting evidence on payment or discharge indicates that the defendant admits the obligation of wealth, whereas he had previously denied it. Hence, there is contradiction (tanazuq) in the defendant's claim, and contradiction corrupts the claim. Therefore, the defendant's claim of payment or discharge is invalid. Since evidence is only accepted for a valid claim, the evidence presented on an invalid claim is not accepted. So the defendant's evidence on payment or discharge will not be accepted. When the defendant's evidence is not accepted, the plaintiff's evidence on the obligation of the debt will be accepted. Our proof is that it is possible to reconcile (tawfiq) between the defendant's denial of obligation and his claim of payment. Hence, there is no contradiction. Reconciliation is possible because sometimes one pays unjustly to avoid conflict and obtains discharge. Thus it is said, 'qada' batil' just as 'qada' bi-haqq' is said. From this it is understood that payment can occur both justly and unjustly. Similarly, if a defendant denies someone's right and then settles with the plaintiff by giving something, the right becomes established and paid. That is, the right was first established unjustly and then paid. This also shows that payment of wealth can occur unjustly. So the defendant's statement 'You had nothing on me' means that justly and rightly nothing was ever wajib on me. And the defendant's claim of payment means: although nothing was wajib on me, I paid this amount unjustly without obligation to avoid conflict. Observe how much contradiction there is in this claim? That is, there is no contradiction. Since there is no contradiction in the defendant's claim, his claim of payment or discharge is valid. And when his claim is valid, the evidence established upon it will also be accepted. Similarly, if a person claims wealth from another and the defendant denies, saying 'You have absolutely nothing on me', then the plaintiff brings evidence for his claim and the defendant brings evidence on payment, even then the defendant's evidence will be accepted. Because in this case, reconciliation is even more apparent. For example, when he says 'laysa laka 'alayya shay' qattu' the word 'laysa' is for negation of the present state. That is, the defendant says: in the present time you have nothing wajib on me, and he establishes evidence that the defendant had paid before the present time or that the plaintiff had discharged him before the present time. Since the claim of payment or discharge is before the present time and the negation of obligation is in the present time, there is no contradiction in the defendant's statement. And when there is no contradiction, the defendant's evidence presented on the wealth will also be accepted.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning whether a defendant who first denies any debt can later present evidence that he has paid or been discharged. The Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa) holds that such evidence is accepted because the two statements can be reconciled: the denial refers to a just obligation, while the payment may have been made unjustly (e.g., to avoid harassment). Imam Zufar and Ibn Abi Layla argue that the statements are contradictory, invalidating the claim, so the evidence is rejected. The author (Ashraf ul Hadaya) supports the Hanafi position, demonstrating through examples like 'laysa laka 'alayya shay' qattu' (you have nothing on me ever) that reconciliation is possible by interpreting the denial as referring to the present state and the payment as a past event. The key principle is that tawfiq (reconciliation) is always sought before tanazuq (contradiction) in legal claims.

Key Terms
بینہ (bayyinah): Evidence (usually two male witnesses or one male and two females) presented in court to prove a claim.
تناقض (tanazuq): Contradiction between two statements of the same party that makes the claim invalid.
توفیق (tawfiq): Reconciliation between apparently conflicting statements to preserve their validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the defendant's evidence of payment accepted even after he denied the debt?
A) Because the denial is invalid
B) Because the statements can be reconciled: the denial refers to a just obligation, while payment may have been unjust
C) Because the plaintiff's evidence is always rejected
D) Because contradiction strengthens the claim

Key Takeaway
Tawfiq (reconciliation) takes precedence over tanazuq (contradiction) in assessing a defendant's statements, allowing his evidence of payment to be accepted even after denial.

Defendant's Denial of Knowledge and Its Effect on Evidence
Ruling on defendant's evidence when he denies knowing claimant

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the default Hanafi ruling on a defendant's evidence when he denies knowing the claimant, and evaluate al-Quduri's exception based on possible reconciliation.

Core Idea
A defendant who denies knowing the claimant cannot later claim payment unless reconciliation is possible.

In court, a defendant may deny both the debt and any acquaintance with the claimant. Then, to escape liability, he presents evidence that he already paid or was discharged. The Hanafi school's default position rejects such evidence, arguing that a transaction cannot occur without mutual knowledge. However, Imam al-Quduri presents a scenario where the evidence should be accepted because reconciliation is possible. This lesson explores the legal reasoning behind both views and their practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the default ruling and its rationale
Identify the default Hanafi ruling: the defendant's evidence is not accepted. Understand the rationale: tawfiq muta'azzir (reconciliation impossible) because a transaction requires mutual knowledge (dalil aqli).
Focus on the logical impossibility: denying knowledge negates any possibility of prior dealing.
2
Analyze al-Quduri's exception
Examine al-Quduri's scenario: a secluded person (muhtajib) or veiled woman (mukhadarah) pays a noisy claimant through a deputy without knowing him, then later recognizes him.
Here, the defendant's statements can be reconciled: he initially did not know the claimant but later learned his identity when the claim was made.
3
Compare the two positions
Contrast the default view (evidence not accepted) with Quduri's view (evidence accepted). Note that both rely on the same principle of tawfiq, but differ in whether reconciliation is possible in the given scenario.
The thamarah al-khilaf: if evidence is accepted, the defendant is freed; if not, the plaintiff's evidence prevails.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Identify the relied-upon position: the default view (not accepted) is the mufta bihi, but Quduri's view is recognized as a valid exception for special circumstances.
The author of Ashraf ul Hadaya presents both but does not explicitly resolve the ikhtilaf.

For there cannot be between two persons taking and giving, payment and receipt, transaction and settlement without mutual acquaintance. Al-Quduri mentioned that it is also accepted, because a secluded person (mujtabib) or a veiled woman (mukhadarah) may be harmed by clamor at his door, so he orders one of his deputies to placate him, not knowing him, then later recognizes him, so reconciliation is possible. Then later he recognizes him, so reconciliation is possible. Commentary: The matn author said: If a person claims wealth from another, and the defendant denies in these words: 'You had nothing on me and I do not recognize you', then the plaintiff brings evidence for his claim and the defendant brings evidence on payment or discharge, the defendant's evidence on payment or discharge will not be accepted. Because in this case, there is such a contradiction that it is impossible to remove and reconcile the two statements. And the reason is: when the defendant paid and gave money, then taking from the plaintiff and giving by the defendant, receiving by the plaintiff and paying by the defendant, in short a transaction and settlement occurred between both. And between two persons, without mutual recognition, lending and borrowing, payment and receipt, transaction and settlement cannot happen. So after the defendant says 'La a'rifuk' (I do not know you), claiming payment is invalid. And when the claim of payment is invalid, the evidence presented by the defendant is also not accepted. In sum, just as reconciliation was possible in the first two cases, here it is not possible. The author of Hidayah said: Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri mentioned that in this case the defendant's evidence is accepted. Because reconciliation is also possible here in the following way: The defendant may be a person whom people cannot see due to his dignity, and he himself does not like mixing with people, or the defendant is a veiled woman. Now the plaintiff comes daily to the defendant's door and makes noise and demands his debt. This useless action inevitably causes hardship to the noble householder. So the defendant, to rid himself of this trouble, orders one of his deputies to give the person some money to satisfy him and push him from the door, even though nothing was actually wajib on the defendant and he did not recognize him. Then when the plaintiff filed the claim and said that he is the same noisemaker, he recognized him. After this explanation, it is possible that the defendant first says 'You had nothing on me and I do not recognize you' and then claims payment. Because in the light of the above explanation, both statements can be combined. So when reconciliation is possible, the defendant's [evidence is accepted, but the text cuts off]

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific case where a defendant denies both the debt and any knowledge of the claimant, then presents evidence of payment or discharge. The default Hanafi ruling from the matn is that such evidence is not accepted because reconciliation is impossible: a transaction requires mutual knowledge, so denying knowledge negates the possibility of a prior transaction. However, al-Quduri (in his Mukhtasar) holds that the evidence can be accepted in certain scenarios, such as a secluded person or veiled woman who pays a noisy claimant through a deputy without initially knowing him, later recognizing him when the claim is made. The commentator (Ashraf ul Hadaya) explains both views, favoring the default ruling but acknowledging Quduri's exception. The key principle is that when reconciliation (tawfiq) between the defendant's statements is impossible, the evidence is rejected; when possible, it is accepted.

Key Terms
توفیق متعذر (tawfiq muta'azzir): Reconciliation between two statements is impossible due to factual impossibility (e.g., transaction requires mutual knowledge).
محتجب (muhtajib): A person who is secluded or not easily accessible due to dignity or social status.
مخدرة (mukhadarah): A woman who observes seclusion (purdah) and is not seen by unrelated men.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because the defendant is lying
B) Because reconciliation is impossible—a transaction cannot occur without mutual knowledge
C) Because the plaintiff's evidence is stronger
D) Because the defendant admitted the debt

Key Takeaway
The acceptance of a defendant's evidence depends on whether his statements can be reconciled; denial of knowledge normally bars evidence of payment, but exceptions exist.

Defendant's Denial of Knowledge and Evidence of Payment: General Rule and Exception
Intra-Hanafi dispute on evidence acceptance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the general Hanafi ruling on a defendant's contradictory statements and apply the exception recognized by Imam al-Quduri in cases where reconciliation is possible.

Core Idea
A defendant who denies knowledge cannot later claim payment — unless he proves an exceptional scenario that reconciles the statements.

This lesson examines a nuanced procedural issue: what happens when a defendant first states he neither owes anything nor knows the plaintiff, but then presents evidence of payment? The Hanafi school's default position rejects such evidence as contradictory. However, Imam al-Quduri introduces a valid exception for reclusive individuals or veiled women who paid through agents. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to distinguish between irreconcilable contradictions and plausible reconciliations in judicial reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defendant's two statements
The defendant says: (a) 'You have nothing against me' and (b) 'I do not know you.' Then he claims payment. Recognize that these two statements appear contradictory because payment implies a prior relationship. Note that the default ruling is non-acceptance of evidence.
The contradiction is between 'no knowledge' and 'payment'.
2
Analyze the legal basis for the default ruling
The Hanafi majority uses rational reasoning (dalil aqli): transactions require mutual knowledge. Therefore, claiming payment after denying knowledge is a contradiction (tanāquḍ) that makes the evidence unreliable.
The principle: taking, giving, paying, receiving cannot occur between strangers.
3
Examine al-Quduri's exception
Imam al-Quduri proposes a scenario: a reclusive man or veiled woman, pestered by a stranger, pays through an agent without knowing the plaintiff at the time. Later, recognizing the plaintiff, he can claim payment without contradiction.
This shows that reconciliation (tawfiq) is possible in specific contexts.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The general rule is applied in ordinary cases; the exception applies only when the defendant proves the special circumstances (seclusion, agency payment, later recognition). The mufta bihi for typical cases is the default ruling.
The burden of proof shifts to the defendant to show exceptional circumstances.
5
Apply the rule to a new scenario
Given a hypothetical case, decide whether the defendant's evidence should be accepted based on the reasoning of this lesson.
Practice using the tawfiq principle to evaluate contradictory statements.
