ولو قال ماكان لك على شئ ولا اعرفك لم يقبل بينته على القضاء و كذا على الابراء لتعذر التوفيق لانه لا يكون بين اثنين اخذ و اعطأ و قضاء واقتضاء ومعاملة ومصالحة بدون المعرفة وذكر القدوري انه تقبل أيضاً لان المحتجب او المخدرة قد يؤذى بالشعب على بابه فيأمر بعض وكلائه بارضائه ولا يعرفه ثم يعرفه بعد ذلك فامكن التوفيق
ترجمہ اور اگر اس نے یہ کہا کہ تیرا مجھ پر کبھی کچھ نہیں ہوا اور نہ میں تجھے پہچانتا ہوں تو اس کامہینہ قبول نہ ہوگا اور اسی طرح بری کرنے پر، کیونکہ توفیق دینا متعذر ہے۔ کیونکہ دو آدمیوں کے درمیان لین دین ادا کرنا اور وصول پانا معاملہ اور مصالحہ کرنا بغیر معرفت کے نہیں ہو سکتا۔ اور صاحب قدوری نے ذکر کیا کہ اس کامہینہ قبول ہوگا۔ کیونکہ متجب (اختلاط نہ رکھنے والا مرد) یا پردہ نشین عورت کبھی اپنے دروازے پر شور و شغب سے ایذاء پاتا ہے۔ پس اپنے بعض وکلاء کو حکم دیتا ہے کہ وہ شور مچانے والے کو راضی کر دے۔ حالانکہ وہ خود اس کو نہیں پہچانتا ہے۔ پھر اس کے بعد اس کو پہچان لیتا ہے تو تو فیق دینا ممکن ہے۔ تشریح ماتن علیہ الرحمۃ نے فرمایا کہ اگر ایک آدمی نے دوسرے پر مال کا دعوی کیا اور دوسرے آدمی یعنی مدعلی علیہ نے ان الفاظ میں انکار کیا کہ تیرا مجھ پر کچھ نہیں تھا اور نہ میں تجھ کو پہچانتا ہوں۔ پھر مدعی نے اپنے دعوئی پر بیتنہ پیش کیا۔ اور مدعی علیہ نے مال ادا کرنے پر یا مدعی کے بری کرنے پر بینہ پیش کیا تو مدعی علیہ کا ادا کرنے پر یا بری کرنے پر ہینہ قبول نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں مدعی علیہ کے قول میں ایسا تناقض ہے۔ جس کو رفع کرنا اور دونوں قولوں کے درمیان توفیق دینا ناممکن اور مستعد رہے اور مستعد راس لئے ہے کہ جب مدعلی علیہ نے اور مال دین ادا کیا ہو گا تو مدعی کی طرف سے لینا اور مدعی علیہ کی طرف سے دینا ، مدعی کی طرف سے وصول کرنا اور مدعلی علیہ کی طرف سے ادا کرنا پایا گیا الغرض دونوں کے درمیان ایک معاملہ اور مصالحہ ہوا۔ اور دو آدمیوں کے درمیان بغیر معرفت کے لین دین ادائیگی اور وصولیابی ، معاملہ اور مصالح نہیں ہو سکتا ۔ پس مدعلی علیہ کے لا اعر فک کہنے کے بعد ادائیگی کا دعوی کرنا غلط ہے۔ اور جب ادائیگی کا دعویٰ غلط ہے تو مدعلی علیہ کا پیش کردہ بعینہ بھی قبول نہ ہوگا۔ حاصل یہ کہ جس طرح پہلی دو صورتوں میں توفیق دینا ممکن تھا یہاں ممکن نہیں ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ شیخ ابوالحسن قدوری نے ذکر کیا کہ اس صورت میں مدعی علیہ کا بینہ قبول کر لیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں بھی توفیق دیناممکن ہے۔ اس طور پر کہ مدعی علیہ ایسا شخص ہو جس کو اس کی عزیمت کی وجہ سے لوگ دیکھ نہیں پاتے اور وہ خود بھی لوگوں سے اختلاط کو پسند نہیں کرتا یا مدعی علیہ پردہ نشین عورت ہو ۔ اب مدعی ہر روز مدعی علیہ کے دروازے پر آکر شور و غوغا کرتا ہے۔ اور اپنے دین کا تقاضا کرتا ہے۔اس بے ہودہ حرکت سے شریف صاحب خانہ کو اذیت کا پپہنچانا ایک لابدی امر ہے۔ پس مدعی علیہ نے اس مصیبت سے نجات پانے کے لئے اپنے کسی وکیل کو حکم دیا کہ وہ اس کو مال دے کر خوش کرے۔ اور دروازے سے دھکا دے حالانکہ مدعی علیہ پر حقیقتا کچھ واجب نہیں تھا۔ اور مدعی علیہ اس کو پہچانتا بھی نہ تھا۔ پھر جب مدعی نے دعوی کیا ، اور بتلایا کہ میں وہی شور کرنے والا ہوں ، تو پہچان گیا۔ اس تقریر کے بعد یہ بات ممکن ہے کہ مدعی علیہ پہلے یہ کہدے کہ تیرا مجھ پر کچھ نہیں تھا۔ اور میں تجھ کو پہچانتا نہیں ہوں ۔ اور پھر ادا کرنے کا دعوی کر دے۔ کیونکہ مذکورہ تقریر کی روشنی میں یہ دونوں باتیں جمع ہوسکتی ہیں۔ پس جب توفیق دینا ممکن ہے تو مدعی علیہ کے دعوئی میں کوئی تناقض نہ رہا۔ اور جب مدعی علیہ کے دعوئی میں کوئی تناقض نہ رہا تو مدعی علیہ کا دعوئی ادائیگی اور اس پر بینہ بالیقین قبول کر لیا جائے گا۔
Kitab al-Adab al-Qadi. If the defendant said, 'You never had anything against me and I do not know you,' his evidence (for payment or discharge) will not be accepted. And similarly for discharge, because reconciliation is impossible, since between two people taking and giving, paying and receiving, transaction and settlement cannot occur without knowledge. Al-Quduri mentioned that it is also accepted, because a reclusive man or a veiled woman may be annoyed by noise at his door, so he orders some of his agents to appease him, while he himself does not know him, then later he comes to know him, so reconciliation is possible. Translation: And if he said, 'You never had anything against me and I do not know you,' his evidence will not be accepted, and similarly for discharge, because reconciliation is impossible. Because between two people, taking and giving, paying and receiving, transaction and settlement cannot happen without knowledge. And Sahib al-Quduri mentioned that his evidence is accepted, because a reclusive man or a veiled woman is sometimes annoyed by noise and clamor at his door, so he orders one of his agents to appease the noisemaker, although he himself does not know him, then later he comes to know him, so reconciliation is possible. Commentary: The author (may Allah have mercy on him) said: If a person claims property from another, and the other (the defendant) denies in these words: 'You had nothing against me and I do not know you,' then the plaintiff presents evidence for his claim, and the defendant presents evidence for payment or for the plaintiff's discharge, the defendant's evidence for payment or discharge will not be accepted. Because in this case the defendant's statement contains a contradiction that cannot be removed and reconciliation between the two statements is impossible. For when the defendant made payment, there occurred taking from the plaintiff and giving from the defendant, receiving from the plaintiff and paying from the defendant; in short, there was a transaction and settlement between them. And between two people, taking and giving, payment and receipt, transaction and settlement cannot occur without knowledge. So after saying 'I do not know you,' claiming payment is invalid, and when the claim of payment is invalid, the defendant's presented evidence is also not accepted. In summary, just as in the first two cases reconciliation was possible, here it is not. The author of al-Hidayah said: Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri mentioned that in this case the defendant's evidence is accepted, because here too reconciliation is possible, in that the defendant is a person whom people do not see due to his seclusion and he himself does not like mixing with people, or the defendant is a veiled woman. The plaintiff comes daily to the defendant's door making noise and clamor and demanding his debt. This vulgar behavior necessarily causes distress to the honorable householder. So the defendant, to get rid of this affliction, orders some agent to give him some money to satisfy him and push him away from the door, although nothing was actually owed, and the defendant did not know him. Then when the plaintiff claimed and explained that he was the same noisemaker, the defendant recognized him. With this explanation, it is possible that the defendant first says, 'You had nothing against me and I do not know you,' and then claims payment, because these two statements can be reconciled in light of the above. So when reconciliation is possible, there is no contradiction in the defendant's claim, and when there is no contradiction, the defendant's claim of payment and his evidence are definitely accepted.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage addresses a procedural issue in court: if a defendant denies both the debt and any acquaintance with the plaintiff, can he later present evidence that he paid the debt or obtained a discharge? The ruling in the Hanafi school, as stated in the base text, is that such evidence is not accepted because the statements are contradictory. The reason is that payment or discharge implies some prior transaction, which cannot occur without the parties knowing each other. However, Imam al-Quduri raises an exception: if the defendant is a reclusive person or a veiled woman who was pestered by the plaintiff and paid through an agent without knowing the plaintiff at the time, then later recognized him, the statements can be reconciled. Therefore, in such a scenario, the evidence should be accepted. The commentary emphasizes that this is an intra-Hanafi difference: the general rule is refusal, but al-Quduri's view allows acceptance based on a plausible scenario. The author of al-Hidayah (presumably al-Marghinani) reports al-Quduri's position without fully adopting it, as the default remains the general rule unless the special circumstances are proven.

Key Terms
بینہ (bayyinah): Evidence or proof presented in court, typically by witnesses or documents.
توفیق (tawfiq): Reconciliation or harmonization of seemingly contradictory statements so that both can be true.
مناقض (munāqiḍ): Contradictory; a statement that conflicts with another statement from the same person, making reconciliation impossible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the general Hanafi ruling, why is the evidence of a defendant who says 'I never owed you and I don't know you' not accepted when he later claims payment?
A) Because the Quran prohibits accepting evidence from a defendant.
B) Because payment implies a prior transaction, which cannot happen between strangers.
C) Because the defendant must first admit knowledge, then deny the debt.
D) Because the plaintiff must also present evidence of the claim first.

Key Takeaway
A defendant's contradictory statements can be reconciled in exceptional circumstances, allowing his evidence to be accepted, but the default ruling is non-acceptance unless the exception is proven.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
8 min
Seller's Evidence of Immunity After Denying Sale
Intra-Hanafi dispute on accepting seller's evidence of immunity after denying sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school (Imam Muhammad) rejects the seller's evidence of immunity after denying the sale, and evaluate Imam Abu Yusuf's counter-argument based on qiyas.

Core Idea
A seller cannot claim immunity after denying the sale: contradiction invalidates the evidence.

In this lesson, we examine a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: a seller denies the sale, but later presents evidence that he included a condition of immunity from defects. Does the court accept such evidence? The majority ruling from Zahir al-Riwayah says no, because it's contradictory. But Imam Abu Yusuf argues by analogy to debt cases that it should be accepted if reconciliation is possible. Understanding this dispute sharpens your grasp of evidentiary consistency and the limits of qiyas in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
Identify the parties and their claims: buyer claims he bought a slave-girl; seller denies; buyer proves purchase with evidence; then discovers a defect; seller now presents evidence of an immunity clause. Observe the sequence.
The buyer seeks to return the slave-girl under khiyar al-'ayb.
2
Identify the Hanafi position (Imam Muhammad)
According to Imam Muhammad in al-Jami' al-Saghir, the seller's evidence is not accepted. The key reason: the condition of immunity (barā'ah) is part of the sale contract; if the seller denied the sale, he cannot later claim a condition that presupposes the sale's existence. This is a clear contradiction (tanāquḍ).
Zahir al-Riwayah supports this view.
3
Analyze Imam Abu Yusuf's opposing view
Imam Abu Yusuf accepts the evidence by qiyas to debt cases where a defendant first denies knowledge of a debt but later claims to have paid it. There, reconciliation is possible (e.g., forgetfulness). Here, similarly, the seller might have forgotten the sale initially and later remembered the condition.
Abu Yusuf's view is a minority opinion.
4
Examine the Hanafi response to Abu Yusuf's qiyas
The majority distinguishes debt from sale: a debt can be paid without a valid contract, so paying after denying is not necessarily contradictory. But a condition of immunity is intrinsically tied to the sale contract; if no sale occurred, the condition cannot exist. Thus, the contradiction is irreconcilable.
This shows how the school prioritizes logical consistency over analogical extension.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its implications
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Imam Muhammad's view: the seller's evidence of immunity is rejected. Practically, this means the buyer can return the defective slave-girl with full refund, and the seller cannot avoid liability by claiming an immunity condition.
The thamarah al-khilaf: the outcome for the buyer differs between the two views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایک شخص نے دوسرے پر دعویٰ کیا کہ اس نے اپنی باندی میرے ہاتھ فروخت کی ہے، مدعی علیہ نے انکار کیا۔ مدعی نے خریدنے پر بینہ قائم کر دیئے پھر باندی میں زائد انگلی پائی پھر مدعی علیہ نے ہینہ پیش کئے کہ بائع ہر عیب سے بری ہے تو مدعی کے پینہ قبول نہ ہوں گے
قال ومن ادعى على اخرانه باعه جاريته فقال لم ابعها منك قط فاقام البيئة على الشراء فوجد بها اصبعا زائدة فاقام البائع البيئة انه برئ اليه من كل عيب لم تقبل بيئة البائع وعن ابي يوسف انه تقبل اعتباراً بما ذكرنا وجه الظاهر ان شرط البراءة تغيير للعقد من اقتضا وصف السلامة الى غيره فيستدعى وجود البيع وقد انكره فكان مناقضاً بخلاف الدين لانه قد يقضى وان كان باطلا على مامر
ترجمہ امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں کہا کہ ایک شخص نے دوسرے پر دعوی کیا کہ اس نے اپنی باندی میرے ہاتھ فروخت کی ہے پس مدعلی علیہ نے کہا میں نے تیرے ہاتھ ہرگز فروخت نہیں کی ۔ پھر مدعی نے خریدنے پر ہینہ پیش کیا۔ پھر اس نے باندی میں ایک زائد انگلی پائی ۔ پھر بائع ( مدعی علیہ ) نے ہینہ پیش کیا کہ بائع اس کے ہر عیب سے بری ہے تو بائع ( مدعی علیہ ) کابینہ قبول نہ ہو گا ۔ اور امام ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے کہ مذکورہ مسائل پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اس کا بینہ بھی قبول کر لیا جائے گا۔ اور ظاہر الروایہ کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ برات کی شرط کرنا عقد کو اقتضائے وصف سلامت غیر سلامت کی طرف متغیر کرنا ہوتا ہے۔ اور یہ بیج موجود ہونے کا تقاضا کرتا ہے۔ حالانکہ بائع نے بیچ سے انکار کیا ہے۔ پس وہ اپنے دعوئی میں مناقض ہو گا۔ برخلاف قرضہ کے، کیونکہ قرضہ بھی ادا کر دیا جاتا ہے اگر چہ وہ باطل ہو ، چنانچہ سابق میں گذر چکا۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے دوسرے پر دعوی کیا کہ اس نے اپنی یہ باندی میرے ہاتھ فروخت کی ہے۔ مدعی علیہ نے بیچ کا انکار کرتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ میں نے تیرے ہاتھ یہ باندی بھی فروخت نہیں کی ہے۔ پس مدعی نے مدعی علیہ سے مذکورہ باندی خریدنے پر ہینہ قائم کر دیا اور اس باندی پر قبضہ کر لیا قبضہ کرنے کے بعد مدعی شراء باندی کے ایسے عیب پر مطلع ہوا جو عیب قبضہ کے بعد سے لے کر اب تک کی مدت میں پیدا نہیں ہو سکتا۔ یعنی ایسے عیب پر مطلع ہوا جس کا مدعی علیہ یعنی بائع کے قبضہ میں پیدا ہونا یقینی ہے۔ مثلاً باندی کے ہاتھ میں ایک زائد انگلی نظر آئی جو عیب ہے۔ پس مدعی نے خیار عیب کے تحت اس باندی کو واپس کرنے کا ارادہ کیا تو مدعی علیہ یعنی بائع نے اس بات پر بیتنہ پیش کیا کہ میں نے مدعی یعنی مشتری سے ہر عیب سے بری ہونے کی شرط کر لی تھی ۔ لہذا اس شرط کے مطابق ہر عیب سے بری ہوں تو مدعی علیہ (بائع) کا یہ بینہ قبول نہ ہو گا حضرت امام ابو یوسف سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں بھی مدعلی علیہ (بائع) کا نہ قبول ہوگا۔
دلیل یہ ہے کہ امام ابو یوسف نے اس مسئلہ بیج کو سابقہ مسائل دین پر قیاس کیا ہے۔ یعنی جس طر : " مابقہ مسائل میں مدعی علیہ کے اقوال ہیں توفیق ممکن ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کامہینہ قبول کر لیا جاتا ہے۔ اس طرح اس مسئلہ میں تو فیق ممکن ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کا مہینہ قبول کر ليا جائے گا۔
One person claimed against another that he sold his slave-girl to him. The defendant denied. The plaintiff presented evidence of purchase, then he found an extra finger on the slave-girl, then the defendant presented evidence that the seller is free from every defect. The plaintiff's evidence will not be accepted. He said: And whoever claims against another that he sold him his slave-girl, and he said, 'I never sold her to you,' then he presented evidence of purchase, and found on her an extra finger, then the seller presented evidence that he is free from every defect, the seller's evidence is not accepted. And from Abu Yusuf that it is accepted, by analogy to what we mentioned. The apparent reason is that the condition of immunity changes the contract from requiring the attribute of soundness to something else, and that requires the existence of the sale, and he has denied it, so he is contradictory, unlike a debt, because it may be paid even if it is invalid, as has passed. Translation: Imam Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: One person claimed against another that he sold his slave-girl to him, so the defendant said, 'I never sold her to you.' Then the plaintiff presented evidence of purchase. Then he found on her an extra finger. Then the seller (the defendant) presented evidence that the seller is free from every defect. The seller's evidence will not be accepted. And from Imam Abu Yusuf it is narrated that it is accepted, by analogy to the previously mentioned issues. The apparent (Zahir al-Riwayah) reason is that the condition of immunity changes the contract from requiring the attribute of soundness to something else, and that requires the existence of the sale, and he has denied the sale, so he is contradictory, unlike a debt, because it may be paid even if it is invalid, as has passed earlier. Commentary: The scenario of the case is: One person claimed against another that he sold this slave-girl of his to me. The defendant denied the sale, saying, 'I did not sell this slave-girl to you.' Then the plaintiff presented evidence that he purchased this slave-girl from the defendant, and he took possession. After taking possession, the purchaser became aware of a defect in the slave-girl that could not have arisen after the period of his possession since taking it; rather, it is certain that the defect occurred while it was in the possession of the seller, e.g., an extra finger was seen on the hand of the slave-girl, which is a defect. So the plaintiff intended to return the slave-girl under the option of defect. Then the defendant (seller) presented evidence that he had stipulated with the plaintiff (purchaser) that he would be free from every defect; therefore, he is free from every defect according to this condition. So the defendant's evidence will not be accepted. There is a narration from Imam Abu Yusuf that, in this case too, the defendant's evidence should be accepted. The reason is that Imam Abu Yusuf analogized this issue of sale to the previous issues of debt, i.e., just as in the previous issues the defendant's statements could be reconciled, so here reconciliation is possible, and therefore his evidence should be accepted.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage presents a specific case from Imam Muhammad's al-Jami' al-Saghir. A buyer claims he bought a slave-girl from the seller, but the seller denies the sale. The buyer proves the purchase with evidence and takes possession. He then discovers an extra finger (a pre-existing defect) and wants to return her due to the option of defect. The seller then presents evidence that he had stipulated freedom from all defects at the time of sale. The ruling according to Zahir al-Riwayah (the authoritative transmission) is that the seller's evidence is not accepted. The reason is that claiming a condition of immunity presupposes that a sale contract existed, but the seller previously denied the sale. Thus, his statements are contradictory (tanāquḍ). However, Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees and accepts the evidence by analogy to the debt cases earlier in the text. In those cases, the defendant could reconcile denying knowledge and claiming payment if there was a plausible scenario. Here, Abu Yusuf argues that similarly, the seller might have forgotten or had a reason for denying the sale initially, and then later remembered the condition. But the majority adopts the view that the contradiction is clear and irreconcilable in this case, unlike debt cases where payment can occur without a valid contract.

Key Terms
براءت (barā'ah): Immunity or freedom from defects; a contractual condition that the seller is not liable for latent defects.
خیار عیب (khiyār al-'ayb): Option of defect; the buyer's right to return a defective item if the defect existed at the time of sale and was not disclosed.
مناقض (munāqiḍ): Contradictory; here, the seller's statements are contradictory because he denies the sale but claims a condition in that sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Imam Muhammad reject the seller's evidence of immunity from defects in the case of the slave-girl?
A) Because the buyer's evidence of purchase is stronger.
B) Because the condition of immunity implies the existence of a sale, but the seller denied the sale.
C) Because the extra finger is not a valid defect.
D) Because Imam Abu Yusuf opposed it.

Key Takeaway
A seller cannot claim immunity from defects after denying the sale; the contradiction invalidates the evidence, protecting the buyer's right to return defective goods.

Effect of 'In Sha Allah' on a Written Document
Intra-Hanafi dispute on exception scope in a document

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the scope of an exception (istithna') in a conjoined document and apply the correct ruling based on the wording.

Core Idea
Exception after conjoined clauses: Abu Hanifa voids all; Sahibayn limit to the immediate predecessor.

When writing a legal document, adding 'in sha Allah' (if Allah wills) at the end can create uncertainty. The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on whether such an exception applies to the entire document or just the nearest statement. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each view and the practical implications for document drafting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the document type and the exception
Recognize the scenario: a written document about a right or a purchase ends with 'in sha Allah'. The passage gives examples of such documents.
The exception is an istithna' that may affect the validity.
2
State the two positions
Abu Hanifa holds the entire document void; the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the exception applies only to the immediately preceding clause.
The latter position is considered istihsan (juristic preference).
3
Examine the reasoning for each view
Abu Hanifa argues that conjoined clauses ('and') form one unit, so the exception applies to all. The Sahibayn argue that each clause is independent and the document is for assurance, so the exception only attaches to what directly precedes it.
The Sahibayn invoke linguistic principle 'al-kalam istibdad' (each part is independent).
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The difference determines which parts of the document remain binding. Under Abu Hanifa, the entire document is void; under the Sahibayn, only the clause immediately before 'in sha Allah' is affected.
This affects whether the guardian clause or the purchase obligation survives.
5
Note the secondary rule about a gap
If the writer leaves a blank space (gap) between the exception and the preceding text, the exception does not attach to that text—it becomes like a pause of silence.
This rule is agreed upon by both parties.

And the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] said: 'If Allah wills' applies only to the release and to the one who stands by the document of right. And their statement is istihsan, mentioned in the chapter of iqrar, because the exception refers only to what follows it, because the document is for assurance, and similarly the principle in speech is that each part is independent. And if he leaves a gap [between exception and the rest], they said it does not attach to it and becomes like a pause of silence. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say that the exception 'if Allah wills' applies only to the release and delivery, and not to the statement about the guardian. And their saying is istihsan, mentioned in the chapter of iqrar, because the exception refers only to what immediately follows it, because the document is for assurance, and similarly the principle in speech is that each part is independent. And Abu Hanifa's reasoning is that all the clauses, by virtue of conjunction, are like one thing, so the exception applies to all, as in conjoined words like his saying: 'His slave is free, and his wife is divorced, and upon him is walking to the House of Allah, if Allah wills.' And if he leaves a gap after the exception, the scholars said it does not attach and becomes like a pause of silence.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage discusses the effect of the phrase 'in sha Allah' (if Allah wills) appended to a written document. The document mentions a right and states that whoever stands by it is its guardian, or mentions a purchase and a responsibility for release and delivery, with 'in sha Allah' at the end. According to Abu Hanifa, the exception applies to the entire document, making it all void (batil). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that the exception only applies to the immediately preceding statement (release and delivery) due to istihsan, because the document is for legal assurance (isti'tha'iq), and in speech each part is independent; therefore, 'in sha Allah' only affects the sentence it directly follows. Abu Hanifa's reasoning is that all clauses are connected by conjunction ('and'), making them like one single statement; thus the exception at the end applies to the whole. The text also notes a secondary rule: if the writer leaves a gap between the exception and the preceding text, then the exception does not attach to it. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute where the two disciples' view is considered istihsan, but Abu Hanifa's view is based on the principle of conjunctive phrases. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is not stated explicitly here; in Hanafi fiqh, the view of the Sahibayn is often preferred in mu'amalat when it is more practical.

Key Terms
اسْتِثناء (istithna'): An exception clause (like 'in sha Allah') that modifies the preceding statement.
اسْتِيثاق (isti'tha'iq): Legal assurance; the purpose of a document is to provide certainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only the last statement is void
B) The entire document is void
C) The document remains valid but the exception is ignored
D) Only the first statement is void

Key Takeaway
The scope of an exception depends on whether conjoined clauses are treated as a unit or as independent statements—a key difference between Abu Hanifa and his disciples.

Contradiction in Defendant's Plea: Condition of Immunity vs. Denial of Sale
Analyzing a defendant's contradictory statements about a sale and condition of immunity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a defendant's contradictory statements render his plea invalid and explain why the Zahir al-Riwayah rejects the attempted reconciliation between denial of sale and claim of condition of immunity.

Core Idea
A condition of immunity presupposes the sale itself; denying the sale while claiming the condition is irreconcilable contradiction.

This lesson examines a procedural dilemma in Islamic court: a defendant first denies a sale, then claims he bought with a condition absolving the seller from defects. The Zahir al-Riwayah holds this is contradictory and the defendant's oath is not accepted. We will unpack the reasoning and contrast it with a similar debt case to highlight the concept of qiyas ma'a al-fariq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contradictory statements
The defendant says 'I did not sell' and later 'I claim the condition of immunity.' The attempted reconciliation (tawfiq) interprets the denial as referring to before the plaintiff's claim and the condition claim as after, so they are not contradictory.
This reconciliation is rejected by Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Understand the Zahir al-Riwayah objection
Claiming a condition of immunity necessarily implies the existence of the sale contract because a condition is an attribute that cannot exist without its subject.
The condition modifies the contract from sound to unsound; modification presupposes the contract.
3
Examine the dalil (proof)
The proof is based on the nature of attributes: changing the contract's quality requires the contract itself. Thus, claiming the condition is equivalent to admitting the sale.
This is an ontological argument, not merely procedural.
4
Compare with the debt case
In the debt case, acknowledging discharge does not necessarily mean the debt was valid because debt can be discharged in an invalid manner. Therefore, statements can be reconciled.
This difference invalidates the analogy between the two cases.
5
Conclude the qiyas ma'a al-fariq
Analogizing the sale case to the debt case is invalid because the 'illa (effective cause) differs: in debt, discharge is independent of validity; in sale, the condition is dependent on the contract.
The Hanafi position is that the defendant's oath is not accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الادب القاضي
اشرف الہدایہ جلد - تنم لیا جائے گا۔ اس مسئلہ میں توفیق اس طرح ممکن ہے کہ جب مدعی علیہ نے یہ کہا کہ میں نے یہ باندی اس کے ہاتھ نہیں بیچی ہے۔ تو اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ میرے اور اس کے درمیان بیچ نہیں ہوئی۔ لیکن جب مدعی نے بیع کا دعوی کیا تو میں نے اس سے درخواست کی کہ مجھ کو باندی کے ہر عیب سے بری کر دے۔ چنانچہ اس نے میری درخواست قبول کی۔ اور مجھ کو باندی کے ہر عیب سے بری کر دیا۔ گویا مد علی علیہ نے مدعی کے دعوی کرنے سے پہلے زمانہ میں بیع کا انکار کیا۔ اور دعویٰ کے وقت بیع کا اقرار کیا تو ان دونوں باتوں میں کوئی تناقض نہ ہوگا۔ اور جب مدعی علیہ کے دعوی میں تناقض نہیں ہے تو اس کا پینہ قبول کرنے میں بھی کوئی مضائقہ نہ ہوگا۔
ظاہر الروایہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مدعی علیہ کا ہر عیب سے بری ہونے کی شرط کا دعویٰ کرنا عقد بیع کو وصف سلامت سے وصف غیر سلامت کی طرف متغیر کرنا ہے بایں طور کہ اس شرط کے بغیر ، عقد بیع کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ مبیع مشتری کے لئے صحیح سالم ہو مگر جب یہ شرط لگادی گئی تو اب بیج کا صحیح سالم ہونا ضروری نہ رہا۔ اور عقد کو سلامتی کے وصف سے غیر سلامتی کے وصف کی طرف متغیر کرنا اس بات کا تقاضا کرتا ہے کہ اصل عقد موجود ہو۔ کیونکہ صفت کا تصور بغیر موصوف کے ممکن نہیں ہے۔ پس مدعی علیہ کا شرط برأت کا دعوی کرنا، اصل عقد کا دعویٰ کرنا ہے۔ حالانکہ مدعی علیہ کے دعوئی میں سراسر تناقض ہے۔ اور دعوی کے اندر تناقض کی صورت میں چونکہ مہینہ قبول نہیں ہوتا۔ اس لئے اس صورت میں بھی مدعی علیہ (بائع ) کا مبینہ قبول نہ ہوگا۔ برخلاف مسئلہ دین کے کیونکہ دین کبھی باطل اور نا حق طریقہ پر بھی ادا کر دیا جاتا ہے جیسے کہ سابق میں اس کی تفصیل گزر چکی ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ مسئلہ دین میں مدعی علیہ کے اقوال میں توفیق دے کر تناقض کو دور کرنا ممکن ہے۔ اور اس مسئلہ بیع میں توفیق دے کر تناقض کود کر ناممکن نہیں۔ پس اس فرق کے ساتھ مسئلہ بیع کو مسئلہ دین پر قیاس کرنا قیاس مع الفارق ہوگا۔
Book of the Etiquette of the Judge. Ashraf al-Hidayah Volume - will be taken. Reconciliation in this issue is possible such that when the defendant said, 'I did not sell this slave-girl to him,' its meaning is that there was no sale between me and him. But when the plaintiff claimed the sale, I asked him to absolve me from every defect of the slave-girl. So he accepted my request and absolved me from every defect of the slave-girl. Thus, the defendant denied the sale before the plaintiff claimed, and at the time of the claim he admitted the sale, so there is no contradiction between these two statements. And when there is no contradiction in the defendant's claim, there is no harm in accepting his oath. The proof of Zahir al-Riwayah is that the defendant's claim of the condition of immunity from every defect changes the contract of sale from the attribute of soundness to the attribute of unsoundness. In that without this condition, the requirement of the contract of sale is that the sold item be sound and healthy for the buyer, but when this condition is added, the soundness of the sold item is no longer necessary. And changing the contract from the attribute of soundness to the attribute of unsoundness requires that the original contract exist, because the conception of an attribute without the characterized entity is not possible. Therefore, the defendant's claim of the condition of immunity is a claim of the original contract, even though his claim is outright contradictory. And when there is contradiction in the claim, the oath is not accepted. For this reason, in this case too, the defendant's (seller's) oath will not be accepted. Contrary to the case of debt, because debt is sometimes discharged in a false and unjust manner, as previously detailed. Summary: In the debt case, it is possible to reconcile the defendant's statements and remove contradiction. In this sale case, it is impossible to reconcile and remove contradiction. So analogizing the sale case to the debt case with this difference would be an analogy with a difference (qiyas ma'a al-fariq).
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage discusses a specific scenario in judicial proceedings: a defendant first denies a sale, then claims he bought with a condition that the seller absolves him from defects. The Zahir al-Riwayah position is that this is a contradiction—claiming a condition of immunity necessarily implies admitting the sale itself (since a condition is an attribute of a contract). So the defendant's oath is not accepted. The text contrasts this with a debt case where contradiction can be reconciled (e.g., paying a debt in a wrongful manner still constitutes payment). Therefore, analogizing the sale case to the debt case is invalid (qiyas ma'a al-fariq).

Key Terms
شرط برأت (shart al-bara'ah): A condition in a sale contract wherein the seller absolves himself from liability for any defects in the sold item.
تناقض (tanaqud): Contradiction in a party's statements, which renders a judicial plea invalid.
قیاس مع الفارق (qiyas ma'a al-fariq): An analogy that is invalid because of a fundamental difference between the two cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the condition of immunity is invalid in Hanafi law.
B) Because claiming a condition of immunity necessarily implies the existence of the sale, creating a contradiction with the denial.
C) Because the defendant cannot change his plea after the plaintiff's claim.
D) Because the sale of a slave-girl requires a written document.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi judicial procedure, a condition of immunity necessarily implies the underlying contract, making a simultaneous denial of the contract a fatal contradiction that invalidates the defendant's plea.

Effect of 'In Sha Allah' in Legal Documents: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on document voidness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the effect of 'In sha Allah' in legal documents and apply the Sahibayn's reasoning to determine which clauses are voided.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, 'In sha Allah' at a document's end voids only the nearest clause, not the whole – per Sahibayn's istihsan.

A person writes a deed of debt and adds 'In sha Allah' at the end. Is the entire acknowledgment void, or only the last line about who holds the document? This lesson unpacks the classical dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two leading students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, on the scope of 'In sha Allah' in legal documents. You will learn the proofs on both sides and the practical implications for drafting contracts today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Read the passage and pinpoint the exact legal issue: what is the effect of writing 'In sha Allah' at the end of a legal document?
Focus on the two scenarios: deed of debt and deed of sale with guarantee.
2
Extract Abu Hanifa's ruling
Find Abu Hanifa's position: the entire document becomes void. Note his proof based on conjunction (عطف) making the whole document one unit.
His analogy: conjoined statements like 'My slave is free, and my wife is divorced...' where exception applies to all.
3
Extract the Sahibayn's ruling
Find the Sahibayn's position: only the immediately preceding clause becomes void. Note their proof based on istihsan and the principle that documents are for strengthening (توثيق), so voiding the whole is contrary to purpose.
Note the term 'istihsan' and the default principle of independence (استبداد) in speech.
4
Apply to practical scenarios
Take the two examples from the passage (debt deed and sale deed) and determine which clauses survive under each position. This reveals the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference).
Consider: if only the last clause is void, the debt acknowledgment remains valid.

Source Text

قال ذکر حق كتب في اسفله ومن قام بهذا الذكر فهو ولى ما فيه ان شاء الله تعالى او كتب في الشراء فعلى فلان خلاص ذلك وتسليمه ان شاء الله تعالى بطل الذكر كله ولهذا عند ابي حنيفة وقالا ان شاء الله تعالى هو على الخلاص وعلى من قام بذكر الحق وقولهما استحسان ذكره فى الاقرار لأن الاستثناء ينصرف الى مايليه لان الذكر للاستيثاق وكذا الاصل فى الكلام الاستبداد وله ان الكل كشئ واحد بحكم العطف فيُصرف الى الكل كما فى الكلمات المعطوفة مثل قوله عبده حر وامراته طالق وعليه المشى الى بيت الله تعالى ان شاء الله ولوترك فرجة قالوا لا يلتحق به و يصير كفاصل السكوت
ترجمہ امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں کہا کہ ایک حق کی ایک تحریر ہے جس کے نیچے یہ لکھا گیا۔ اور جو شخص اس تحریر کے ساتھ قائم ہوا تو جو کچھ اس میں ہے وہ اس کا ولی ہے ان شاء اللہ تعالی۔ یا اس نے خریدنے کے بارے میں لکھا۔ پس فلاں شخص پر اس کو خلاص کر نا اور مشتری کے سپر د کر نا لا زم ہے ان شاء اللہ تعالیٰ ۔ تو یہ پوری تحریر دستاویز ) باطل ہوگی اور یہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے۔ اور صاحبین نے کہا کہ ان شاء اللہ کا لفظ فقط خلاص یا من قام بذکر الحق کے ساتھ متعلق ہے۔ اور صاحبین کا قول استحسان ہے۔ امام محمد نے اس کو مبسوط کے کتاب الاقرار میں ذکر کیا ہے۔ اس لئے کہ استثناء اپنے متصل کی طرف پھرتا ہے۔ کیونکہ دستاویز تو مضبوطی کے لئے ہوتی ہے ۔ اور اسی طرح کلام میں مستقل ہونا اصل ہے۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عطف کی وجہ سے پوری تحریر ایک چیز کے مانند ہے، تو انشاء اللہ کا لفظ پوری تحریر کی طرف پھرے گا۔ جیسے کلمات معطوفہ میں ہوا کرتا ہے۔ مثلا کسی نے کہا عبدی حر وامراتي طالق وعلى المشى الى بيت الله تعالى انشاء اللہ تعالیٰ اور اگر اس نے درمیان میں کچھ جگہ خالی چھوڑ دی ( پھر انشاء اللہ تعالیٰ لکھا ) تو مشائخ نے فرمایا کہ میہ دستاویز سے متصل نہ ہوگا۔ اور ایسا ہو جائے گا جیسے سکوت سے فصل کرنے والا ۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے اپنی ذات پر قرضہ کے اقرار کی ایک تحریر دستاویز کے طور پر لکھ دی اور آخر میں یہ لکھاو من قام بهذا الذكر فهو ولى ما فيه انشا الله تعالی ۔ یعنی جس شخص کے پاس یہ دستاویز ہو تو جو کچھ اس میں تحریر ہے وہ اس کا ولی یعنی مستحق ہے انشاء اللہ تعالی ۔ یا کسی چیز کو خریدنے کی تحریر یعنی بیعنا مہ لکھ کر اس کے آخر میں لکھا کہ فلاں مشتری کو اگر کچھ درک پیش آئے یعنی کوئی شخص مبیع کے مستحق ہونے کا دعوی کر کے اس کو مشتری سے لینا چاہے تو فلاں شخص یعنی تحریر لکھنے والے پر یعنی مجھ پر اس کو چھٹکارا دلا کر سپر د کر نالازم ہے انشاء اللہ تعالی ۔ حاصل یہ کہ تحریر کے آخر میں لفظ انشاء اللہ لکھ دیا تو حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک یہ پوری تحریر کا لعدم اور باطل ہو جائے گی۔ اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ لفظ انشاء اللہ تعالیٰ کا تعلق فقط آخری جملہ سے ہے۔ یعنی پہلی صورت میں لفظ انشاء الله ومن قام بهذا الذكر فهو ولی ما فيه سے متعلق ہے۔ اور دوسری صورت میں فعلی فلان خلاص ذلک و تسلیمہ سے متعلق ہے۔ اور لفظ انشاء اللہ جس سے تعلق ہوتا ہے اس کو باطل کر دیتا ہے۔ کیونکہ لفظ انشاء اللہ ایسا کلمہ ہے جس سے کوئی امر لازم نہیں رہتا۔ اور لفظ انشاء اللہ کہنے سے کوئی چیز لازم اس لئے نہیں ہوتی کہ انشاء اللہ میں اس کام کو اللہ کی مشیت پر معلق کیا گیا ہے اور اللہ کی مشیت کسی کو معلوم نہیں ہوسکتی ۔ الہذا جو چیز اللہ کی مشیت پر معلق ہوگی وہ بھی واقع نہ ہوگی، بلکہ کالعدم اور باطل ہوگی ۔ جیسے کسی نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا کہ انت طالق انشاء اللہ تو یہ طلاق واقع نہیں ہوتی۔ بہر حال لفظ انشاء اللہ پر جس چیز کو معلق کیا جائے گا وہ واقع نہیں ہو گی۔ لیکن مسئلہ مذکورہ میں حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ لفظ انشاء اللہ کہنے سے پوری تحریر باطل ہوگئی۔ اور صاحبین کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ آخری عبارت جس کے ساتھ لفظ انشاء اللہ متعلق ہے وہ باطل ہوتی ہے۔ صاحبین کا مذہب "استحسان" ہے اور ان کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ دستاویز اس لئے لکھی جاتی ہے تا کہ اس سے معاملہ مضبوط ہو۔ پس لفظ انشاء اللہ کو پوری تحریر کی طرف تحریر کو باطل اور کالعدم کرنا خلاف اصل ہے۔ اور جب پوری تحریر کو باطل کرنا خلاف اصل ہے تو لفظ انشاء اللہ اسی کی طرف پھیرا جائے گا جو اس سے متصل ہے۔ یعنی پہلی صورت میں و من قام بهذا الذكر فهو ولى ما فیہ کی طرف پھیرا جائے گا۔ اور دوسری صورت میں فعلی فلان خلاص ذلک و تسلیمہ کی طرف پھیرا جائے گا۔ نیز کلام میں اصل یہ ہے کہ وہ مستقل ہو، تو گویا تحریر کا ہر جملہ مستقل ہے اور جب تحریر کا ہر جملہ مستقل ہے، تو لفظ انشاء اللہ اخیر کے مستقل جملہ سے متعلق ہو کہ آخری جملہ کو باطل کرے گا۔ اور باقی تحریر بدستور باقی رہے گی۔ حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بلاشبہ کلام میں اصل یہ ہے کہ وہ مستقل ہومگر یہ اس وقت ہے جب اس کے خلاف پر دلیل
He said: Mention of a right written at its bottom: 'And whoever stands by this mention is the guardian of what is in it, if Allah wills,' or he wrote regarding purchase: 'So on so-and-so is the release and delivery of that, if Allah wills.' Then the entire mention (document) becomes void. This is according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: 'If Allah wills' is regarding the release and regarding 'whoever stands by the mention of the right.' And their statement is istihsan. He mentioned it in the book of Iqrars (acknowledgments) because the exception refers to what follows it, because the mention (document) is for confirmation, and similarly the principle in speech is independence. And his (Abu Hanifa's) proof is that the whole is like one thing by virtue of conjunction, so it refers to the whole, as in conjoined words like his saying: 'My slave is free, and my wife is divorced, and upon him is the walk to the House of Allah, if Allah wills.' And if he left a gap, they said it does not attach to it and becomes like a separator due to silence.
Translation: Imam Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: There is a document of a right at the bottom of which is written: 'And whoever stands by this document is the guardian of what is in it, if Allah wills.' Or he wrote regarding purchase: 'Upon so-and-so is the release and delivery of that to the buyer, if Allah wills.' Then the entire document becomes void. This is according to Abu Hanifa. And the Sahibayn said: The phrase 'In sha Allah' is only related to 'release' or 'whoever stands by the mention of the right.' And their statement is istihsan. Imam Muhammad mentioned this in al-Mabsut in the Book of Iqrars. Because the exception (istithna) refers to what is adjacent to it, since the document is for strengthening, and similarly the principle in speech is independence. And Abu Hanifa's proof is that due to conjunction, the entire document is like one thing, so 'In sha Allah' will refer to the whole, as in conjoined words. For example, if someone says: 'My slave is free, and my wife is divorced, and upon him is the walk to the House of Allah, if Allah wills.' And if he left a gap in between, the scholars said it does not attach to it and becomes like a separator due to silence.
Explanation of the case: A person wrote a document acknowledging a debt upon himself and wrote at the end: 'Whoever stands by this document is the guardian of what is in it, if Allah wills.' That is, whoever has this document, whatever is written in it is his due, if Allah wills. Or he wrote a deed of purchase and at its end wrote: 'If some defect occurs to the buyer, i.e., someone claims title to the sold item and wants to take it from the buyer, then upon so-and-so, the writer, is the release and delivery, if Allah wills.' Summary: When the phrase 'In sha Allah' is written at the end, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the entire document becomes null and void. And the Sahibayn said: The phrase 'In sha Allah' is only related to the last sentence. In the first case, 'In sha Allah' relates to 'whoever stands by this document is the guardian of what is in it,' and in the second case to 'upon so-and-so is the release and delivery of that.' And whatever 'In sha Allah' relates to becomes void, because 'In sha Allah' is a word that does not make anything binding. And nothing becomes binding by saying 'In sha Allah' because it suspends the action on the will of Allah, and Allah's will is unknown. Therefore, whatever is suspended on Allah's will will not occur, but will be as if non-existent and void. For example, if someone says to his wife: 'You are divorced, if Allah wills,' the divorce does not occur. In any case, whatever is suspended by 'In sha Allah' will not occur. But in the mentioned issue, Imam Abu Hanifa's position is that saying 'In sha Allah' invalidates the entire document. And the Sahibayn's position is that only the last phrase to which 'In sha Allah' is related becomes void. The Sahibayn's position is istihsan, and their proof is that a document is written to strengthen the transaction. So making the entire document void by referring 'In sha Allah' to the whole is contrary to the principle. And when invalidating the whole is contrary to principle, 'In sha Allah' will be referred only to what is adjacent to it. In the first case, it refers to 'whoever stands by this document is the guardian of what is in it,' and in the second case to 'upon so-and-so is the release and delivery of that.' Also, the principle in speech is independence, so each sentence of the document is independent. When each sentence is independent, 'In sha Allah' relates to the last independent sentence and invalidates it, while the rest of the document remains valid. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that undoubtedly the principle in speech is independence, but this applies only when there is no evidence to the contrary.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of writing 'In sha Allah' at the end of a legal document (such as a deed of acknowledgment or a sale deed). Abu Hanifa holds that the entire document becomes void because the phrase, being at the end after a conjunction, refers to the whole document. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold, on the basis of istihsan, that 'In sha Allah' only invalidates the immediately preceding clause, not the entire document. They argue that documents are meant for confirmation, so voiding the whole contradicts the purpose. Additionally, each clause in a document is independent, so the phrase only affects the clause it is adjacent to. Abu Hanifa uses the analogy of conjoined statements (e.g., 'My slave is free, and my wife is divorced, and upon him is the walk to the House of Allah, if Allah wills') where the exception applies to all due to conjunction. The text also notes that if a gap (farjah) is left before 'In sha Allah,' it does not attach. The dispute is practical: in the first case (deed of debt), if 'In sha Allah' is written, the entire deed is void per Abu Hanifa, but only the clause about 'whoever stands by the document' is void per the Sahibayn, leaving the acknowledgment of debt intact. In the second case (deed of sale with guarantee), similarly, only the guarantee clause becomes void according to the Sahibayn.

Key Terms
ان شاء اللہ (in sha Allah): A phrase meaning 'if Allah wills,' used to suspend a statement on divine will, which in legal documents renders the statement non-binding.
استثناء (istithna): Exception; here it refers to the phrase 'In sha Allah' which excepts or suspends the preceding statement.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; the Sahibayn's ruling is based on istihsan, favoring the preservation of the document's main content over a strict application of conjunction rules.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn's position in this passage, what happens to a deed of debt that ends with 'In sha Allah' immediately after the clause 'Whoever stands by this document is the guardian of what is in it'?
A) The entire deed is void.
B) Only the clause 'whoever stands...' is void, but the acknowledgment of debt remains valid.
C) The deed is valid as long as the debtor affirms it in court.
D) The deed becomes unenforceable until the condition is fulfilled.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, 'In sha Allah' appended to a document voids only the directly preceding clause (Sahibayn's view, based on istihsan), not the entire document, unless the document is treated as a single unit due to conjunction (Abu Hanifa's view).

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
8 min
Trustee's Acknowledgment of Heir in Deposit: Ruling and Distinctions
Ruling with proof via qiyas and contrast with exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a trustee's acknowledgment of a sole heir obligates handing over the deposit, and distinguish it from invalid acknowledgments affecting a living depositor's rights and from valid debtor acknowledgments.

Core Idea
After death, the trustee's acknowledgment of the heir binds himself; during life, it cannot affect the depositor's right.

When a trustee acknowledges someone as the heir of a deceased depositor, does he have to hand over the property? The Hanafi school says yes, because the acknowledgment is about the heir's right after the depositor's ownership has ended. But what if the depositor is alive and the trustee acknowledges an agent or buyer? Then the acknowledgment is invalid because it tries to affect a third party's property rights. This lesson unpacks these distinctions and compares them with a debtor's acknowledgment of an agent, which is valid because debts are repaid by equivalents.

اشرف البدایہ جلد نهم
ويشهد بھم سے دوسری دلیل ہے۔ اس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اسلام یعنی عورت نصرانیہ کا مسلمان ہونا ایک امر حادث ہے۔ اور امر حادث کو اقرب اوقات کی طرف منسوب کیا جاتا ہے۔ اور اقرب اوقات ما بعد الموت ہے نہ کہ ماقبل الموت۔ پس اقرب اوقات کی طرف منسوب کرتے ہوئے یہی کہا جائے گا کہ یہ عورت اپنے شوہر کی موت کے بعد مسلمان ہوئی ہے۔ اور جب یہ عورت اپنے شوہر کی موت کے بعد مسلمان ہوئی ہے۔ تو موت کے وقت یقینا انصرانی تھی اور جب اپنے شوہر کی موت کے وقت نصرانی تھی تو میاں بیوی دونوں کے درمیان چونکہ اختلاف دین تھا۔ اس لئے یہ عورت اپنے شوہر کی میراث کی مستحق نہ ہوگی۔
ایک شخص فوت ہوا اس کے چار ہزار درہم کسی کے پاس امانت تھے امین نے کہا کہ یہ میت کا بیٹا ہے اور اس کے علاوہ میت کا کوئی وارث نہیں ہے تو مال ودیعت میت کے بیٹے کو دیدے
قال ومن مات وله في يدرجل اربعة الاف درهم وديعة فقال المستودع هذا ابن الميت لاوارث له غيره فانه يدفع المال اليه لانه اقرَانَ ما فى يده حقُ الوارث خلافةً فصار كما اذا اقرانه حق المورث وهو حى اصالة بخلاف ما اذا اقر لرجل انه وكيل المودع بالقبض اوانه اشتراه منه حيث لا يؤمر بالدفع اليه لانه اقر بقيام حق المودع اذ هو حى فيكون اقرار على مال الغير ولا كذلك بعد موته بخلاف المديون اذا اقر بتوكيل غيره بالقبض لان الديون تقضى بامثالها فيكون اقراراً على نفسه فيؤمر بـالـدفـع الـيـه
اور
ترجمہ اور اگر کوئی شخص مرا۔ اور اس کے چار ہزار درہم کسی کے پاس ودیعت ہیں ۔ پس مستودع ( امین ) نے کہا کہ یہ میت کا بیٹا ہے۔ اور اس کے علاوہ میت کا کوئی وارث نہیں ہے تو وہ مال ودیعت میت کے بیٹے کو دیدے۔ اس لئے کہ مستودع نے یہ اقرار کیا کہ جو کچھ اس کے قبضہ میں ہے وہ میت کا نائب ہو کر وارث کا حق ہے۔ پس یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے اس نے میت کی زندگی میں اقرار کیا کہ یہ مال اصالہ اس شخص کا حق ہے۔ برخلاف اگر مستودع نے کسی کے لئے اقرار کیا کہ یہ ودیعت رکھنے والے کا وکیل بالقبض ہے۔ یا یہ کہ اس نے ودیعت رکھنے والے سے خریدا ہے تو مستودع کو یہ حکم نہ دیا جائے گا کہ وہ اس شخص کو مال امانت دیدے کیونکہ مستودع نے اقرار کیا کہ ودیعت رکھنے والے کا حق قائم ہے۔ اس لئے کہ وہ زندہ ہے۔ پس یہ اقرار، مال غیر پر اقرار ہو گا ۔ اور ودیعت رکھنے والے کی موت کے بعد ایسا نہیں ہے۔ برخلاف قرضدار کے جب وہ دوسرے آدمی کے بارے میں قرض خواہ کی طرف سے وکیل بالقبض ہونے کا اقرار کرے۔ اس لئے کہ قرضے با مثالہا ادا کئے جاتے ہیں۔ پس یہ اپنی ذات پر اقرار ہوگا۔ لہذا قرضدار کو حکم دیا جائے گا کہ وہ وکیل بالقبض کو دیدے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص مثلا خالد مر گیا اور اس کے چار ہزار درہم دوسرے شخص مثلاً حامد کے پاس ودیعت ہیں ۔ پس مستودع یعنی حامد نے کہا کہ یہ شخص یعنی شاہد اس میت یعنی خالد کا بیٹا ہے۔ اور اس کے علاوہ میت کا کوئی وارث نہیں ہے ۔ حاصل یہ کہ مستودع یعنی حامد نے ایک دعوی تو یہ کیا کہ شاہد میت (خالد) کا بیٹا ہے اور دوسرا دعوئی یہ کیا کہ اس کے علاوہ میت کا کوئی وارث نہیں ہے تو اس صورت میں قاضی مستودع (حامد) کو حکم کرے گا کہ مال ودیعت میت کے بیٹے یعنی شاہد کو دیدے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ مستودع نے یہ اقرار کیا ہے کہ جو کچھ میرے قبضہ میں ودیعت ہے وہ میت ( خالد ) کا نائب ہونے کی حیثیت سے وارث ( شاہد ) کاحق اور اس کی ملک ہے۔ اور جو شخص اپنے پاس کسی کی ملک کا اقرار کرے اس پر واجب ہے کہ وہ اس ملک کو اسی کے حوالے کر دے جس کے لئے اقرار کیا ہے۔ جیسا کہ اگر مورث یعنی خالد زندہ ہوتا اور مستودع اس کے حق کا اقرار کرتا تو اصالہ مورث کے حوالے کرنا واجب ہوتا ۔ پس اسی طرح جب مورث کے مرنے کے بعد اُس کے وارث (شاہد ) کے لئے نیابتہ اقرار کیا تو مستودع پر وارث یعنی شاہد کو دیدینا واجب اور ضروری ہوگا۔
اس کے برخلاف اگر مستودع یعنی حامد نے یہ اقرار کیا کہ واصف ودیعت دینے والے یعنی عارف کی طرف سے ودیعت پر قبضہ کرنے کا وکیل ہے۔ یا واصف نے ودیعت دینے والے یعنی عارف سے مال ودیعت خرید لیا ہے۔ تو قاضی ہمستودع کو یہ کم نہیں کرے گا کہ وہ ودیعت کا مال وکیل بالقبض یا مشتری کے سپر د کرے۔ کیونکہ مستودع نے ودیعت دینے والے کے حق اور اس کی ملک کا اقرار کیا ہے حالانکہ ودیعت دینے والا زندہ بھی ہے۔ اس طور پر کہ مستورع نے جب یہ کہا کہ واصف، ودیعت دینے والے یعنی عارف کی طرف سے ودیعت پر قبضہ کا وکیل ہے تو گویا مستودع نے اس بات کا اقرار کیا کہ ودیعت اس کا یعنی عارف کا حق اور اس کی ملک ہے۔ اسی طرح مستودع نے جب یہ کہا کہ واصف نے یہ مال ودیعت عارف سے خرید لیا ہے تو گویا اس کا اقرار کیا کہ اس مال ودیعت کا مالک عارف ہے۔ بہر حال مستودع نے ودیعت دینے والے کے حق اور ملک کا اقرار کیا ہے اور وہ زندہ بھی ہے پس مستودع کا یہ اقرار کہ واصف، مودع یعنی عارف کا وکیل بالقبض ہے۔ غیر یعنی مودع کے مال پر اقرار ہے۔ اور اقرار چونکہ حجت قاصر ہے اس لئے دوسرے کے حق میں اس کا اقرار درست نہ ہوگا۔ اور جب مستودع کا یہ اقرار درست نہیں ہے تو مستودع کو یہ حکم نہ دیا جائے کہ وہ مال، ودیعت، وکیل بالقبض یعنی واصف کو دیدے اسی طرح مستودع نے جب یہ کہا کہ واصف نے ودیعت دینے والے یعنی عارف سے مال ودیعت خرید لیا ہے تو گویا مستودع نے مودع یعنی عارف کی ملک کے زائل ہونے کا اقرار کیا ہے۔ حالانکہ مستودع، مودع کی ملک باطل کرنے اور زائل کرنے کا مالک نہیں ہے۔ پس مستودع کے اس اقرار کی وجہ سے مودع ( ودیعت دینے والے) کی ملک زائل نہ ہوگی۔ اور جب مودع کی ملک زائل نہیں ہوئی تو قاضی مستودع کو یہ حکم بھی نہ کرے گا کہ وہ مشتری یعنی واصف کو مال ودیعت دیدے۔ اور مودع ( ودیعت دینے والے کی ) موت کے بعد اقرار علی مال غیر لازم نہیں آتا۔ کیونکہ مودع ( ودیعت دینے والے ) کی ملک اس کی موت کی وجہ سے زائل ہوگئی یعنی مودع کی موت کے بعد ودیعت کا مالک مودع نہ رہا بلکہ اس کا وارث ہو گیا اور جب وارث مالک ہو گیا اور مستودع (امین) نے اس کے لئے اقرار کیا ہے تو یہ اقرار علی غیر مال نہ ہو گا۔ بلکہ اقرار علی مال ہو گا۔ اور اقرار علی مال درست ہے۔ اس لئے مستودع کا مورع کے وارث کے لئے اقرار بھی درست ہوگا۔
اور اگر قرضدار نے یہ اقرار کیا کہ قرض خواہ نے قرضہ پر قبضہ کا وکیل فلاں شخص کو بنایا ہے تو قاضی قرضدار کو حکم دے گا کہ وہ قرضہ کا مال اُس وکیل کو دیدے۔ کیونکہ قرضہ باغیانہا ادا نہیں کیا جاتا بلکہ با مثالہا ادا کیا جاتا ہے یعنی قرضہ میں جو چیز لی جاتی ہے بعینہ وہ ادا نہیں کی جاتی بلکہ اس کا مثل ادا کیا جاتا ہے اور مثل کا مالک خود قرضدار ہے نہ کہ قرض خواہ۔ لہذا قرضدار کا وکیل بالقبض کے بارے میں اقرار اپنی ذات پر اقرار ہے اور اپنی ذات پر اقرار کرنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ لہذا یہ اقرار درست ہوگا۔ اور جب یہ اقرار درست ہے تو قرضدار کو مال قرض اُسی مقرلہ، وکیل کے لئے دینے کا حکم دیا جائے گا۔
Book of Etiquette of the Judge. Ashraf al-Hidayah Volume Nine. And this is another proof for them. Its summary is that Islam, i.e., a Christian woman becoming Muslim, is a new event. And a new event is attributed to the nearest time. And the nearest time is after death, not before death. So when attributing to the nearest time, it will be said that this woman became Muslim after her husband's death. And when she became Muslim after her husband's death, at the time of death she was certainly Christian. And when she was Christian at the time of her husband's death, then because there was difference of religion between husband and wife, this woman will not be entitled to her husband's inheritance. A person died and he had four thousand dirhams as a trust with someone. The trustee said: This is the son of the deceased and there is no other heir besides him. So he should give the deposited property to the son of the deceased. He said: And whoever dies and he has four thousand dirhams as a deposit in the hand of a person, and the depositary said: This is the son of the deceased, no heir other than him, then he gives the money to him because he acknowledged that what is in his hand is the right of the heir by way of succession. So it is as if he acknowledged the right of the testator while he was alive originally. Contrary to when he acknowledged for a man that he is the agent of the depositor for taking possession, or that he bought it from him, where he is not ordered to pay to him, because he acknowledged the establishment of the right of the depositor while he is alive, so it is an acknowledgment upon the property of another, and not so after his death. Contrary to the debtor when he acknowledged that someone else is authorized to take possession, because debts are repaid with their equivalents, so it is an acknowledgment upon himself, so he is ordered to pay to him. And translation: And if a person died and he had four thousand dirhams as a deposit with someone, then the depositary (trustee) said: This is the son of the deceased and there is no other heir besides him, then he should give the deposited property to the son of the deceased. Because the depositary acknowledged that what is in his possession, as a deputy of the deceased, is the right of the heir. So this becomes as if he acknowledged during the life of the deceased that this property is originally the right of that person. Contrary to if the depositary acknowledged for someone that he is the agent of the depositor for taking possession, or that he bought it from the depositor, then the depositary will not be ordered to give the trust property to that person, because the depositary acknowledged that the right of the depositor is established. Because he is alive. So this acknowledgment is an acknowledgment upon the property of another. And after the death of the depositor, it is not so. Contrary to a debtor when he acknowledges that another person is an agent for taking possession from the creditor, because debts are paid with their equivalents. So it is an acknowledgment upon himself. Therefore the debtor will be ordered to give it to the agent for taking possession. Explanation of the case: For example, a person Khalid died and he had four thousand dirhams as a deposit with another person, Hamid. Then the depositary, Hamid, said: This person, Shahid, is the son of this deceased, Khalid, and there is no other heir besides him. The summary is that the depositary, Hamid, made two claims: one that Shahid is the son of the deceased (Khalid), and the second that there is no other heir besides him. In this case, the judge will order the depositary (Hamid) to give the deposited property to the son of the deceased, i.e., Shahid. The proof is that the depositary acknowledged that what is in his possession as a deposit is, as a deputy of the deceased (Khalid), the right and property of the heir (Shahid). And whoever acknowledges the property of someone in his possession, it is obligatory on him to hand over that property to the one for whom he acknowledged. Just as if the testator, i.e., Khalid, were alive and the depositary acknowledged his right, then it would be obligatory to hand it over to the testator originally. So likewise, when after the death of the testator he acknowledged for his heir (Shahid) by way of succession, it becomes obligatory and necessary for the depositary to give it to the heir, i.e., Shahid. Contrary to this, if the depositary, i.e., Hamid, acknowledged that Wasif is the agent of the depositor, i.e., Arif, for taking possession of the deposit, or that Wasif bought the deposited property from the depositor, i.e., Arif, then the judge will not order the depositary to hand over the deposit property to the agent for taking possession or the buyer. Because the depositary acknowledged the right and property of the depositor while the depositor is alive. In that manner, when the depositary said that Wasif is the agent of the depositor, i.e., Arif, for taking possession of the deposit, it is as if the depositary acknowledged that the deposit is the right and property of Arif. Similarly, when the depositary said that Wasif bought this deposited property from Arif, he acknowledged that the owner of this deposited property is Arif. In any case, the depositary acknowledged the right and property of the depositor and he is alive. So the depositary's acknowledgment that Wasif is the agent of the depositor, i.e., Arif, for taking possession is an acknowledgment upon the property of another, i.e., the depositor. And since acknowledgment is a limited proof, his acknowledgment in favor of another is not valid. And when this acknowledgment of the depositary is not valid, the depositary is not ordered to give the deposit property to the agent for taking possession, i.e., Wasif. Similarly, when the depositary said that Wasif bought the deposited property from the depositor, i.e., Arif, it is as if the depositary acknowledged the termination of the depositor's property. However, the depositary is not the owner of invalidating and terminating the depositor's property. So due to this acknowledgment of the depositary, the depositor's property will not terminate. And when the depositor's property does not terminate, the judge will not order the depositary to give the deposit property to the buyer, i.e., Wasif. And after the death of the depositor, acknowledgment upon the property of another is not binding. Because the depositor's property terminated due to his death, i.e., after the depositor's death, the owner of the deposit is no longer the depositor but his heir. And when the heir became the owner and the depositary (trustee) acknowledged for him, this acknowledgment will not be upon non-property, but upon property. And acknowledgment upon property is valid. Therefore the depositary's acknowledgment for the heir of the testator is also valid. And if a debtor acknowledged that the creditor appointed a certain person as agent for taking possession of the debt, then the judge will order the debtor to give the debt money to that agent. Because a debt is not paid in kind but by its equivalent. That is, in a debt, what is taken is not given back in kind but its equivalent is given. And the owner of the equivalent is the debtor himself, not the creditor. Therefore the debtor's acknowledgment regarding the agent for taking possession is an acknowledgment upon his own self, and there is no harm in acknowledging upon one's own self. Hence this acknowledgment is valid. And when this acknowledgment is valid, the debtor will be ordered to give the debt money to that acknowledged agent.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Adab al-Qadi presents a nuanced ruling on the validity of an iqrar (acknowledgment) by a trustee (mustawda') regarding a deposited item (wadi'ah). The text first presents the base ruling from the matn: If a person dies leaving a deposit with someone, and the trustee acknowledges that a specific individual is the son and sole heir of the deceased, the judge orders the trustee to hand over the deposit to that heir. The reasoning given is that the trustee has acknowledged that what he holds is the right of the heir by way of succession (khilafah). This is analogized to the case where the depositor is alive: if the trustee acknowledges the depositor's right to the deposit, he must return it to him. Here, after death, the same acknowledgment is made in favor of the heir as a substitute. The text then delineates two contrasting scenarios. First, if the trustee acknowledges that someone is the agent (wakil) of the depositor (who is alive) for receiving the deposit, or that someone purchased the deposit from the depositor, the judge does not order the trustee to hand it over to that person. The reason is that such an acknowledgment affirms the right of the living depositor, and it is considered an acknowledgment regarding the property of another (iqrar 'ala mal al-ghayr), which is not binding on the trustee as it would affect a third party's rights. Second, the text distinguishes the case of a debtor (madyun) who acknowledges that the creditor has appointed an agent to receive payment. In that instance, the judge orders the debtor to pay the agent. The key difference is that debts are repaid with equivalents (mithliyyat), so the debtor's acknowledgment is considered an acknowledgment upon himself (iqrar 'ala nafsih) — he is confirming his own obligation — and therefore valid and enforceable. The commentary elaborates on these distinctions, emphasizing that the trustee's acknowledgment after the depositor's death is valid because the depositor's ownership has terminated by death and transferred to the heir, making the acknowledgment one regarding property that is now in the heir's right. This ruling is part of the Hanafi school's detailed jurisprudence on iqrar and its limitation as a proof that cannot affect third parties without consent.

Key Terms
وديعة (wadi'ah): Property entrusted to another for safekeeping without compensation.
مستودع (mustawda'): The person who receives the deposit; the trustee.
اقرار (iqrar): An admission or acknowledgment of a right or obligation against oneself.
وكل بالقبض (wakil bil-qabd): An agent appointed to take possession of property.
قرض (qard): A loan of fungible items (mithliyyat) that must be repaid with equivalents.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school order the trustee (mustawda') to hand over the deposit to the heir when he acknowledges the claimant as the sole heir, but not when he acknowledges someone as the agent of the living depositor?
A) Because the heir is a more deserving person than the agent.
B) Because after the depositor's death, the trustee's acknowledgment pertains to property that no longer belongs to a third party but to the heir, whereas acknowledging the depositor's agent affirms the depositor's right over the property and the trustee cannot affect a third party's right without consent.
C) Because the agent is not a valid representative.
D) Because the judge has no jurisdiction over the trustee in agency cases.

Key Takeaway
A trustee's acknowledgment of a sole heir after the depositor's death is valid and obligates delivery, while similar acknowledgments during the depositor's life are invalid because they affect a third party's property rights.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
12 min
Depositary's Acknowledgment: Heirs, Agents, and Debt Repayment
Three rulings on depositary's acknowledgment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish when a depositary's acknowledgment of a third party's claim to the deposit obligates the judge to order handover and when it does not, by applying the Hanafi principle of hujjat qasira.

Core Idea
Acknowledgment (iqrar) is a limited proof that cannot affect a living owner's rights.

This lesson examines three scenarios where a depositary (mustawda') acknowledges someone else's claim to the deposit. The key is whether the acknowledgment affects only the depositary's own liability or also the depositor's ownership. The Hanafi principle of hujjat qasira (limited proof) determines the outcome: after the depositor's death, the heir's right can be acknowledged; while the depositor is alive, no third party's claim can be enforced through the depositary's acknowledgment. For debts, the debtor's own property is at stake, so his acknowledgment is valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acknowledgment scenario
Determine whom the depositary (or debtor) acknowledges: an heir of the deceased depositor, an agent/buyer while the depositor is alive, or an agent of the creditor in a debt.
Each scenario leads to a different ruling.
2
Assess the status of the original owner
Is the depositor alive or dead? If alive, his ownership is intact; if dead, ownership has transferred to heirs.
This determines whether the acknowledgment is upon the property of another.
3
Apply the principle of hujjat qasira
Iqrar is a limited proof: it binds only the one who makes it. It cannot affect the rights of a third party without their consent. If the acknowledgment would infringe on a living owner's property, it is invalid and the judge will not enforce it.
If the acknowledgment is upon the acknowledging party's own property (e.g., debtor's equivalent), it is valid.
4
Determine the judge's order
Based on the validity of the acknowledgment, decide whether the judge orders delivery: valid → wajib to hand over; invalid → no order.
The first and third scenarios result in wajib; the second results in no order.

اشرف البدایہ جلد نم حوالے کر دے جس کے لئے اقرار کیا ہے۔ جیسا کہ اگر مورث یعنی خالد زندہ ہوتا اور مستودع اس کے حق کا اقرار کرتا تو اصالہ مورث کے حوالے کرنا واجب ہوتا ۔ پس اسی طرح جب مورث کے مرنے کے بعد اُس کے وارث (شاہد ) کے لئے نیابتہ اقرار کیا تو مستودع پر وارث یعنی شاہد کو دیدینا واجب اور ضروری ہوگا۔
اس کے برخلاف اگر مستودع یعنی حامد نے یہ اقرار کیا کہ واصف ودیعت دینے والے یعنی عارف کی طرف سے ودیعت پر قبضہ کرنے کا وکیل ہے۔ یا واصف نے ودیعت دینے والے یعنی عارف سے مال ودیعت خرید لیا ہے۔ تو قاضی ہمستودع کو یہ کم نہیں کرے گا کہ وہ ودیعت کا مال وکیل بالقبض یا مشتری کے سپر د کرے۔ کیونکہ مستودع نے ودیعت دینے والے کے حق اور اس کی ملک کا اقرار کیا ہے حالانکہ ودیعت دینے والا زندہ بھی ہے۔ اس طور پر کہ مستورع نے جب یہ کہا کہ واصف، ودیعت دینے والے یعنی عارف کی طرف سے ودیعت پر قبضہ کا وکیل ہے تو گویا مستودع نے اس بات کا اقرار کیا کہ ودیعت اس کا یعنی عارف کا حق اور اس کی ملک ہے۔ اسی طرح مستودع نے جب یہ کہا کہ واصف نے یہ مال ودیعت عارف سے خرید لیا ہے تو گویا اس کا اقرار کیا کہ اس مال ودیعت کا مالک عارف ہے۔ بہر حال مستودع نے ودیعت دینے والے کے حق اور ملک کا اقرار کیا ہے اور وہ زندہ بھی ہے پس مستودع کا یہ اقرار کہ واصف، مودع یعنی عارف کا وکیل بالقبض ہے۔ غیر یعنی مودع کے مال پر اقرار ہے۔ اور اقرار چونکہ حجت قاصر ہے اس لئے دوسرے کے حق میں اس کا اقرار درست نہ ہوگا۔ اور جب مستودع کا یہ اقرار درست نہیں ہے تو مستودع کو یہ حکم نہ دیا جائے کہ وہ مال ، ودیعت، وکیل بالقبض یعنی واصف کو دیدے اسی طرح مستودع نے جب یہ کہا کہ واصف نے ودیعت دینے والے یعنی عارف سے مال ودیعت خرید لیا ہے تو گویا مستودع نے مودع یعنی عارف کی ملک کے زائل ہونے کا اقرار کیا ہے۔ حالانکہ مستودع، مودع کی ملک باطل کرنے اور زائل کرنے کا مالک نہیں ہے۔ پس مستودع کے اس اقرار کی وجہ سے مودع ( ودیعت دینے والے) کی ملک زائل نہ ہوگی۔ اور جب مودع کی ملک زائل نہیں ہوئی تو قاضی مستودع کو یہ حکم بھی نہ کرے گا کہ وہ مشتری یعنی واصف کو مال ودیعت دیدے۔
اور مودع ( ودیعت دینے والے کی ) موت کے بعد اقرار علی مال غیر لازم نہیں آتا۔ کیونکہ مودع ( ودیعت دینے والے ) کی ملک اس کی موت کی وجہ سے زائل ہوگئی یعنی مودع کی موت کے بعد ودیعت کا مالک مودع نہ رہا بلکہ اس کا وارث ہو گیا اور جب وارث مالک ہو گیا اور مستودع (امین) نے اس کے لئے اقرار کیا ہے تو یہ اقرار علی غیر مال نہ ہو گا۔ بلکہ اقرار علی مال ہو گا۔ اور اقرار علی مال درست ہے۔ اس لئے مستودع کا مورع کے وارث کے لئے اقرار بھی درست ہوگا۔
اور اگر قرضدار نے یہ اقرار کیا کہ قرض خواہ نے قرضہ پر قبضہ کا وکیل فلاں شخص کو بنایا ہے تو قاضی قرضدار کو حکم دے گا کہ وہ قرضہ کا مال اُس وکیل کو دیدے۔ کیونکہ قرضہ باغیانہا ادا نہیں کیا جاتا بلکہ با مثالہا ادا کیا جاتا ہے یعنی قرضہ میں جو چیز لی جاتی ہے بعینہ وہ ادا نہیں کی جاتی بلکہ اس کا مثل ادا کیا جاتا ہے اور مثل کا مالک خود قرضدار ہے نہ کہ قرض خواہ۔ لہذا قرضدار کا وکیل بالقبض کے بارے میں اقرار اپنی ذات پر اقرار ہے اور اپنی ذات پر اقرار کرنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ لہذا یہ اقرار درست ہوگا۔ اور جب یہ اقرار درست ہے تو قرضدار کو مال قرض اُسی مقرلہ ، وکیل کے لئے دینے کا حکم دیا جائے گا۔
Book of Conduct of the Judge. Ashraf al-Bidayah, volume number. Hand over to the one for whom the acknowledgment was made. For example, if the ancestor, Khalid, were alive and the depositary acknowledged his right, then it would be obligatory to hand over originally to the ancestor. So likewise, when after the ancestor's death, acknowledgment is made by proxy for his heir (the witness), then it becomes obligatory and necessary for the depositary to give to the heir, i.e., the witness. Contrary to this, if the depositary, i.e., Hamid, acknowledged that Wasif is the agent of the depositor, i.e., Arif, for taking possession of the deposit, or that Wasif bought the deposited property from Arif, then the judge will not order the depositary to hand over the deposited property to the agent for possession or the buyer. Because the depositary has acknowledged the right and ownership of the depositor, while the depositor is still alive. In this way, when the depositary said that Wasif is the agent of the depositor, i.e., Arif, for possession, then it is as if the depositary acknowledged that the deposit is Arif's right and ownership. Similarly, when the depositary said that Wasif bought this deposited property from Arif, then it is as if he acknowledged that the owner of this deposited property is Arif. In any case, the depositary has acknowledged the right and ownership of the depositor, and he is alive, so this acknowledgment of the depositary that Wasif is the agent of the depositor, i.e., Arif, is an acknowledgment regarding the property of another, i.e., the depositor. And since acknowledgment is a limited proof, its acknowledgment regarding another's right will not be valid. And when this acknowledgment of the depositary is not valid, then the depositary will not be ordered to hand over the property, the deposit, to the agent for possession, i.e., Wasif. Similarly, when the depositary said that Wasif bought the deposited property from the depositor, i.e., Arif, then it is as if the depositary acknowledged the elimination of the depositor's ownership. However, the depositary is not capable of invalidating and eliminating the depositor's ownership. So due to this acknowledgment of the depositary, the ownership of the depositor (the depositor) will not be eliminated. And when the depositor's ownership is not eliminated, then the judge will also not order the depositary to hand over the deposited property to the buyer, i.e., Wasif. And after the death of the depositor, an acknowledgment is not considered 'ala ghayr mal (upon other's property). Because the ownership of the depositor has been eliminated due to his death, i.e., after the death of the depositor, the owner of the deposit is no longer the depositor, but his heir becomes the owner. And when the heir becomes the owner and the depositary (trustee) has made an acknowledgment for him, then this acknowledgment is not upon other's property, but it is upon property. And an acknowledgment upon property is valid. Therefore, the depositary's acknowledgment for the heir of the depositor is also valid. And if the debtor acknowledged that the creditor appointed a certain person as agent for taking possession of the debt, then the judge will order the debtor to hand over the debt amount to that agent. Because a debt is not paid by its specific identity, but by its likeness; that is, in a debt, the thing taken is not paid in kind, but its equivalent is paid, and the owner of the equivalent is the debtor himself, not the creditor. Hence, the debtor's acknowledgment regarding the agent for possession is an acknowledgment upon himself, and there is no issue in acknowledging upon oneself. Therefore, this acknowledgment is valid. And when this acknowledgment is valid, the debtor will be ordered to give the debt amount to that specified agent.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This lesson presents three distinct rulings from the Book of Adab al-Qadi regarding the depositary's (ameen's) acknowledgment of others' claims on a deposit. The first ruling: If the depositor dies, the depositary may acknowledge the heir as the rightful owner, and the judge will order the depositary to hand over the deposit to the heir. This is because the depositor's ownership transfers to the heir upon death, so the acknowledgment is upon property, which is valid. The second ruling: If the depositor is still alive and the depositary acknowledges that a third party is the depositor's agent for possession (wakil bil-qabd) or has bought the deposit, the judge will not order the depositary to hand it over. Reason: The acknowledgment pertains to the depositor's right, and since the depositor is alive, the acknowledgment is 'ala ghayr (upon another's property), and acknowledgment is a limited proof (hujjat qasira) that cannot affect another's rights. The depositary cannot eliminate the depositor's ownership. The third ruling: For a debt, the situation is different. If the debtor acknowledges that the creditor appointed an agent to collect the debt, the judge orders the debtor to pay the agent. Because debt is mithli (fungible), repayment is by equivalent, and the equivalent belongs to the debtor himself. Thus, the acknowledgment is upon his own property, which is valid. Each ruling is rooted in the nature of ownership and the limits of acknowledgment.

Key Terms
مستودع (mustawda'): The depositary, the person with whom the deposit is left for safekeeping. Also called ameen (trustee).
مودع (mudi'): The depositor, the person who leaves the deposit.
اقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment or confession of a right or ownership. It is a form of proof in Islamic law.
حجت قاصر (hujjat qasira): A limited proof that only operates against the one who makes the acknowledgment, not against others.
وکیل بالقبض (wakil bil-qabd): An agent authorized to take possession of property or money on behalf of the principal.
مثل (mithl): An equivalent or similar item, used in repayment of fungible goods (mithliyat).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A depositary acknowledges that a third party is the agent of the depositor to collect the deposit. The depositor is alive and denies appointing any agent. What is the judge's order?
A) Order the depositary to hand over to the agent because the acknowledgment is valid.
B) Order the depositary to hand over to the depositor only after confirmation.
C) Not order the depositary to hand over to the agent because the acknowledgment is invalid.
D) Order the deposit to be divided between the agent and the depositor.

Key Takeaway
A depositary's acknowledgment can only bind himself, not the living depositor; after death, the heir's right can be acknowledged; debtor's acknowledgment of creditor's agent is valid because it concerns his own property.
