Ruling on Movable Property in Possession Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on taking movable property from respondent despite denial

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the preferred Hanafi ruling that movable property is taken from the respondent for preservation, distinguish it from immovable property, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute and its resolution.

Core Idea
Movable property is taken from the respondent for preservation; immovable property is left because it is inherently secure.

This lesson examines an important procedural rule in Hanafi qada (judgment). When a claimant proves part of a movable property inheritance, but the respondent denies the rest, should the remaining half be taken from the respondent or left? The passage from al-Hidayah presents an intra-Hanafi dispute and resolves it with Imam Abu Hanifa's preferred view. You will learn the reasoning based on the need for preservation (hifz) and the contrast with immovable property (aqar), which is considered self-secure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal scenario
Understand the dispute: a claimant proves that half of a movable property belongs to him and his absent brother; the respondent denies the other half. The judge must decide what to do with the remaining half.
This is a common scenario when inheritance claims involve movable goods.
2
State the two intra-Hanafi views
Recognize that some scholars say the property is taken 'by agreement' (bil ittifaq) from the respondent, while others hold that it is also a matter of dispute (al-khilaf) and not settled unanimously.
The text first says 'it has been taken by agreement' but then notes a difference of opinion.
3
Analyze the reasoning for taking movable property
The key illa (reason) is preservation: movable property is not self-secure; it can be moved, stolen, or misused. Therefore, removing it from the respondent who has denied the claim protects it. Contrast with immovable property, which is inherently safe.
The analogy with the executor's (wasi) authority to sell the movable property of an absent adult heir reinforces this reasoning.
4
Understand the tarjih (preference) for Abu Hanifa's view
The author of al-Hidayah states that Abu Hanifa's view is 'azhar' (more apparent) because movable property needs safeguarding. Thus, the mufta bihi is that the property is taken and placed with a trustworthy person.
The tarjih is based on the stronger need for preservation compared to immovable property.
5
Apply the ruling to distinguish manqul from aqar
Use the principle elsewhere: the executor may sell manqul but not aqar of an absent heir. This consistency confirms that the ruling is sound and not an isolated case.
The same logic governs both possession disputes and executor sales.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر دعویٰ مال منقول میں ہو تو بالا تفاق قابض سے بقیہ مال لے لیا جائے گا
ولو كانت الدعوى فى منقول فقد قيل يؤخذ منه بالاتفاق لانه يحتاج فيه الى الحفظ والنزع ابلغ فيه بخلاف العقار لانها محصنة بنفسها ولهذا يملك الوصى بيع المنقول على الكبير الغائب دون العقار وكذا حكم وصى الام والاخ والعم على الصغير وقيل المنقول على الخلاف ايضاً وقول ابي حنيفة فيه اظهر لحاجته الى الحفظ وانما لا يؤخذ الكفيل لانه انشاء الخصومة والقاضى انما نُصِب لقطعها لا لا نشائها
ترجمہ اور اگر دعوئی مال منقول میں ہو تو کہا گیا کہ بالاتفاق قابض سے باقی مال لے لیا جائے گا۔ اس لئے کہ مال منقول میں حفاظت کی ضرورت ہے اور نکال لینے میں حفاظت زیادہ ہے۔ برخلاف جائداد غیر منقولہ کے کہ وہ بذات خود محفوظ ہے۔ اور انی وجہ سے میت کا وسی، بالغ غائب وارث پر منقول کی بیع کا مالک ہے نہ کہ غیر منقولہ جائداد کی بیع کا۔ اور یہی حکم ماں اور بھائی اور چچا کے وھی کا نابالغ وارث کے حق میں ہے۔ اور کہا گیا کہ مال منقول بھی مختلف فیہ ہے۔ اور منقول کی صورت میں ابوحنیفہ کا قول زیادہ ظاہر ہے۔ کیونکہ مال منقول حفاظت کا محتاج ہے۔ اور کفیل نہیں لیا جائے گا۔ اس لئے کہ کفیل لینا خصومت پیدا کرنا ہے۔ حالانکہ قاضی خصومت قطع کرنے کے لئے مقرر ہے نہ کہ خصومت پیدا کرنے کے لئے ۔
تشریح صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ اگر دعوی مال منقول میں ہو یعنی مال منقول ایک شخص کے قبضہ میں ہو۔ اور دوسرے نے مبینہ پیش کیا ہو کہ میرا باپ مر چکا ہے اور اس نے یہ مال میرے اور میرے غائب بھائی کے لئے میراث چھوڑا ہے۔ تو قاضی نصف مال کا فیصلہ تو اس مدعی کے لئے کرے گا اور بقول بعض حضرات مشائخ کے نزدیک باقی نصف مال بھی بالاتفاق قابض سے لے کر کسی امین آدمی کو دے دیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ مال منقول میں حفاظت کی ضرورت ہے۔ بایں طور کہ وہ بذات خود محفوظ نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے ایک محل سے دوسرے محل کی طرف منتقل کیا جا سکتا ہے اور قابض کے قبضہ سے نکال لینے میں زیادہ حفاظت ہے۔ کیونکہ جب وہ مدعی کے دعوی کا انکار کر چکا اور یہ کہہ چکا کہ میرے قبضہ میں میت کا کچھ مال نہیں ہے تو خیانت کر کے یا اس کو اپنی ملک سمجھ کر اس میں تصرف بھی کر سکتا ہے۔ لیکن جب قاضی نے اس کے قبضہ سے نکال کر کسی امین آدمی کے قبضہ میں دے دیا اور بظاہر وہ امین آدمی عادل بھی ہے تو وہ مال محفوظ ہو گیا۔ پس حفاظت کے پیش نظر باقی نصف مال بھی قابض کے قبضہ سے لے لیا جائے گا۔ برخلاف غیر منقول جائداد کے کہ وہ بذات خود محفوظ ہے۔ اس میں غصب اور چوری کا کوئی احتمال نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے اُس کو قابض کے پاس چھوڑنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ چونکہ مال منقول حفاظت کا زیادہ محتاج ہے اس لئے میت کے وصی کو یہ اختیار حاصل ہے کہ وہ میت کے بالغ وارث جو غائب ہے اس کا وہ حصہ جو مال منقول سے متعلق ہو اس کو فروخت کر دے۔ اگر وصی نے فروخت کر دیا تو اس کی یہ بیچ بالغ وارث ( غائب ) پر نافذ ہو جائے گی ۔ اور غیر منقول مال کی بیج کا وصی کو اختیار نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ غیر منقول جائداد چونکہ بذات خود محفوظ ہے اس لئے اس کو فروخت کرنے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔
And if the claim is in movable property, then by agreement the remaining property will be taken from the possessor. And if the claim is in movable property, it has been said that it is taken from him by agreement because it needs preservation, and removal is more effective for it, unlike immovable property because it is inherently safe. For this reason, the executor of the deceased has the right to sell the movable property of the absent adult heir, but not the immovable property. Similarly is the ruling of the executor of the mother, brother, and uncle over the minor. And it has been said that movable property is also a matter of dispute. And the statement of Abu Hanifa in it is more apparent because of the need for preservation. And the guarantor (kafil) is not taken because it creates litigation, whereas the judge is appointed to cut off litigation, not to create it. Translation: And if the claim is in movable property, it has been said that by agreement the remaining property will be taken from the possessor. This is because movable property requires preservation, and removal offers greater preservation, unlike immovable property which is inherently safe. For this reason, the executor of the deceased can sell the movable property of the absent adult heir, but not the immovable property. And the same ruling applies to the executor of the mother, brother, and uncle over the minor. And it has been said that movable property is also a matter of dispute. In the case of movable property, Abu Hanifa's view is more apparent because movable property needs preservation. And a guarantor (kafil) will not be taken because taking a guarantor creates litigation, whereas the judge is appointed to cut off litigation, not to create it. Explanation: The author of Hidayah said that if the claim is in movable property, meaning that movable property is in the possession of one person, and another presents evidence that my father has died and he left this property as inheritance for me and my absent brother, then the judge will decide half the property for the claimant. And according to some scholars (mashayikh), the remaining half will also be taken from the possessor by agreement and given to a trustworthy person, because movable property needs preservation, in that since it is not inherently safe, it can be transferred from one place to another, and removing it from the possessor's possession offers more preservation. Because when he has denied the claim and said that there is no property of the deceased in his possession, he may dispose of it through treachery or by considering it his own. But when the judge removes it from his possession and gives it to a trustworthy person who is apparently just, then the property is preserved. So, due to preservation, the remaining half will also be taken from the possessor. Unlike immovable property, which is inherently safe; there is no possibility of usurpation or theft, so leaving it with the possessor is not harmful. Since movable property is more in need of preservation, the executor of the deceased has the authority to sell the share of the adult absent heir that pertains to movable property. If the executor sells it, the sale will be binding on the absent adult heir. But the executor does not have the authority to sell immovable property, because immovable property is inherently safe, so there is no need to sell it.
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling for movable property (manqul) when a similar dispute arises. It begins by stating that by agreement (bil ittifaq), the remaining half of movable property is taken from the respondent and given to a trustworthy person. The reason is that movable property requires preservation—it is not inherently secure like immovable property (aqar) and can be moved or disposed of. Therefore, removing it from the respondent's possession offers better protection. The text then mentions a difference of opinion: some say this is agreed, others say it is also disputed. Imam Abu Hanifa's view is preferred because movable property needs safeguarding. The passage also draws an analogy with the executor (wasi) of a deceased: he has the authority to sell the movable property of an absent adult heir but not immovable property, because immovable is self-secure. Additionally, a guarantor (kafil) is not taken from the respondent because that would create litigation, whereas the judge's role is to end disputes, not create them. This lesson underscores the Hanafi emphasis on practical preservation (hifz) in property disputes.

Key Terms
منقول (manqūl): Movable property—items that can be physically moved or transferred.
عقار (ʿaqār): Immovable property—land and buildings considered inherently secure.
وصی (waṣī): Executor appointed in a will or by the court to manage the deceased's estate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in this passage, what is done with the remaining half of movable property in such a dispute?
A) It remains with the respondent because the denial is nullified.
B) It is taken from the respondent and given to a trustworthy person.
C) It is destroyed to prevent theft.
D) It is given to the state treasury.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi qada, movable property is taken from a denying respondent for preservation; immovable property is left because it is self-secure.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
12 min
Dispute on Taking Movable Property from Possessor
Intra-Hanafi dispute on property custody

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Imam Abu Hanifah prefers leaving the remaining half of movable property with the possessor and evaluate the Sahibayn's counter-argument.

Core Idea
Imam Abu Hanifah: liability ensures substantive protection; Sahibayn: removal to trustee prevents treachery. Al-Hidayah favors Abu Hanifah.

In this passage from al-Hidayah, we encounter a scenario where a claimant proves an absent heir's share in movable property, but the possessor denies the claim. The key dispute between Imam Abu Hanifah and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), concerns whether the remaining half should be left with the possessor or taken and placed with a trustworthy trustee. The commentary explores the rationale of each view and provides a tarjih favoring Abu Hanifah's position. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to analyse property protection principles in Hanafi qada.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and legal question
Recognise the factual setting: movable property in the possession of a denier (qabid), where a claimant proves that an absent heir has a share. The question is: what should the judge do with the remaining half after awarding the claimant his share? Should it be left with the possessor or taken and given to a trustee?
This question only arises for movable (manqul) property because immovable (aqar) is inherently secure.
2
State the positions of Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn
Imam Abu Hanifah holds that the remaining half should be left with the possessor. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that it should be taken from him and given to a trustworthy person (amin).
Both views are within the Hanafi school; this is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
3
Analyse the dalil of each side
The Sahibayn argue that movable property needs protection; the possessor has already denied the claim, so he may dispose of it. Removing it to a trustee ensures physical safety. Abu Hanifah responds that leaving it with the possessor provides both formal and substantive protection: if it perishes, the possessor becomes liable (damin) for compensation, so the absent heir's right is always recoverable. A trustee is not liable, so the property is only formally protected.
The key concept is hifz ma'nawi (substantive protection) vs hifz suri (formal protection).
4
Understand the tarjih and its basis
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah declares Abu Hanifah's view more apparent (azhar) and thus mufta bihi. The reason is that the possessor's liability ensures the property's value is preserved even if the physical item is lost, whereas a trustee's non-liability means the absent heir bears the loss.
This tarjih relies on the principle that the stronger protection is that which guarantees compensation.
5
Consider the ruling on taking a surety
The matn states that a surety (kafil) is not taken from the possessor because it would create litigation. The commentary notes that if the present heir demands the surety, the judge's decree to enforce it would end the dispute, not create it, so the rule is not absolute.
This shows that the ruling is contextual and aims to avoid unnecessary litigation.

اشرف البدایہ جلد نہم
اور مال منقول چونکہ بذات خود محفوظ نہیں ہے اس لئے اس کو فروخت کر کے اس کی رقم کی حفاظت کی جائے گی ۔ اسی طرح ماں کا وصی یا بھائی کا وصی یا چا کا وصی ، نا بالغ وارث کے مال منقول کو فروخت کر سکتا ہے۔ حالانکہ ماں، بھائی اور چا کے وھی کو تصرف کا اختیار نہیں ہوتا بلکہ فقط حفاظت کرنے کا اختیار ہوتا ہے مگر چونکہ مال منقول کو فروخت کرنا ، حفاظت ہی کا ایک طریقہ ہے اس لئے ان کے وصی کو ، نا بالغ وارث کے مال منقول کو فروخت کرنے کی اجازت دیدی گئی ہے۔
بعض مشائخ نے فرمایا کہ غیر منقولہ مال کی طرح مال منقول میں بھی اختلاف ہے۔ چنانچہ صاحبین کے نزدیک اگر قاضی منکر ہوا ہو تو دعوی ثابت ہونے پر نصف مال منقول، مدعی کو دے کر باقی نصف بھی قابض کے قبضہ سے نکال کر کسی امین آدمی کے پاس رکھا جائے گا۔ اور حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک مال منقول میں بھی باقی نصف قابض کے قبضہ میں چھوڑا جائے۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ منقول کی صورت میں امام ابو حنیفہ کا قول زیادہ ظاہر ہے کیونکہ منقول مال میں حفاظت کی ضرورت ہے۔ ظاہر ہونے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ صاحبین کے قول سے امام ابو حنیفہ کا قول زیادہ واضح ہے۔ اس لئے کہ نصف مال قابض کے قبضہ میں چھوڑنے کی صورت میں حفاظت زیادہ مکمل ہے یہ نسبت اس کے کہ اس کے قبضہ سے نکال کر کسی امین آدمی سے قبضہ میں رکھا جائے۔ کیونکہ مال قابض کے پاس صورۃ اور معنی دونوں طرح محفوظ ہے۔ اس لئے کہ اگر مال اس کے پاس سے ہلاک ہو گیا تو اس پر مضمان واجب ہوگا۔ اور ضمان اس لئے واجب ہوگا کہ قابض مدعی کے دعوئی کا انکار کرنے کی وجہ سے ضامن ہو گیا ہے۔ اور اگر قابض سے لے کر کسی امین آدمی کے پاس رکھ دیا گیا تو یہ مال معنی محفوظ نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ہلاک ہونے کی صورت میں امین پر مضمان واجب نہیں ہوتا۔ حاصل یہ کہ نصف مال قابض کے پاس بہر صورت محفوظ ہے خواہ ہلاک ہو یا بلاک نہ ہوا ہو۔ اور امین کے پاس ہلاک نہ ہونے کی صورت میں اگر چہ محفوظ ہے لیکن ہلاک ہونے کی صورت میں قطعا محفوظ نہیں ہے۔ اور حضرت امام صاحب کا قول یہ ہے کہ نصف مال قابض ہی کے پاس چھوڑا جائے ۔ اس لئے امام صاحب کا قول صاحبین کے قول کے مقابلہ میں زیادہ واضح ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ یہ جو متن میں کہا گیا کہ قابض سے کفیل نہیں لیا جائے گا۔ اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ کفیل کا لینا جھگڑا پیدا کرنا ہے۔ کیونکہ قابض کفیل دینے سے انکار کرے گا۔ اور قاضی اس سے مطالبہ کرے گا تو جھگڑا پیدا ہو گا۔ حالانکہ قاضی کو جھگڑا پیدا کرنے کے لئے مقرر نہیں کیا جاتا بلکہ جھگڑا ختم کرنے کے لئے مقرر کیا جاتا ہے۔ (عنایہ ) مگر اس دلیل پر اشکال ہے وہ یہ کہ کفیل کا مطالبہ قاضی نہ کرے بلکہ جو وارث حاضر ہے وہ قابض سے کفیل کا مطالبہ کرے اور قابض کنیل دینے سے انکار کرے گا تو جھگڑا قابض اور وارث حاضر میں ہو گا۔ پس قاضی ، کفیل دینے کا فیصلہ کر کے اس جھگڑے کو ختم کرے تو اس صورت میں قابض سے کفیل بھی لیا جا سکے گا۔ اور قاضی کا منصب جھگڑا پیدا کرنے کے لئے بھی نہ ہوگا، بلکہ جھگڑا ختم کرنے کے لئے ہوگا۔
Chapter of Adab al-Qadi. Ashraf al-Bidaya Vol. 9. If someone objects: If the judge and witnesses die, or both forget the incident, and the file burns, then there is a possibility that the possessor (al-qabid) denies the claim? The answer is that this possibility is rare, and no ruling is given for the rare, and the improbable is not considered. If the claim concerns movable property, then by consensus the remaining property is taken from the possessor. "And if the claim concerns movable property, it has been said that it is taken from him by consensus because it needs protection, and removal is more effective in it, unlike immovable property because it is inherently secure. For this reason, the executor has the power to sell movable property on behalf of the adult absent heir but not immovable property. Similarly is the ruling of the executor of the mother, brother, and paternal uncle over the minor. And it has been said that movable property is also subject to disagreement, and the statement of Abu Hanifah regarding it is more apparent because of its need for protection. And the surety is not taken because it would create litigation, while the judge is appointed to cut off litigation, not to create it." Translation: And if the claim concerns movable property, it has been said that by consensus the remaining property is taken from the possessor, because movable property needs protection and removal affords greater protection, unlike immovable property which is inherently secure. For this reason, the executor of the deceased has authority to sell the movable property of the adult absent heir but not the immovable property. The same ruling applies for the executor of the mother, brother, and uncle over the minor. And it has been said that movable property is also subject to disagreement, and in the case of movable property, Abu Hanifah's statement is more apparent because movable property is in need of protection. And the surety is not taken, because taking a surety creates litigation, while the judge is appointed to end litigation, not to create it. Explanation: The author of al-Hidayah said: If the claim concerns movable property, i.e., movable property is in the possession of one person, and another presents evidence that his father has died and left this property as inheritance for him and his absent brother, then the judge will decree half of the property for this claimant, and according to some mashayikh, the remaining half is also taken by consensus from the possessor and given to a trustworthy person, because movable property requires protection, in the sense that being not inherently secure, it can be transferred from one place to another, and removing it from the possessor's possession provides more protection. Because when he has denied the claimant's claim and said that there is no property of the deceased in his possession, he may act treacherously or consider it his own and dispose of it. But when the judge removes it from his possession and places it with a trustworthy person who is apparently just, the property is protected. So for the sake of protection, the remaining half is also taken from the possessor's possession. Unlike immovable property which is inherently secure; there is no possibility of usurpation or theft in it, so there is no harm in leaving it with the possessor. Since movable property is more in need of protection, the executor of the deceased has the authority to sell the share of the absent adult heir that pertains to movable property. If the executor sells it, this sale becomes binding on the absent adult heir. And the executor does not have authority to sell immovable property, because immovable property is inherently secure, so there is no need to sell it. And since movable property is not inherently secure, it is sold to protect its value. Similarly, the executor of the mother, or the executor of the brother, or the executor of the uncle can sell the movable property of the minor heir, even though the mother, brother, and uncle as guardians do not have the power of disposal but only the power of protection. However, since selling movable property is itself a method of protection, their executors are permitted to sell the movable property of the minor heir. Some mashayikh have said that there is disagreement regarding movable property as well, just like immovable property. Thus, according to the Sahibayn, if the possessor is a denier, then when the claim is proven, after giving the claimant half of the movable property, the remaining half is also taken from the possessor's possession and placed with a trustworthy person. According to Imam Abu Hanifah, regarding movable property, the remaining half is left with the possessor. The author of al-Hidayah says: In the case of movable property, the statement of Imam Abu Hanifah is more apparent because movable property needs protection. 'More apparent' means that Imam Abu Hanifah's statement is clearer than the statement of the Sahibayn. This is because leaving the half in the possessor's possession provides more complete protection compared to taking it from his possession and placing it with a trustworthy person. For the property is protected both formally and substantively when with the possessor, because if it perishes in his possession, he becomes liable for compensation. And liability is imposed because the possessor becomes a guarantor (damin) by denying the claimant's claim. If it is taken from him and placed with a trustworthy person, the property is not protected substantively, because in case of loss, the trustee is not liable for compensation. The conclusion is that the half is protected in all circumstances when with the possessor, whether it perishes or not. With the trustee, it is protected if it does not perish, but absolutely not protected if it perishes. And Imam Abu Hanifah's opinion is to leave the half with the possessor; therefore, his opinion is clearer in comparison to that of the Sahibayn. The author of al-Hidayah said: The text states that a surety will not be taken from the possessor. Its proof is that taking a surety creates a dispute. Because the possessor will refuse to give a surety, and the judge will demand it, thereby creating a dispute. Whereas the judge is not appointed to create disputes but to end them. (From al-Inayah) However, there is an objection to this proof: that the demand for a surety could be made not by the judge but by the present heir; the possessor would refuse, and a dispute would arise between the possessor and the present heir. Then the judge, by decreeing that the surety be given, would end this dispute. In that case, the surety could be taken from the possessor, and the judge's office would not be to create a dispute but to end one.
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the procedure for handling movable property when a claimant proves that an absent heir (gha'ib) has a share, but the possessor (qabid) denies the claim. The passage begins by addressing an objection: what if the judge, witnesses, or records are lost? The answer is that such rare possibilities are not considered in legal rulings. Then the focus shifts to movable property (manqul). The matn of al-Hidayah states that in movable property, the remaining half (after giving the claimant his share) is taken from the possessor by consensus because movable property needs protection. However, the commentary explains that there is disagreement: Imam Abu Hanifah holds that the remaining half should be left with the possessor, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it should be taken and given to a trustee (amin). The author of al-Hidayah (al-Marghinani) declares Abu Hanifah's view as more apparent (azhar) because protection is more complete when the property remains with the possessor: he becomes a guarantor (damin) if it is lost, whereas a trustee is not liable. The passage also discusses the authority of executors to sell movable property of an absent adult heir or a minor, contrasting with immovable property which cannot be sold because it is inherently secure. Finally, the issue of taking a surety (kafil) from the possessor is addressed: the matn says a surety is not taken because it would create litigation. The commentary counters that if the present heir demands the surety, then the judge's decree to enforce it would end the dispute, not create it, so the rule is not absolute.

Key Terms
قابض (qabid): The person who has physical possession of the property claimed by the absent heir; he denies the claim.
منقول (manqul): Movable property that can be transferred from place to place and is not inherently secure.
عقار (aqar): Immovable property (real estate) that is inherently secure and cannot be easily stolen or lost.
كفيل (kafil): A surety or guarantor for the appearance of the possessor or the return of the property if needed.
وصى (wasi): An executor appointed by the deceased to manage his estate; has authority to sell movable property for protection.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the tarjih in al-Hidayah, whose view is more apparent regarding leaving the remaining half of movable property with the possessor?
A) Abu Yusuf
B) Muhammad al-Shaybani
C) Imam Abu Hanifah
D) All three agree

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the preferred view (mufta bihi) is to leave the remaining half of movable property with the possessor because his liability as a guarantor provides substantive protection, unlike a trustee who is not liable.

Absent Heir Need Not Re-Present Evidence
Procedural ruling from al-Hidayah on representation of absent heirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi procedural rule for absent heirs and explain the rationale of representation (khasm).

Core Idea
An absent heir need not re-present evidence because the judgment binds all heirs through representation.

This concise ruling from al-Hidayah establishes a key procedural efficiency in Hanafi inheritance litigation. When one heir appears in court and presents evidence, the resultant judgment covers all heirs—including those absent. The reason is that the present heir acts as a representative (khasm) for the others, and the judgment is essentially against the deceased's estate. Understanding this rule prevents redundant litigation and ensures timely distribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the procedural ruling
Read the first part of the source: 'When the absent heir appears, he does not need to re-present evidence.' This is the core ruling—no new bayyinah required.
Focus on the phrase 'لا يحتاج الى اعادة البينة'.
2
Understand the rationale of representation
The source explains that 'one of the heirs stands as a litigant (khasm) on behalf of the others.' This means the present heir legally represents the absent ones in court. Thus, the judgment binds all heirs collectively.
The key term 'خصم' (khasm) denotes this representative capacity.
3
Apply the rule to a scenario
Consider a case: Three siblings inherit a house. One sibling sues the tenant for rent arrears and obtains a judgment. Later, the other two siblings return from abroad. They can claim their shares without bringing new witnesses because the first sibling represented them.
This efficiency prevents the court from rehearing the same evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غائب وارث حاضر ہوا تو اس کو دوبارہ بینہ پیش کرنے کے ضرورت نہیں ہے
و اذا حضر الغائب لا يحتاج الى اعادة البينة وسلم اليه النصف بذلك القضأ لان احد الورثة ينتصب خصماً عن الباقين فيما يستحق له وعليه ديناً كان او عيناً لان المقضى له وعليه انما هو الميت في الحقيقة
When the absent heir appears, he does not need to re-present evidence. "And when the absent one appears, he does not need to re-present evidence, and the half is handed over to him by that judgment because one of the heirs stands as a litigant on behalf of the others regarding what is due to or against them, whether it is a debt or a specific property, because the one for whom and against whom the judgment is given is in reality the deceased."
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from al-Hidayah (matn) followed by a brief rationale. The rule is that when the absent heir (gha'ib) returns, he does not have to bring new evidence (bayyinah) to claim his share. The previous judgment in favor of the present heir is sufficient for the absent heir as well. The reason given is that one heir acts as a representative (khasm) for the others in the litigation, whether the claim is for a debt or a specific property ('ayn). The judgment is considered to be essentially for and against the deceased, so it binds all heirs. This procedural rule ensures efficiency and avoids redundant litigation.

Key Terms
غائب (gha'ib): An heir who is absent from the jurisdiction or unknown at the time of the judgment.
بينة (bayyinah): Evidence, usually witness testimony, required to prove a claim before a judge.
خصم (khasm): A litigant or party in a lawsuit; one heir can stand as khasm for the others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the absent heir not need to re-present evidence according to the Hanafi ruling?
A) Because the judge remembers the previous evidence
B) Because one heir stands as a litigant on behalf of all heirs
C) Because the property is still in the court's custody
D) Because the absent heir has a separate right

Key Takeaway
An absent heir need not re-present evidence because the judgment, obtained by a present heir representing all, binds the entire estate.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Protecting Movable Property in Heir Claims
Intra-Hanafi dispute on custodianship of movables in heir claims.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on leaving movable property with the possessor and explain why the possessor's liability ensures better protection.

Core Idea
Liability (daman) makes the possessor a guarantor, so leaving property with him guarantees protection; an amin lacks this.

In inheritance disputes where some heirs are absent, the court may award half the property to the present claimant. The remaining half, especially if movable, requires careful handling. The Hanafi school debated whether to leave it with the current possessor or place it with a trustee. This lesson examines the views of Imam Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn and the reasoning behind the preferred opinion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the procedural context
Recognize that the discussion arises when movable property is claimed by some heirs and half is awarded to the present claimant.
Movable property cannot be stored safely like immovable.
2
State the dispute
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the remaining half should stay with the possessor; Sahibayn hold it should be placed with an amin (trustee).
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
The possessor becomes a guarantor (daman) by denying the claim, so he must compensate if property is lost. An amin is not liable, so property is less protected.
Protection is both formal (possession) and meaningful (liability).
4
Examine the kafil rule
The text states that a surety (kafil) is not demanded from the possessor because that would create dispute, contrary to the judge's role.
An objection is raised and addressed: if the present heir demands it, the judge can end the dispute by ordering a kafil.
5
Conclude with the tarjih
Sahib al-Hidayah prefers Imam Abu Hanifa's view as more apparent (azhar) and protective.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ یہ جو متن میں کہا گیا کہ قابض سے کفیل نہیں لیا جائے گا۔ اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ کفیل کا لینا جھگڑا پیدا کرنا ہے۔ کیونکہ قابض کفیل دینے سے انکار کرے گا۔ اور قاضی اس سے مطالبہ کرے گا تو جھگڑا پیدا ہو گا۔ حالانکہ قاضی کو جھگڑا پیدا کرنے کے لئے مقرر نہیں کیا جاتا بلکہ جھگڑا ختم کرنے کے لئے مقرر کیا جاتا ہے۔ (عنایہ ) مگر اس دلیل پر اشکال ہے وہ یہ کہ کفیل کا مطالبہ قاضی نہ کرے بلکہ جو وارث حاضر ہے وہ قابض سے کفیل کا مطالبہ کرے اور قابض کنیل دینے سے انکار کرے گا تو جھگڑا قابض اور وارث حاضر میں ہو گا۔ پس قاضی ، کفیل دینے کا فیصلہ کر کے اس جھگڑے کو ختم کرے تو اس صورت میں قابض سے کفیل بھی لیا جا سکے گا۔ اور قاضی کا منصب جھگڑا پیدا کرنے کے لئے بھی نہ ہوگا، بلکہ جھگڑا ختم کرنے کے لئے ہوگا۔
غائب وارث حاضر ہوا تو اس کو دوبارہ بینہ پیش کرنے کے ضرورت نہیں ہے
و اذا حضر الغائب لا يحتاج الى اعادة البينة وسلم اليه النصف بذلك القضأ لان احد الورثة ينتصب خصماً عن الباقين فيما يستحق له وعليه ديناً كان او عيناً لان المقضى له وعليه انما هو الميت في الحقيقة
واحد من الورثة يصلح خليفة عنه فى ذلك بخلاف الاستيفاء لنفسه لانه عامل فيه لنفسه فلا يصلح نائباً عن غيره ولهذا لا يستوفى الانصيبه وصار كما اذا قامت البينة بدين الميت الا انه انما يثبت استحقاق الكل على احد الورثة اذا كان الكل في يده ذكره في الجامع لانه لا يكون خصماً بدون اليد فيقتصر القضاء على ما في يده
ترجمہ اور جب غائب وارث حاضر ہوا تو اس کو دوبارہ مہینہ پیش کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے اور باقی نصف مکان اس کو اسی حکم قضاء سے سپر د کر دیا جائے گا۔ اس لئے کہ وارثوں میں سے ایک وارث بھی باقیوں کی طرف سے ہر اس معاملہ میں خصم ہو جاتا ہے جو اس کے لئے حق ثابت ہو یا اس پر ثابت ہو خواہ دین ہو یا عین ہو۔ اس لئے کہ جس کے لئے حکم قضاء ہو یا جس پر حکم قضاء ہو وہ در حقیقت میت ہے۔ اور وارثوں میں سے ایک وارث بھی اس معاملہ میں میت کی طرف سے خلیفہ ہو سکتا ہے۔ برخلاف اپنی ذات کے لئے حق حاصل کرنے کے۔ کیونکہ اس میں وہ اپنی ذات کے واسطے کام کرتا ہے۔ پس وہ اپنے علاوہ کی طرف سے نائب نہیں ہو سکتا ہے۔ اسی لئے مدعی حاضر صرف اپنے حصہ پر قبضہ کر سکتا ہے اور ایسا ہو گیا جیسے میت کے قرضہ پر گواہ قائم ہوئے مگر یہ کہ کل مال کا استحقاق صرف ایک وارث پر جب ہی ہو گا جبکہ کل ترکہ اسی وارث (حاضر) کے قبضہ میں ہو اس کو جامع کبیر میں ذکر کیا ہے۔ اس لئے کہ وارث حاضر قبضہ کے خصم نہیں ہو سکتا ہے۔ پس حکم قضاء اسی مال پر منحصر ہوگا۔ جس قدر اس کے قبضہ میں ہے۔
تشریح صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ سابق میں گذرا ہے کہ اگر ایک مکان ایک آدمی کے قبضہ میں ہو۔ اور دوسرے آدمی نے بینہ پیش کیا کہ یہ مکان میرے مرحوم باپ کا ہے۔ اس نے میرے اور میرے غائب بھائی کے لئے میراث چھوڑا ہے تو قاضی نصف مکان کا فیصلہ مدعی کے لئے کر کے اس کو نصف مکان دیدے گا۔ اور باقی نصف غائب کی آمد تک کے لئے قابض کے قبضہ میں رہے گا۔ پس جب وہ غائب وارث آگیا تو اپنا حق ثابت کرنے کے لئے اُس پر دوبارہ بینہ پیش کرنا ضروری ہے یا نہیں۔ تو اس بارے میں بعض حضرات کا قول یہ ہے کہ غائب پر حاضر ہونے کے بعد بینہ پیش کرنا ضروری ہے۔ کیونکہ مدعی نے جو ہینہ پیش کیا تھا وہ خاص طور پر اُسی کے لئے تھا۔ پس یہ غائب اپنا حق ثابت کرنے کے لئے دوبارہ بینہ پیش کرے۔ مصنف ہدایہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ غائب کو قابض سے اپنا حصہ لینے کے لئے بینہ پیش کرنے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے بلکہ قاضی کے سابقہ فیصلہ کے نتیجہ میں نصف مکان اس غائب کو حاضر ہونے کے بعد سپر د کر دیا جائے گا کیونکہ مدعی حاضر کا بینہ خود اس کے لئے بھی تھا۔ اور اس کے غائب بھائی کے لئے بھی تھا۔ لیکن اگر یہ کہا جائے کہ غائب کی طرف سے نہ تو کوئی دعوی ہے اور نہ خصم موجود ہے تو مدعی حاضر کا پیش کردہ بینہ غائب کی طرف سے کس طرح معتبر ہو گا ؟ تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ وارثوں میں سے ایک وارث باقی وارثوں کی طرف سے ہر اس معاملہ میں خصم ہو جاتا ہے۔ جس میں میت کے لئے یا میت پر کوئی حق ثابت ہو۔ اور جو حق میت کے لئے یا میت پر ثابت ہو وہ دین ہو یا مال معین ہو۔ یعنی اگر ایک وارث کی موجودگی میں میت کے لئے کوئی حق ثابت ہوا یا میت پر کسی کا کوئی حق ثابت ہوا تو یہ حکم قاضی تمام وارثوں پر نافذ ہو گا ۔ یعنی اگر میت کے لئے کوئی حق ثابت ہوا ہے۔ تو میت کے تمام در ثناء اس میں شریک ہوں گے۔ اور اگر میت پر حق ثابت ہوا تو تمام در ثا ء اس کو ادا کرنے میں شریک ہوں گے۔ گویا تمام ورثاء حاضر میں یعنی وارث حاضر باقی تمام ورثاء کی طرف سے قائم مقام ہو جائے گا۔ نہیں جب ایک وارث باقی تمام ورثاء کی طرف سے خصم ہو جاتا ہے تو مسئلہ مذکورہ میں مدعی حاضر اپنے غائب بھائی کی طرف سے خصم ہو جائے گا۔ اور اس کا پیش کردہ مہینہ جس طرح خود اس
And movable property, because it is not inherently protected, it will be sold and its amount protected. Similarly, the guardian of the mother, or the guardian of the brother, or the guardian of the paternal uncle, can sell the movable property of the minor heir. Although the mother, brother, and paternal uncle do not have the authority to dispose, but only have the authority to protect, yet because selling movable property is a method of protection, their guardians are permitted to sell the movable property of the minor heir. Some mashayikh said that there is a difference regarding movable property like immovable property. According to Sahibayn, if the judge denies, then upon proof of the claim, half of the movable property is given to the claimant, and the remaining half is taken from the possessor's possession and placed with a trustworthy person. And according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the remaining half is left with the possessor even in movable property. Sahib al-Hidayah says that in the case of movable property, the saying of Imam Abu Hanifa is more apparent because movable property requires protection. The meaning of 'apparent' is that the saying of Imam Abu Hanifa is clearer than the saying of the two companions. Because leaving half the property in the possession of the possessor results in more complete protection compared to taking it from his possession and placing it with a trustworthy person. Because the property is protected both apparently and meaningfully with the possessor. This is because if the property is destroyed in his possession, he will be liable for compensation (daman). And compensation becomes obligatory because the possessor, by denying the claimant's claim, becomes a guarantor. And if it is taken from the possessor and placed with a trustworthy person, this property will not be protected meaningfully, because in case of destruction, the trustworthy person does not become liable for compensation. The conclusion is that half the property is protected in every case with the possessor, whether it is destroyed or not. And with the trustworthy person, although it is protected if not destroyed, but if destroyed, it is absolutely not protected. And Imam Sahib's saying is that half the property should be left with the possessor. Therefore, Imam Sahib's saying is clearer in comparison to the saying of the two companions. Sahib al-Hidayah said that what is stated in the text, that a surety will not be taken from the possessor, its proof is that taking a surety is creating a dispute. Because the possessor will refuse to give a surety, and the judge will demand it from him, so a dispute will arise. Although the judge is not appointed to create a dispute, but to end a dispute. (Inayah) But there is an objection to this proof: that the demand for a surety should not be made by the judge, but the present heir should demand a surety from the possessor, and the possessor will refuse to give a surety, so the dispute will be between the possessor and the present heir. Then the judge, by deciding that a surety be given, would end this dispute, so in that case a surety could be taken from the possessor. And the judge's office would not be for creating a dispute, but for ending a dispute. When the absent heir appears, he does not need to present evidence again. And when the absent appears, he does not need to repeat the evidence, and the half is handed over to him by that judgment, because one of the heirs becomes a representative (khasm) for the others in what is established for him or against him, whether it be a debt or a specific property, because the one for whom or against whom the judgment is made is in reality the deceased. And any one of the heirs is suitable as a deputy for him in that, unlike taking for himself, because he acts for himself in that, so he cannot be a deputy for another. Hence, he does not take his own share, and it becomes as if evidence of the deceased's debt is established, except that the entitlement of all is established against one of the heirs only if all (the estate) is in his possession, mentioned in al-Jami', because he cannot be a representative without possession, so the judgment is limited to what is in his possession. Translation: And when the absent heir appears, he does not need to present evidence again, and the remaining half of the house will be handed over to him by that judgment. Because even one of the heirs becomes a representative for the others in every matter where a right is established for him or against him, whether it be a debt or a specific property. Because the one for whom or against whom the judgment is made is in reality the deceased. And any one of the heirs can be a deputy for the deceased in that matter. Unlike obtaining a right for oneself, because in that he acts for himself. So he cannot be a deputy for others. Hence, the present claimant can only take possession of his own share. And it becomes as if evidence of the deceased's debt is established, except that the entitlement of all (the property) is established against only one heir only when the entire estate is in his possession, as mentioned in al-Jami' al-Kabir. This is because the present heir cannot be a representative without possession. So the judgment is confined to that property which is in his possession. Explanation: Sahib al-Hidayah says that it has passed previously that if a house is in the possession of one person, and another person presents evidence that this house belongs to his deceased father, and he left it as inheritance for me and my absent brother, then the judge will decide half the house for the claimant and give him half the house. And the remaining half will remain in the possession of the possessor until the arrival of the absent one. Then, when that absent heir comes, is it necessary for him to present evidence again to prove his right? In this regard, some people say that it is necessary for the absent one to present evidence after appearing, because the evidence that the claimant presented was specifically for himself. So this absent one should present evidence again to prove his right. The author of al-Hidayah has said that the absent one does not need to present evidence to take his share from the possessor; rather, as a result of the judge's previous decision, half the house will be handed over to the absent one after he appears, because the evidence of the present claimant was for himself and also for his absent brother. But if it is said that on behalf of the absent one, there is neither a claim nor an adversary present, how can the evidence presented by the present claimant be valid for the absent one? The answer to this is that one of the heirs becomes a representative for the other heirs in every matter where a right is established for the deceased or against the deceased. And whether the right established for the deceased or against the deceased is a debt or a specific property. That is, if a right is established for the deceased in the presence of one heir, or someone's right is established against the deceased, then this judgment of the judge will apply to all heirs. That is, if a right is established for the deceased, then all heirs will share in it. And if a right is established against the deceased, then all heirs will share in paying it. Thus, all heirs are considered present, meaning the present heir stands in place of all other heirs. In short, when one heir becomes a representative for all other heirs, then in the mentioned case, the present claimant becomes a representative for his absent brother. And his presented evidence, just as it is for himself,
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is a commentary on the chapter of Adab al-Qadi, specifically discussing the procedure when property is claimed by heirs, some of whom are absent. The passage begins by addressing movable property and explaining that guardians of a minor can sell movable property for protection. It then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding whether the remaining half of movable property should be left with the possessor or given to an amin (trustee). The author supports Imam Abu Hanifa's position because leaving property with the possessor ensures better protection: the possessor is liable (daman) if the property is destroyed, whereas an amin is not liable. The passage then discusses the rule that a kafil (surety) is not taken from the possessor, as that would create dispute. However, an objection is raised that if the present heir demands a surety, the judge can decide it and end the dispute, so a surety could be taken. The main ruling is that when the absent heir appears, he does not need to re-present evidence because one heir acts as a representative (khasm) for all heirs in matters concerning the deceased. The evidence presented by the present heir suffices for all, as the judgment is based on the rights of the deceased. The exception is when the entire estate is in the possession of one heir, then only that property is subject to the judgment.

Key Terms
خصم (khasm): One who acts as an adversary/representative in litigation, standing in for another party.
بینہ (bayyinah): Evidence, typically witness testimony, presented in court to prove a claim.
کفیل (kafil): Surety or guarantor who undertakes to produce a person or property if required.
قابض (qabid): Possessor; the person who currently holds the property in question.
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for loss or destruction of property, arising from denial of claim or wrongful possession.
امین (amin): Trustee who holds property without liability for loss unless negligent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is it better to leave the remaining half of movable property with the possessor rather than with an amin?
A) The possessor is more honest.
B) The possessor becomes liable (daman) if the property is destroyed.
C) The amin cannot be trusted.
D) The judge does not have authority to move it.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi procedure, leaving movable property with the possessor is preferred because his liability (daman) provides complete protection, unlike an amin who is not liable.

Absent Heir Need Not Re-Present Evidence
Ruling on absent heir not needing to re-present evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle that one heir acts as khasm for all heirs, so an absent heir does not need to re-present evidence after appearance.

Core Idea
One heir acts as khasm for all heirs in matters concerning the deceased; thus, evidence presented by one suffices for all.

When a court rules on an inheritance claim based on evidence from a present heir, does the absent heir have to start over? This lesson establishes that the absent heir receives his share automatically without new evidence, because the present heir represented all heirs as khasm. The passage also explains the exception when only part of the estate is in the present heir's possession.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
A present heir presents evidence and wins half the property; the other half is held with the possessor pending the absent heir's appearance.
2
Identify the ruling
When the absent heir appears, he does not need to present new evidence. He receives his share based on the prior judgment.
3
Extract the proof
One heir becomes a khasm (representative) for all heirs in matters relating to the deceased, whether the right is for or against the deceased.
The judgment is effectively made for the deceased, so all heirs are bound.
4
Apply the condition
This representation only applies if the entire estate is in the possession of the present heir. Otherwise, the judgment is limited to the property in his possession.
Mentioned in al-Jami' al-Kabir.
5
Conclude
The absent heir benefits from the evidence without re-litigation, streamlining the process.

تشریح صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ سابق میں گذرا ہے کہ اگر ایک مکان ایک آدمی کے قبضہ میں ہو۔ اور دوسرے آدمی نے بینہ پیش کیا کہ یہ مکان میرے مرحوم باپ کا ہے۔ اس نے میرے اور میرے غائب بھائی کے لئے میراث چھوڑا ہے تو قاضی نصف مکان کا فیصلہ مدعی کے لئے کر کے اس کو نصف مکان دیدے گا۔ اور باقی نصف غائب کی آمد تک کے لئے قابض کے قبضہ میں رہے گا۔ پس جب وہ غائب وارث آگیا تو اپنا حق ثابت کرنے کے لئے اُس پر دوبارہ بینہ پیش کرنا ضروری ہے یا نہیں۔ تو اس بارے میں بعض حضرات کا قول یہ ہے کہ غائب پر حاضر ہونے کے بعد بینہ پیش کرنا ضروری ہے۔ کیونکہ مدعی نے جو ہینہ پیش کیا تھا وہ خاص طور پر اُسی کے لئے تھا۔ پس یہ غائب اپنا حق ثابت کرنے کے لئے دوبارہ بینہ پیش کرے۔ مصنف ہدایہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ غائب کو قابض سے اپنا حصہ لینے کے لئے بینہ پیش کرنے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے بلکہ قاضی کے سابقہ فیصلہ کے نتیجہ میں نصف مکان اس غائب کو حاضر ہونے کے بعد سپر د کر دیا جائے گا کیونکہ مدعی حاضر کا بینہ خود اس کے لئے بھی تھا۔ اور اس کے غائب بھائی کے لئے بھی تھا۔ لیکن اگر یہ کہا جائے کہ غائب کی طرف سے نہ تو کوئی دعوی ہے اور نہ خصم موجود ہے تو مدعی حاضر کا پیش کردہ بینہ غائب کی طرف سے کس طرح معتبر ہو گا ؟ تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ وارثوں میں سے ایک وارث باقی وارثوں کی طرف سے ہر اس معاملہ میں خصم ہو جاتا ہے۔ جس میں میت کے لئے یا میت پر کوئی حق ثابت ہو۔ اور جو حق میت کے لئے یا میت پر ثابت ہو وہ دین ہو یا مال معین ہو۔ یعنی اگر ایک وارث کی موجودگی میں میت کے لئے کوئی حق ثابت ہوا یا میت پر کسی کا کوئی حق ثابت ہوا تو یہ حکم قاضی تمام وارثوں پر نافذ ہو گا ۔ یعنی اگر میت کے لئے کوئی حق ثابت ہوا ہے۔ تو میت کے تمام در ثناء اس میں شریک ہوں گے۔ اور اگر میت پر حق ثابت ہوا تو تمام در ثا ء اس کو ادا کرنے میں شریک ہوں گے۔ گویا تمام ورثاء حاضر میں یعنی وارث حاضر باقی تمام ورثاء کی طرف سے قائم مقام ہو جائے گا۔ نہیں جب ایک وارث باقی تمام ورثاء کی طرف سے خصم ہو جاتا ہے تو مسئلہ مذکورہ میں مدعی حاضر اپنے غائب بھائی کی طرف سے خصم ہو جائے گا۔ اور اس کا پیش کردہ مہینہ جس طرح خود اس
And movable property, because it is not inherently protected, it will be sold and its amount protected. Similarly, the guardian of the mother, or the guardian of the brother, or the guardian of the paternal uncle, can sell the movable property of the minor heir. Although the mother, brother, and paternal uncle do not have the authority to dispose, but only have the authority to protect, yet because selling movable property is a method of protection, their guardians are permitted to sell the movable property of the minor heir. Some mashayikh said that there is a difference regarding movable property like immovable property. According to Sahibayn, if the judge denies, then upon proof of the claim, half of the movable property is given to the claimant, and the remaining half is taken from the possessor's possession and placed with a trustworthy person. And according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the remaining half is left with the possessor even in movable property. Sahib al-Hidayah says that in the case of movable property, the saying of Imam Abu Hanifa is more apparent because movable property requires protection. The meaning of 'apparent' is that the saying of Imam Abu Hanifa is clearer than the saying of the two companions. Because leaving half the property in the possession of the possessor results in more complete protection compared to taking it from his possession and placing it with a trustworthy person. Because the property is protected both apparently and meaningfully with the possessor. This is because if the property is destroyed in his possession, he will be liable for compensation (daman). And compensation becomes obligatory because the possessor, by denying the claimant's claim, becomes a guarantor. And if it is taken from the possessor and placed with a trustworthy person, this property will not be protected meaningfully, because in case of destruction, the trustworthy person does not become liable for compensation. The conclusion is that half the property is protected in every case with the possessor, whether it is destroyed or not. And with the trustworthy person, although it is protected if not destroyed, but if destroyed, it is absolutely not protected. And Imam Sahib's saying is that half the property should be left with the possessor. Therefore, Imam Sahib's saying is clearer in comparison to the saying of the two companions. Sahib al-Hidayah said that what is stated in the text, that a surety will not be taken from the possessor, its proof is that taking a surety is creating a dispute. Because the possessor will refuse to give a surety, and the judge will demand it from him, so a dispute will arise. Although the judge is not appointed to create a dispute, but to end a dispute. (Inayah) But there is an objection to this proof: that the demand for a surety should not be made by the judge, but the present heir should demand a surety from the possessor, and the possessor will refuse to give a surety, so the dispute will be between the possessor and the present heir. Then the judge, by deciding that a surety be given, would end this dispute, so in that case a surety could be taken from the possessor. And the judge's office would not be for creating a dispute, but for ending a dispute. When the absent heir appears, he does not need to present evidence again. And when the absent appears, he does not need to repeat the evidence, and the half is handed over to him by that judgment, because one of the heirs becomes a representative (khasm) for the others in what is established for him or against him, whether it be a debt or a specific property, because the one for whom or against whom the judgment is made is in reality the deceased. And any one of the heirs is suitable as a deputy for him in that, unlike taking for himself, because he acts for himself in that, so he cannot be a deputy for another. Hence, he does not take his own share, and it becomes as if evidence of the deceased's debt is established, except that the entitlement of all is established against one of the heirs only if all (the estate) is in his possession, mentioned in al-Jami', because he cannot be a representative without possession, so the judgment is limited to what is in his possession. Translation: And when the absent heir appears, he does not need to present evidence again, and the remaining half of the house will be handed over to him by that judgment. Because even one of the heirs becomes a representative for the others in every matter where a right is established for him or against him, whether it be a debt or a specific property. Because the one for whom or against whom the judgment is made is in reality the deceased. And any one of the heirs can be a deputy for the deceased in that matter. Unlike obtaining a right for oneself, because in that he acts for himself. So he cannot be a deputy for others. Hence, the present claimant can only take possession of his own share. And it becomes as if evidence of the deceased's debt is established, except that the entitlement of all (the property) is established against only one heir only when the entire estate is in his possession, as mentioned in al-Jami' al-Kabir. This is because the present heir cannot be a representative without possession. So the judgment is confined to that property which is in his possession. Explanation: Sahib al-Hidayah says that it has passed previously that if a house is in the possession of one person, and another person presents evidence that this house belongs to his deceased father, and he left it as inheritance for me and my absent brother, then the judge will decide half the house for the claimant and give him half the house. And the remaining half will remain in the possession of the possessor until the arrival of the absent one. Then, when that absent heir comes, is it necessary for him to present evidence again to prove his right? In this regard, some people say that it is necessary for the absent one to present evidence after appearing, because the evidence that the claimant presented was specifically for himself. So this absent one should present evidence again to prove his right. The author of al-Hidayah has said that the absent one does not need to present evidence to take his share from the possessor; rather, as a result of the judge's previous decision, half the house will be handed over to the absent one after he appears, because the evidence of the present claimant was for himself and also for his absent brother. But if it is said that on behalf of the absent one, there is neither a claim nor an adversary present, how can the evidence presented by the present claimant be valid for the absent one? The answer to this is that one of the heirs becomes a representative for the other heirs in every matter where a right is established for the deceased or against the deceased. And whether the right established for the deceased or against the deceased is a debt or a specific property. That is, if a right is established for the deceased in the presence of one heir, or someone's right is established against the deceased, then this judgment of the judge will apply to all heirs. That is, if a right is established for the deceased, then all heirs will share in it. And if a right is established against the deceased, then all heirs will share in paying it. Thus, all heirs are considered present, meaning the present heir stands in place of all other heirs. In short, when one heir becomes a representative for all other heirs, then in the mentioned case, the present claimant becomes a representative for his absent brother. And his presented evidence, just as it is for himself,
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is a commentary on the chapter of Adab al-Qadi, specifically discussing the procedure when property is claimed by heirs, some of whom are absent. The passage begins by addressing movable property and explaining that guardians of a minor can sell movable property for protection. It then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding whether the remaining half of movable property should be left with the possessor or given to an amin (trustee). The author supports Imam Abu Hanifa's position because leaving property with the possessor ensures better protection: the possessor is liable (daman) if the property is destroyed, whereas an amin is not liable. The passage then discusses the rule that a kafil (surety) is not taken from the possessor, as that would create dispute. However, an objection is raised that if the present heir demands a surety, the judge can decide it and end the dispute, so a surety could be taken. The main ruling is that when the absent heir appears, he does not need to re-present evidence because one heir acts as a representative (khasm) for all heirs in matters concerning the deceased. The evidence presented by the present heir suffices for all, as the judgment is based on the rights of the deceased. The exception is when the entire estate is in the possession of one heir, then only that property is subject to the judgment.

Key Terms
خصم (khasm): One who acts as an adversary/representative in litigation, standing in for another party.
بینہ (bayyinah): Evidence, typically witness testimony, presented in court to prove a claim.
ید (yad): Possession, a key concept for standing in litigation; a person without possession cannot act as khasm.
میت (mayyit): Deceased person; the one for or against whom the judgment is in reality made.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for the ruling that an absent heir does not need to re-present evidence after a judgment?
A) The judge has discretion to include absent heirs.
B) One heir acts as khasm for all heirs in matters concerning the deceased.
C) The absent heir is considered to have waived his rights.
D) The property is assumed to be common.

Key Takeaway
An absent heir need not re-litigate because the present heir, as khasm, represents all heirs in establishing the deceased's rights.

One Heir's Evidence Suffices for All Heirs
One heir's evidence suffices for all heirs; absent heir need not re-prove.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that an absent heir need not re-present evidence and explain the legal reasoning (khasm/khalifah) that supports it.

Core Idea
One heir's evidence in court binds all heirs because the case belongs to the deceased.

This passage from Al-Hidayah (Kitab al-Adab al-Qadi) tackles a practical scenario: when one heir proves a property belonged to the deceased, does an absent heir need to present evidence again upon return? The Hanafi school, as presented here, says no. The reasoning hinges on the concept that one heir can represent the deceased and all heirs in litigation (khasm). However, there is a nuance: the present heir can only take his own share, not the absent heir's, because taking possession is a personal act, not a representative one.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Determine what the text rules regarding an absent heir's need to re-present evidence after appearing.
2
Locate the main proof
Find the key legal concepts (khalifah, khasm) that support the ruling and explain how they apply.
3
Note the apparent objection
Understand why someone might think the present heir could take the whole property, and how the text answers this.
4
Analyze the exception
Identify when the judgment covers the entire estate: when the whole property is in the present heir's possession.
Referenced from al-Jami' al-Kabir.

ومن قال مالى فى المساكين صدقة فهو على ما فيه الزكوة وان اوصى بثلث ماله فهو على ثلث كل شئ
And when the absent heir appears, he does not need to present evidence again, and the remaining half of the house will be handed over to him by the same judicial decision. Because one of the heirs becomes a representative for the rest in every matter in which a right is established for or against him, whether it is a debt or a specific property. Because the one for whom judgment is given or against whom judgment is given is in reality the deceased. And one of the heirs can be a deputy for the deceased in that matter. Unlike seeking a right for oneself, because in that he acts for himself, so he cannot be a deputy for others. Hence the present claimant can only take possession of his own share, and it becomes as if evidence was presented for the deceased's debt. But the entitlement of the whole property is established against one heir only if the whole property is in his possession. This is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Kabir, because without possession one cannot be a litigant. So the judgment is limited to what is in his possession.
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Adab al-Qadi (Ashraf al-Hidayah) discusses a scenario where one heir presents evidence that a property belonged to the deceased, and another heir is absent. The ruling states that the absent heir does not need to present new evidence when he appears; the initial judgment benefits all heirs. The reasoning is that one heir can act as a litigant (khasm) for all heirs because the right ultimately belongs to the deceased, and the present heir represents the deceased. However, the present heir can only take his own share; he cannot take the absent heir's share because when taking possession, he acts for himself, not as a deputy. An exception is when the entire estate is in the present heir's possession; then the judgment applies to the whole estate, as per al-Jami' al-Kabir. The passage also clarifies a potential objection: if the present heir represents the deceased, why can't he take the whole property? The answer is that representation is for litigation, not for personal benefit.

Key Terms
خصم (khasm): A litigant or party in a lawsuit; one who represents himself or others in court.
خليفة (khalīfah): Deputy or representative of the deceased in litigation.
بينة (bayyinah): Evidence, usually two male witnesses or one male and two females.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the present heir not have the right to take possession of the absent heir's share after the judgment?
A) Because the absent heir is not present to give permission.
B) Because when taking possession, the heir acts for himself, not as deputy for the deceased.
C) Because the judgment only applies to the present heir's share.
D) Because the absent heir has a separate right that must be proven independently.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, one heir's valid evidence in a property dispute suffices for all heirs because the real litigant is the deceased, and the present heir acts as his deputy.

One Heir Representing Absent Heirs in Property Claims
Ruling with proof via analogy (qiyas) and qualification from al-Jami' al-Kabir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a present heir can represent absent heirs in litigation but can only take his own share in execution, and state the condition (possession) required for such representation.

Core Idea
A present heir represents absent heirs in court, but when taking possession, he acts for himself — so only his share.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies a nuanced point in Hanafi procedural law: one heir can stand as representative for all heirs in a property dispute, making the judge's ruling binding on everyone. However, the representative cannot take possession of the absent heirs' shares because at that point he acts for himself, not as a deputy. The ruling also hinges on a key condition: the present heir must have some possession of the deceased's estate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Understand the factual setting: one heir is present, others absent; a property claim is made against a third party. The present heir sues and provides evidence.
The judge rules that the property belongs to the deceased.
2
Establish the representational capacity
The present heir acts as a representative (khasm) for the absent heirs because the judgment concerns the deceased's estate, and the heir is a caliph of the deceased in litigation.
This is the key principle: representation in litigation is valid.
3
Differentiate between litigation and execution
While the judgment binds all heirs, the present heir can only take possession of his own share. When taking possession, he acts for himself, not as a deputy. The analogy to a debt claim illustrates this: the heir who proves the debt can only collect his share.
This resolves the apparent contradiction.
4
Identify the condition of possession
The representation is valid only if the present heir has possession of some of the deceased's estate. The judge's decision is limited to the value of what the present heir possesses.
Without possession, no one can be a representative (khasm).
5
Apply the ruling to new cases
Use the analogy (qiyas) from the debt case to any similar situation where one heir proves a right belonging to the deceased. The same rule applies: the proving heir can only take his share.
This confirms the general principle.

Book of Adab al-Qadi. Page 352. Ashraf al-Hidayah Volume 9. (Discussion on representation of heirs) The evidence presented by the present plaintiff will be valid on behalf of his absent brother as well. And when the evidence presented by the present plaintiff is valid on behalf of his absent brother, then after the absentee appears, it will not be necessary for him to present evidence again. As for the question of why one heir becomes a representative (khasm) on behalf of the remaining heirs, the answer is that the one for whom the judge gave a decision or against whom the judge gave a decision is in reality the deceased. And one heir can be a caliph and deputy on behalf of the deceased in this matter. So in the aforementioned case, the decision on the house based on the claim of the present heir and the possession of the defendant was in reality for the deceased. That is, the judge decided that this house belongs to the deceased. And when it is established that the house belongs to the deceased, then this house will belong to both the present and absent heirs, because both are heirs of the deceased. So when in one decision the right to the house is established for both the present and absent, there is no need for the absent to prove his right separately. (Then a question and answer) The question: You said that one heir becomes a caliph on behalf of the deceased. If that is correct, then that one heir becomes like the deceased and his representative, and it is permissible for the deceased to take possession of the entire house, so by virtue of being his representative, it should be permissible for this one heir to take the entire house as well. However, by consensus, he is not given more than his share. The answer: When the present heir takes possession of his share, he acts for himself, not for the deceased. And when he acts for himself, he will not be a deputy on behalf of others. This is why the plaintiff (the present heir) can only take possession of his share. This is like a case where one heir establishes witnesses for the deceased's debt. If one heir proves the deceased's debt against someone by evidence, the judge will decide the entire debt against the defendant, but the claimant heir can only collect his share from it. Similarly here, although the judge decided the entire house due to the evidence of the present heir, the present heir will only take his share from it, and he will not be authorized to take the absent heir's share. (Then a qualification) The phrase 'because the right of the whole is established' etc. is an exception to the statement 'one heir becomes a representative on behalf of the rest'. That is, one heir becomes a representative on behalf of the remaining heirs in every matter where there is a right for the deceased or an obligation on the deceased. That is, when the judge decides a right for the deceased or a right against the deceased, this decision will be binding on all heirs. But this is provided that the deceased's estate is in the possession of the present heir. Even if some of the deceased's estate is in the possession of the present heir, the judge's decision will be enforced against this present heir only to that extent. Because without possession, no one can be a representative. So the judge's decision will be limited to the amount of the deceased's estate that is in the possession of the present heir. This is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Kabir.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage discusses a key ruling in Hanafi procedural law: when one heir is present and the others are absent, the present heir can represent the absent heirs in litigation concerning the deceased's property. The judge's ruling on the entire property is binding on all heirs, but the present heir can only take his own share in execution. The author first establishes that the present heir's evidence is valid for the absent heir, so no need for the absent heir to reprove. Then he addresses a potential objection: if the present heir is a representative of the deceased, why can't he take the whole property? The answer is that when taking possession, the heir acts for himself, not for the deceased or absent heirs. He analogizes to a debt claim where the proving heir only collects his share. Finally, a qualification from al-Jami' al-Kabir: this representation only applies if the present heir has possession of some of the estate; the judge's ruling is limited to what he possesses. This shows the Hanafi emphasis on actual possession as a condition for legal representation (khusumat).

Key Terms
خصم (khasm): A representative or litigant who acts on behalf of another party in a legal case.
بینه (bayyinah): Evidence, typically witness testimony, used to prove a claim in court.
استيفاء (istifa): Taking possession or receiving what is due, such as collecting a debt or taking physical control of property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can the present heir only take his share of the house despite the judge's ruling on the entire house?
A) Because the judge's ruling was only for the present heir's share.
B) Because the present heir acts for himself when taking possession, not for the absent heirs.
C) Because the absent heir must approve the sale.
D) Because the property is undivided.

Key Takeaway
A present heir can represent absent heirs in litigation, but execution is limited to his own share because possession is taken for himself, not as a deputy.

Conditions for Dismissal Notification of a Wakeel
Ruling on number and 'adalah required for dismissal notification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions required for a dismissal notification to be effective and distinguish between dismissal testimony, wakalah, and principal's messenger.

Core Idea
Dismissal of a wakeel by testimony requires two witnesses or one just man; but the agency contract and principal's own message do not.

The Hanafi school carefully distinguishes between situations that carry the legal meaning of testimony and those that do not. In this passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah, we learn that when a third party informs a wakeel of his dismissal, it partakes in the nature of testimony and thus requires either two male witnesses or one just man. However, the appointment of a wakeel (wakalah) and the principal's personal message via a messenger are not subject to these strict rules. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the rules of agency in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
Read the passage and list the three distinct situations discussed: dismissal notification by a third party, establishment of wakalah, and dismissal via principal's messenger.
These scenarios have different legal conditions.
2
Extract the condition for dismissal notification
The text states that for a third party's report to effectively dismiss the wakeel, either two men must testify or one just man. Note that the condition includes both number and 'adalah (upright character).
The condition is explicitly stated: 'two men absolutely' or 'one just man'.
3
Contrast with wakalah
The passage explains that wakalah (the contract of agency) does not carry the meaning of imputation (ilzam), so it does not require the conditions of testimony. Even a fasiq person's news is sufficient.
The rationale is a key distinction.
4
Contrast with principal's messenger (qasid)
When the principal sends a messenger to dismiss the wakeel, the messenger is treated as the principal himself. Therefore, no number or 'adalah condition applies.
The message is considered direct from the principal.
5
Apply the rule to a new scenario
Consider a case where a friend tells the wakeel he is dismissed. The friend is one just man. Determine if the dismissal is effective based on the conditions learned.
Test your understanding by applying the condition.

Source Text

کتاب الادب القاضي

اشرف الہدایہ جلد-نم جزوں میں سے ایک جز یعنی عدد یا عدالت کا ہونا شرط ہوگا یعنی یا تو مطلقا دو آدمی گواہی دیں کہ تجھ کو موکل نے معزول کر دیا ہے یا ایک عادل آدمی گواہی دے برخلاف وکالت کے کہ اس میں الزام کے معنی باطل نہیں ہے لہذاوہ شہادت کے معنی میں بھی نہ ہوگی ۔ اور جب وکالت شہادت کے معنی میں نہیں ہے تو اس میں نہ دو کا عدد شروط ہوگا نہ عدالت شرط ہو گی بلکہ ایک فاسق آدمی کی خبر بھی کافی ہو جائے گی۔ اور برخلاف مؤکل کے قاصد کے یعنی اگر مؤکل نے وکیل کو معزول کرنے کے لئے اپنا قاصد بھیجا تو اس میں بھی عدد یا عدالت شرط نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ قاصد کا معزول ہونے کے پیغام کو ادا کرنا ایسا ہے گویا اس نے خود اپنی زبان سے معزول کیا ہے اور خود حاضر ہو کر معزول کرنے کی صورت میں چونکہ نہ عدد شرط ہے اور نہ عدالت شرط ہے اس لئے قاصد کے ذریعہ معزول ہونے کا پیغام بھیجنے کی صورت میں بھی عددیا عدالت شرط نہ ہو گی۔ اور ہر آدمی کو چونکہ ہر وقت بالغ عادل آدمی میسر نہیں آتا اس لئے وکیل کو معزولی کا پیغام پہنچانے کے لئے قاصد بھیجنے کی ضرورت بھی ہے۔
Book of the Conduct of the Judge. 144. From among the parts, one part (i.e., number) or 'adalah is a condition. That is, either two men absolutely testify that the principal has dismissed you, or one just man testifies. Contrary to wakalah, because in it the meaning of imputation (ilzam) is not valid, hence it will not be in the meaning of testimony. And when wakalah is not in the meaning of testimony, then neither number of two nor 'adalah is a condition, rather even the news of a fasiq person will be sufficient. And contrary to the principal's messenger: that is, if the principal sends his own messenger to dismiss the wakeel, then in that also number or 'adalah is not a condition. Because the messenger's delivery of the message of dismissal is as if he himself dismissed him with his own tongue, and in the case of being present and dismissing, since number is not a condition nor 'adalah is a condition, therefore in the case of sending the message of dismissal through a messenger also, number or 'adalah will not be a condition. And because every person does not always have a mature just person available, there is also a need to send a messenger to convey the message of dismissal to the wakeel.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains the conditions required for the effective notification of a wakeel's dismissal. The ruling states that when someone informs the wakeel of his dismissal, if the informer is just a witness, then either two men or one just man is required. This is because the act of informing about dismissal carries the meaning of a testimony (shahadah) that the principal has dismissed him. In contrast, the original contract of wakalah itself does not have this meaning of imputation, so it does not require the conditions of testimony. Therefore, even a fasiq person's news is sufficient for establishing wakalah. Similarly, if the principal sends his own messenger (qasid) to deliver the dismissal, no number or 'adalah is required because the messenger is acting as the principal's direct agent, equivalent to the principal himself speaking. This leniency is practical because people often cannot find two just witnesses at all times. The passage thus distinguishes between three scenarios: dismissal notification (requires testimony), wakalah (no testimony conditions), and principal's messenger (no testimony conditions).

Key Terms
شہادت (shahadah): Testimony in the sense of reporting a fact with legal consequence; here specifically about dismissal of a wakeel.
عدالت ('adalah): The quality of being a just and upright person, fulfilling religious duties and avoiding major sins.
وکالت (wakalah): Agency; the contract by which one person appoints another to act on his behalf.
قاصد (qasid): A messenger sent by the principal specifically to convey the dismissal to the wakeel.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi view, what is required for a third party's report to effectively dismiss a wakeel?
A) Two men or one just man
B) Any one person regardless of character
C) Only the principal himself
D) Two men and one woman

Key Takeaway
Dismissal of a wakeel by a third party requires either two male witnesses or one just man to be effective; wakalah itself and principal's direct message do not require these conditions.
