Intra-Hanafi Dispute on the Reliability of a Fasiq's News
Four intra-Hanafi disputes on the reliability of a fasiq's report

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four cases where Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ on the reliability of a fasiq's news and explain the underlying principle and its practical consequences.

Core Idea
The reliability of a fasiq's news splits the Hanafi school: Imam requires confirmation; Sahibayn treat the informer as a messenger.

This passage from the Hidayah presents four specific cases where Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), disagree on whether news from a fasiq (sinner) is legally sufficient. The root of the dispute is whether 'adalah (moral integrity) is a condition for the credibility of a reporter outside the context of formal testimony. The Sahibayn analogize an informer to a messenger, for whom neither number nor 'adalah are required. The practical consequences affect liability, property rights, marital consent, and religious obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the common issue
Recognize that all four cases share the same unresolved question: can news from a fasiq alone establish a legal consequence without the recipient's confirmation?
The dispute is not about the definition of fisq but about the evidentiary weight of a fasiq's report.
2
Contrast the two principles
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that a fasiq's report is unreliable (ghayr mu'tabar) and requires the recipient's confirmation (tasdiq) to have legal effect. The Sahibayn hold that the report is reliable (mu'tabar) in itself, analogous to a messenger's communication.
The Sahibayn's analogy: every informer is a messenger of the Prophet (PBUH) for conveying obligations; messengers require neither 'adalah nor a specific number.
3
Apply to Case 1: Slave's crime and master's liability
If a fasiq informs the master that his slave committed a crime, and the master then frees or sells the slave without confirming, does that signify acceptance of fidyah (ransom)? According to Imam, no; according to Sahibayn, yes.
The thamarah: the master's financial liability differs.
4
Apply to Case 2: Pre-emption (shuf'ah)
If a fasiq informs a co-owner (shafi') of a sale and the shafi' remains silent, does his right of pre-emption lapse? Imam says no; Sahibayn says yes.
The practical effect: the shafi' may lose the right to buy the share if he does not speak up after hearing the news.
5
Apply to Cases 3 and 4: Marriage consent and obligations for a new Muslim
For a virgin's silence after a fasiq's report of her marriage, Imam says it is not consent; Sahibayn says it is. For a new Muslim in dar al-harb informed by a fasiq of fara'id, Imam says they are not binding without confirmation; Sahibayn says they are binding.
In the fourth case, Shams al-A'imma al-Sarkhasi prefers the Sahibayn's view, analogizing the informer to a messenger.
6
Evaluate the tarjih
While the text does not explicitly prefer one view for the first three cases, for the fourth case Sarkhasi declares the Sahibayn's position as asah (more correct). This suggests a trend toward accepting a fasiq's report for conveying divine obligations.
The mufta bihi for the fourth case is the Sahibayn's view, but for the others it remains a valid ikhtilaf within the school.

Source Text

صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ امام صاحب اور صاحبین کے درمیان مندرجہ ذیل مسائل میں بھی اختلاف ہے۔ پہلا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ غلام نے خطاء کسی کو قتل کیا یا کسی کا مال تلف کیا تو مولیٰ کو اس کے غلام کے جرم کرنے کی خبر دی پھر اس کے بعد مولیٰ نے اس غلام کو آزاد کر دیا یا فروخت کر دیا تو یہ مولیٰ کی طرف سے فدیہ اختیار کرنا ہوگا ۔ گویا مولیٰ نے فدیہ دینے کو اختیار کر لیا ہے اور اگر کسی فاسق آدمی نے خبر دی اور مولی نے اس کے قول کی تصدیق کی تو بھی یہی حکم ہے اور اگر تصدیق نہ کی تو اختلاف ہے۔ چنانچہ حضرت امام صاحب کے نزدیک مولی کا غلام کو آزاد کرنا، یا بیچنا فدیہ اختیار کرنا نہ ہوگا۔ یعنی ایک فاسق کی خبر سے غلام کا مجرم ہونا مولیٰ کے نزدیک ثابت نہ ہوگا اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اس صورت میں بھی فدیہ اختیار کرنا ہے۔ کیونکہ صاحبین کے نزدیک ایک فاسق آدمی کی خبر نے شفیع کو اس بیع کی خبر دی۔ یہ خبر سنکر شفیع خاموش ہو گیا تو اس کا شفعہ ساقط ہو گیا اور اگر کسی فاسق نے خبر دی اور شفیع خاموش ہو گیا تو حضرت امام صاحب کے نزدیک چونکہ یہ خبر نا کافی ہے اسلئے شفیع کا شفعہ ساقط نہ ہوگا۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک چونکہ یہ خبر کافی ہے اس لئے شفیع کے خاموش رہنے سے اس کا شفعہ ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ تیسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر با کرہ کو دو آدمیوں یا ایک عادل نے خبر دی کہ تیرے آدمی نے تیرا نکاح کر دیا ہے وہ خاموش رہی تو بالا تفاق اس کا یہ سکوت رضامندی ہے۔ اور اگر مخبر فاسق ہو تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک چونکہ ایک فاسق آدمی کی خبر غیر معتبر ہے اس لئے اس کا سکوت رضا مندی نہ ہوگا۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک ایک فاسق کی خبر چونکہ معتبر ہے اس لئے باکرہ کا سکوت رضامندی ہوگا۔ چوتھا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جو شخص دار الحرب میں مسلمان ہوا اور دار الاسلام کی طرف ہجرت کر کے نہیں آیا پھر دو مسلمانوں یا ایک عادل مسلمان نے اس کو فرائض کی خبر دی تو فرائض اس پر لازم ہو جائیں گے ۔ حتی کہ ترک فرض سے قضاء لا زم ہوگی۔ اور اگر فاسق مسلمان نے فرائض کی خبر دی اور اس نے تصدیق کر لی تو بھی یہی حکم ہے اور اگر تصدیق نہ کی تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک فرائض اس پر لازم نہ ہوں گے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک لازم ہو جائیں گے۔ صاحب عنایہ نے لکھا ہے کہ شمس الائمہ سرخی نے کہا کہ میرے نزدیک اصح یہ ہے کہ ایک فاسق مسلمان کی خبر سے یہاں فرائض لازم ہو جائیں گے اور ترک کرنے سے قضاء لازم ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ ہر ایک خبر دینے والا رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قاصد اور نیچی ہے اور قاصد میں نہ عدد شرط ہے اور نہ عدالت شرط ہے۔
The author of Hidayah states that there is also difference between Imam Sahib and the Sahibayn in the following issues. The first issue: A slave kills someone by mistake or destroys someone's property, then the master is informed of his slave's crime; thereafter the master frees or sells the slave. This will be considered as the master's choosing to pay the ransom (fidyah), i.e., he has opted to pay the ransom. If a fasiq person gave the news and the master confirmed his statement, the same ruling applies; but if he did not confirm, there is difference. According to Imam Sahib, the master's freeing or selling the slave will not be considered as choosing fidyah, meaning the slave's being a criminal is not proven to the master by the news of a fasiq. According to the Sahibayn, in this case also it is choosing fidyah. [...] The second issue: If a fasiq gives news to a shafi' about a sale, and the shafi' remains silent, then according to Imam Sahib, since this news is insufficient, the shafi's right of pre-emption is not lost; according to the Sahibayn, since this news is sufficient, the silence of the shafi' causes loss of his right of pre-emption. The third issue: If a virgin (bikr) is informed by two people or one just person that your guardian has married you, and she remains silent, then by consensus her silence is consent. If the informer is fasiq, then according to Imam Sahib, her silence is not consent because a fasiq's news is unreliable; according to the Sahibayn, her silence is consent because a fasiq's news is reliable. The fourth issue: A person who becomes Muslim in Dar al-Harb and does not migrate to Dar al-Islam, then if two Muslims or one just Muslim inform him of the obligatory acts (fara'id), they become binding upon him, such that leaving a fard necessitates qada. If a fasiq Muslim informs him of the fara'id and he confirms, same ruling; if he does not confirm, according to Imam Sahib the fard are not binding, and according to the Sahibayn they are binding. The author of al-'Inayah wrote that Shams al-A'imma al-Sarkhasi said: In my view, the more correct (asah) is that from a fasiq Muslim's news, the fara'id become binding, and leaving them necessitates qada, because every informer is a messenger and deputy of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), and for a messenger number and 'adalah are not conditions.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage from the Hidayah commentary presents four intra-Hanafi disputes between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), concerning the legal effect of news from a fasiq (sinner) person. The underlying principle is whether a fasiq's report is credible enough to establish legal consequences. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that a fasiq's report is not reliable unless the recipient confirms its truth, while the Sahibayn consider it reliable in itself. The four cases are: (1) A master informed by a fasiq that his slave committed a crime; if the master then frees or sells the slave, Imam Abu Hanifa does not consider this as acceptance of liability (fidyah) unless the master confirms the news, while the Sahibayn consider it acceptance regardless. (2) In pre-emption (shuf'ah), if a fasiq informs the shafi' of a sale and the shafi' remains silent, Imam Abu Hanifa says the right is not lost because the news is insufficient; the Sahibayn say it is lost. (3) For a virgin's consent to marriage, if a fasiq informs her that her guardian married her, Imam Abu Hanifa says her silence is not consent; the Sahibayn say it is consent. (4) For a new Muslim in dar al-harb, if a fasiq informs him of Islamic obligations, Imam Abu Hanifa says they are not binding unless confirmed; the Sahibayn say they are binding. The commentary of al-'Inayah cites Shams al-A'imma al-Sarkhasi, who prefers the Sahibayn's position in the fourth case, arguing that every informer is a messenger of the Prophet, and messengers require neither number nor 'adalah.

Key Terms
فاسق (fasiq): A person who commits major sins or regularly commits minor sins, lacking 'adalah (moral integrity).
شفعہ (shuf'ah): The right of pre-emption: a co-owner's right to purchase a sold share before a stranger.
فدیہ (fidyah): Ransom or compensation paid by the master for a slave's crime, giving the option to surrender the slave or pay.
قاصد (qasid): A messenger; in the context, the informer is considered a messenger of the Prophet (PBUH) for spreading knowledge of obligations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, if a fasiq informs a co-owner (shafi') of a sale and the shafi' remains silent, what is the ruling?
A) The shafi' loses his right of pre-emption.
B) The shafi' retains his right of pre-emption until he confirms the news.
C) The shafi' must file a lawsuit immediately.
D) The shafi' is not affected by the fasiq's news.

Key Takeaway
The reliability of a fasiq's news is a contested issue within the Hanafi school, with Imam Abu Hanifa requiring confirmation and the Sahibayn treating the informer as a messenger, especially for conveying obligations.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
8 min
No Liability for Qadi or Trustee When Sold Slave is Reclaimed
Ruling that qadi and trustee are not liable for lost price

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling regarding qadi/trustee liability when a sold slave is reclaimed and explain the public interest rationale (maslahah) that justifies the exemption.

Core Idea
To protect the judiciary, qadi and trustee are exempt from liability; the purchaser recovers from creditors.

Imagine a qadi sells a debtor's property, the price is lost, and then the property turns out to belong to someone else. Who bears the loss? This lesson addresses a specific scenario in judicial sales, balancing the need for justice with the practical necessity of encouraging qualified individuals to serve as judges and trustees. The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on analogy (qiyas) and public interest (maslahah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Parties and Transaction
The qadi or his trustee (amin) sells a slave belonging to a debtor (or deceased) for the benefit of creditors. The sale is authorized by the court.
The amin acts as the qadi's deputy.
2
Understand the Loss Scenario
After receiving the price, the money is lost (e.g., destroyed or stolen) before distribution. Later, the slave is reclaimed by its true owner (mustahaqq), who takes it from the purchaser.
The sale is void ab initio due to istihqaq, so the purchaser is entitled to a refund of the price.
3
Locate the Ruling: No Liability
The qadi and amin are not liable (la yadmanun) for the lost price. The purchaser must seek recovery from the creditors.
The ruling aims to prevent reluctance to accept judicial office.
4
Trace the Reasoning: Analogy and Maslahah
The qadi is like an Imam (ruler); the amin is like the qadi—they hold positions of trust. If they were held liable, no one would accept these roles, leading to loss of rights. This is analogous to a case where an agent is under interdiction (mahjur 'alayh): the principal bears responsibility.
The creditors are the principals here because the sale was for their benefit.
5
Apply to Purchaser's Recourse
Since recourse against the qadi/amin is difficult (they are agents), the purchaser recovers from the creditors, just as one recovers from the principal when the agent is a minor or slave.
This ensures the purchaser is not left without remedy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قاضی یا امین نے قرض خواہوں کے واسطے مدیون کے غلام کو فروخت کیا اور مال وصول کیا
پھر وہ مال ضائع ہو گیا اور غلام مستحق ہو گیا تو کوئی ضامن نہ ہوگا
قال واذا باع القاضي أو أمينه عبداً للغرماء و اخذ المال فضاع و استحق العبد لم يضمن لان امين القاضي قائم مقام القاضى والقاضي قائم مقام الامام وكل واحد منهم لا يلحقه ضمان كيلا يتقاعد الناس عن قبول هذه الامانة فتضيع الحقوق و يرجع المشترى عن الغرماء لان البيع واقع لهم فيرجع عليهم عند تعذر الرجوع عـلـى الـعـاقد كما اذا كان العاقد محجوراً عليه ولهذا يباع بطلبهم
ترجمہ اور اگر قاضی یا اس کے امین نے قرض خواہوں کے واسطے مدیون کا غلام فروخت کیا اور مال وصول کیا پھر وہ مال ضائع ہو گیا۔اور وہ غلام مستحق ہو گیا تو کوئی ضامن نہ ہو گا۔ اس لئے کہ قاضی کا امین تو قاضی کا قائم مقام ہے اور قاضی قائم مقام ہے امام مسلمین کا اور ان میں سے کسی کو ضمان لاحق نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ تاکہ لوگ اس امانت کے قبول کرنے سے انکار نہ کریں کہ حقوق ضائع ہو جائیں گے۔ اور مشتری اپنا ثمن قرض خواہوں سے واپس لے گا۔ کیونکہ بیع انہیں لوگوں کے واسطے واقع ہوئی ہے تو مشتری عاقد سے رجوع متعذر ہونے کے وقت انہیں سے واپس لے گا جیسا کہ جب عاقد محجور علیہ ہو اور اسی وجہ سے قرض خواہوں کی درخواست پر غلام فروخت کیا جاتا ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر قاضی یا اس کے امین نے میت کا غلام اس لئے فروخت کیا تا کہ میت کے قرض خواہوں کا قرضہ ادا کرے پس قاضی یا اس کے امین نے ثمن پر قبضہ کیا مگر قاضی یا امین کے قبضہ سے وہ ثمن ضائع ہو گیا اور مذکورہ غلام مستحق ہو گیا یعنی کسی شخص نے اپنا استحقاق ثابت کر کے غلام مشتری سے لے لیا تو عاقد یعنی قاضی اس کا امین اُس ثمن کا ضامن نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ قاضی کا امین قاضی کا قائم مقام ہوتا ہے اور قاضی امام مسلمین کا قائم مقام ہوتا ہے۔ اور امام المسلمین ، قاضی اور امین ان تینوں میں سے کوئی ضامن نہیں ہوتا۔ اس لئے که اگر ان حضرات کو ضامن بنایا گیا تو کوئی اس منصب جلیل کو قبول نہ کرے گا۔ اور جب کوئی اس امانت ( منصب ) کو قبول نہیں کرے گا تو لوگوں کے حقوق ضائع ہو جائیں گے حالانکہ حقوق کا ضائع ہونا ممنوع ہے۔ اس لئے ان میں سے کوئی ضامن نہ ہوگا۔ اور مشتری اپنا ثمن میت کے قرضخواہوں سے واپس لے گا۔ کیونکہ میت کا غلام انہیں قرض خواہوں کے لئے فروخت کیا گیا ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ قاضی یا اس کا امین قرضخواہوں کی درخواست پر میت کا غلام فروخت کرے گا۔ بہر حال جب بیع قرض خواہوں کے لئے سمجھدار کو یا غیر ماذون في التجارة کو کسی نے اپنا غلام فروخت کرنے کا وکیل کیا اور وکالت کے نتیجہ میں غلام فروخت کر دیا۔ اور ثمن لے لیا پھر ثمن ضائع ہو گیا اور غلام مستحق ہو گیا یعنی کسی نے اپنا استحقاق ثابت کر کے غلام مشتری سے لے لیا۔ تو مشتری اپنا ثمن عاقد ( محجورعلیہ) سے واپس نہیں لے سکتا بلکہ ان کے موکل سے واپس لے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ بیع مؤکل ہی کے واسطے واقع ہوئی ہے۔ اسی طرح یہاں قرض خواہوں سے واپس لے گا۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں بیع قرض خواہوں کے لئے ہی واقع ہوئی ہے
If the qadi or his trustee sold a slave for the creditors and took the money, then that money was lost and the slave turned out to be owned by another, no one will be liable. He said: And if the qadi or his trustee sold a slave for the creditors and took the money, then it was lost and the slave was reclaimed, he will not be liable because the qadi's trustee stands in the place of the qadi, and the qadi stands in the place of the Imam, and none of them incur liability (daman), so that people do not refrain from accepting this trust and thus rights be lost. And the purchaser will seek return of his price from the creditors, because the sale occurred for their benefit, so he will seek return from them when recourse against the contracting party becomes difficult, as when the contracting party is under interdiction. For this reason, it is sold at their request. Translation: And if the qadi or his trustee sold the debtor's slave for the creditors and took the money, then the money was lost and the slave was reclaimed, then no one will be liable. Because the qadi's trustee is the representative of the qadi, and the qadi is the representative of the Imam of the Muslims, and none of them incur liability. So that people do not refuse to accept this trust and rights are lost. And the purchaser will take back his price from the creditors. Because the sale occurred for these people, so when recourse against the contracting party becomes difficult, he will take from them, just as when the contracting party is under interdiction. For this reason, the slave is sold at their request. Explanation of the issue: If the qadi or his trustee sold a slave of the deceased in order to pay the deceased's creditors, then the qadi or his trustee took possession of the price, but that price was lost while in their possession, and the aforementioned slave was reclaimed, i.e., someone proved his ownership and took the slave from the purchaser, then the contracting party (the qadi or his trustee) will not be guarantor of that price. Because the qadi's trustee is the representative of the qadi, and the qadi is the representative of the Imam of the Muslims. And none of the Imam, qadi, and trustee incur liability. Because if these persons were made guarantors, no one would accept this great office. And when no one accepts this trust (office), the rights of people will be lost, whereas the loss of rights is prohibited. Therefore, none of them will be liable. And the purchaser will take back his price from the deceased's creditors. Because the deceased's slave was sold for those creditors. That is why the qadi or his trustee will sell the slave at the request of the creditors. In any case, when the sale occurred for the creditors and recourse against the contracting party (qadi or trustee) becomes impossible, then the price will be taken from those creditors. Just as if the contracting party is under interdiction, such as a minor or a slave not permitted in trade, for example, someone appointed a discerning minor or a slave not permitted in trade as an agent to sell his slave, and he sold the slave and took the price, then the price was lost and the slave was reclaimed. Then the purchaser cannot take his price from the contracting party (the one under interdiction), but will take it from their principal. Because the sale occurred for the principal. Similarly here, he will take from the creditors, because in this case the sale occurred for the creditors.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hidayah and its commentary regarding the liability (daman) of a qadi or his trustee (amin) when they sell a debtor's slave to pay creditors. The scenario: The qadi or his trustee sells the slave, receives the price, but then the price is lost (e.g., destroyed or stolen) and after that the slave turns out to belong to a third party (mustahaqq). The third party takes the slave from the purchaser. The question is: who is liable for the lost price? The ruling: The qadi, the trustee, and the Imam are all not liable. The reasoning is that these officials act as representatives of the Muslim community; if they were held liable, no one would accept these positions, leading to the loss of people's rights—a result that must be avoided. Therefore, the purchaser must seek his price from the creditors (ghurama'), because the sale was for their benefit. The text analogizes this to a case where a minor or a non-permitted slave acts as an agent: if the agent is under interdiction (mahjur 'alayh), the purchaser cannot sue the agent but must sue the principal. Here, the creditors are the principals (the sale was for them), so the purchaser returns to them. This ruling is specific to sales made by judicial authorities for creditors; it does not apply to ordinary sales.

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for loss; here, the qadi not being held responsible for the lost price.
امین (amin): A trustee appointed by the qadi to handle sales and other matters; here specifically for selling debtor's property.
مستحق (mustahaqq): A person who proves ownership or right to property, reclaiming it from a buyer.
محجور علیہ (mahjur 'alayh): A person under legal interdiction, such as a minor or insane person, who cannot be sued directly for damages from their contracts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a qadi sells a debtor's slave for creditors, the price is lost, and the slave is reclaimed by its true owner, from whom does the purchaser recover the price?
A) The qadi
B) The trustee (amin)
C) The creditors
D) The debtor

Key Takeaway
Qadi and trustee are exempt from liability in this scenario to protect the judiciary; the purchaser recovers from the creditors, who are the beneficiaries of the sale.

Chain of Recourse in Executor's Sale for Creditors
Ruling with reasoning (ta'lil) on liability chain

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the chain of recourse when an executor's sale for creditors fails due to loss or claim, and apply the rule to analogous cases.

Core Idea
When an executor's sale fails, buyer recovers from executor, who recovers from creditors or estate.

This passage from Kitab al-Adab al-Qadi addresses a practical scenario: a judge orders an executor to sell a deceased debtor's slave to pay creditors. The slave is either reclaimed or dies before delivery, and the sale price is lost. The text establishes a clear chain of recourse—buyer to executor, executor to creditors—and raises a dispute among later scholars about whether the creditor can recover compensation from the estate. Understanding this chain reveals the Hanafi principle of agency and liability in estate management.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The act is the judge's order to the executor to sell the slave for creditors. The ruling is a set of legal consequences: buyer recovers from executor, executor recovers from creditors.
This is not a ruling on validity but on liability.
2
Trace the Chain of Recourse
Follow the chain: buyer → executor → creditors/estate. Understand why each link exists: buyer recovers from executor because executor is the direct counterparty as deputy of the deceased; executor recovers from creditors because he acted for them.
The chain ends with the creditors or the estate if new assets appear.
3
Understand the Reasoning (Ta'lil) Based on Agency
The executor is a deputy (na'ib) of the deceased, even if appointed by the judge. Thus the contract is as if the deceased himself sold. This makes the executor directly liable to the buyer. The executor then recovers from those for whose benefit he acted (creditors or heir).
Agency is key: the executor is not personally liable beyond what he recovers.
4
Note the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Creditor's Compensation
Later scholars (mashayikh) differ on whether the creditor, who paid compensation (ta'awan) to the executor or buyer, can recover that amount from the deceased's estate. One view allows it (loss in the matter of deceased), another disallows (creditor is guarantor since contract was for his benefit).
The matn only gives the first view; the second is added by later commentaries.
5
Apply to the Heir Case
If the estate has no debts, the executor acts for the heir. The same chain applies: buyer recovers from executor, executor recovers from heir. The loss falls on the one for whom the sale was made.
This extension shows the principle is consistent.

کو وصی مقرر کیا تھا تب تو اس کا نائب ہونا ظاہر ہے اور اگر قاضی نے مقرر کیا ہے تو بھی وہ میت کا نائب ہے اس لئے کہ قاضی نے اس کو میت کی طرف سے نائب مقرر کیا ہے نہ کہ اپنی طرف سے بہر حال وصی میت کا نائب ہے۔ اور نائب کا عقد ایسا ہے جیسے منوب عنہ کا عقد ہوتا ہے۔ پس یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ میت نے خود اپنی زندگی میں فروخت کیا ہو۔ اور اس صورت میں مشتری مولیٰ سے رجوع کرنے کا مجاز تھا تو یہاں اس کے قائم مقام گا۔ اب سوال یہ ہے کہ قرضخواہ نے وصی کو جو تاوان دیا ہے مثلاً سو درہم وہ بھی میت کے مال سے لے سکتا ہے یا نہیں؟ بعض مشائخ نے فرمایا کہ اس کو بھی لے سکتا ہے اس لئے کہ یہ بھی اس کو میت ہی کے معاملہ میں دینے پڑے ہیں۔ لہذا اس تاوان یعنی سو درہم کو بھی میت کے مال سے وصول کر لے گا۔ اور بعض مشائخ نے کہا کہ اس کے لئے تاوان کی رقم میت کے مال سے لینے کا حق نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ قرض خواہ اس لئے ضامن ہوا ہے کہ عقد اسی کے لئے واقع ہوا ہے۔ پس جب عقد قرض خواہ کے لئے واقع ہوا تو اس کو اپنے علاوہ سے تاوان کی رقم واپس

اشرف الهدایہ جلد نہم لینے کا حق نہ ہوگا۔
العمر
كتاب الادب القاضي
اور وارث کے لئے اگر ترکہ میں سے کچھ فروخت کیا گیا تو اس کا حکم بمنزلہ قرض خواہ کے ہے۔ مثلاً اگر وارث نابالغ ہو اور ترکہ میں سے کسی چیز کو بیچنے کی ضرورت ہو پس اُس چیز کو وصی نے بیچا اور ثمن لے لیا اور پھر وہ ثمن ضائع ہو گیا اور وہ چیز مستحق ہوگئی تو مشتری اپنا ثمن وصی سے رجوع کرے گا ۔ اور وصی وارث سے رجوع کرے گا۔ کیونکہ جب میت کے ترکہ میں کسی کا قرضہ نہ ہو تو عاقد یعنی وصی وارث کے واسطے کام کرنے والا ہوا۔ اور جس کے لئے کام کیا جائے نقصان کی صورت میں تاوان بھی اسی پر آتا ہے۔
And if the judge ordered the executor to sell [the slave] for the creditors, then the slave was claimed [by another] or died before delivery and the price was lost, the buyer recovers from the executor because he contracted as a deputy of the deceased, even if the judge appointed him; so it is as if the deceased himself sold it. He said: And the executor recovers from the creditors because he acted for them. And if property of the deceased appears, the creditor recovers his debt from it. They said: And it is permissible to say that he recovers the one hundred dirhams he paid as compensation as well, because it occurred to him in the matter of the deceased. And the heir, when [property] is sold, is in the position of the creditor, because if there is no debt in the estate, the contractor acts for him.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with reasoning (ta'lil) from Kitab al-Adab al-Qadi. It addresses a specific scenario: a judge orders an executor to sell a slave belonging to a deceased debtor to satisfy creditors. The slave is either reclaimed by a rightful owner (mustahaqq) or dies before the buyer takes possession, and the sale price is lost. The ruling states that the buyer may recover the price from the executor because the executor acts as a deputy (na'ib) of the deceased. Even if the judge appointed the executor, he remains the deceased's representative, not the judge's. Thus the contract is treated as if the deceased himself made it. The executor then recovers from the creditors because he acted on their behalf. If later the deceased's estate yields money, the creditors can collect their debts from it. A difference among later scholars (mashayikh) arises: some say the creditor can also recover from the estate the compensation (ta'awan) he paid to the executor or buyer, as it is a loss suffered in the deceased's matter. Others say no, because the creditor became guarantor (damin) since the contract was made for his benefit, so the loss falls on him. Finally, the same rule applies to an heir if the estate has no debts: the executor acts for the heir, and any loss is borne by the heir. The reasoning throughout is based on agency and benefit.

Key Terms
وصی (wasi): The executor appointed by the deceased or by the judge to manage the estate.
غرماء (ghuramaa'): Creditors of the deceased to whom debts are owed.
ثمن (thaman): The sale price paid by the buyer.
تاوان (ta'awan): Compensation paid by the creditor to the executor or buyer due to the loss.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a judge orders an executor to sell a deceased debtor's slave for creditors, and the slave is reclaimed by its rightful owner before delivery, from whom does the buyer recover his price?
A) The creditors
B) The executor
C) The judge
D) The deceased's estate

Key Takeaway
The chain of recourse in an executor's failed sale for creditors is buyer → executor → creditors/estate, based on the principle of agency.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
8 min
Acting on a Judge's Oral Punishment Order
Ruling on acting on a judge's oral punishment order

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on acting on a judge's oral punishment order, explain the tarjih (preference) of the later scholars, and apply the conditions under which a judge's word is accepted.

Core Idea
A judge's oral punishment order is not blindly obeyed; evidence must be verified unless the judge is trustworthy and knowledgeable.

This passage from Kitab al-Adab al-Qadi tackles a critical procedural question: can an executioner carry out a judge's verbal sentence (stoning, amputation, flogging) without written documentation? The Hanafi school has an internal dispute, with the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwaya) allowing it, but Imam Muhammad later retracted, requiring evidence due to the risk of irreversible error. The later scholars (mashayikh) preferred Imam Muhammad's caution, except for the judge's written letter. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the practical ruling today.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and the two Hanafi positions
Identify the core question: can one act on a judge's oral statement that he has sentenced someone to a punishment? Recognize that there are two positions within the Hanafi school: the Zahir al-Riwaya (permissible) and Imam Muhammad's retracted view (not permissible without evidence).
This is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf, not a disagreement between schools.
2
Analyze the proofs for each position
For Zahir al-Riwaya: the judge has authority and is free from suspicion; obedience to rulers (ulu'l-amr) is wajib. For Imam Muhammad: the judge's word may be erroneous and punishment cannot be undone; later scholars added concern about corrupt judges.
Note that Imam Muhammad's view is a retraction, making it a nawadir narration that later gained preference.
3
Examine the tarjih (preference) of the later scholars
Understand why the mashayikh preferred Imam Muhammad's view: widespread corruption among judges made caution necessary. Exception: the judge's written letter (kitab al-qadi) is accepted out of necessity.
The exception for the letter shows that written evidence is more reliable than oral statements.
4
Apply Imam Abu Mansur's classification
Analyze the conditions: a just and knowledgeable judge's word is accepted; a just but ignorant judge must explain and if he explains well, his word is accepted; a sinful or ignorant judge's word is rejected unless one personally sees the basis of the judgment.
This classification balances trust with caution based on the judge's character and competence.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
Conclude that the relied-upon position for fatwa is that one should not carry out a punishment based on an oral statement unless evidence (hujja) is produced, except for the judge's written letter. Always verify when in doubt.
This ruling protects against irreversible miscarriages of justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل آخر واذا قال القاضي قد قضيتُ على هذا بالرجم فارجمه أو بالقطع فاقطعه او بالضرب فاضربه .. وسعك ان تفعل وعن محمد انه رجع عن هذا وقال لا تأخذ بقوله حتى تعاين الحجة لان قوله يحتمل الغلط والخطأ والتدارك غير ممكن وعلى هذا الرواية لا يقبل كتابه واستحسن المشائخ هذه الرواية لفساد حال اكثر القضاة في زماننا الا فى كتاب القاضى للحاجة اليه وجه ظاهر الرواية انه اخبر عن امر یملک انشاءه فيقبل لخلوه عن التهمة ولان طاعة اولى الأمر واجبة و فى تصديقه طاعة و قال الامام ابو منصور أن كان عدلا عا لما يقبل قوله لانعدام تهمة الخطا والخيانة وان كان عدلاً جاهلاً يستفسر فان احسن التفسير وجب تصديقه والافلاوان كان جاهلاً فاسقاً او عالماً فاسقاً لا يقبل الا ان يعاين سبب الحكم لتهمة الخطأ والخيانة
ترجمہ اور اگر قاضی نے کہا کہ میں نے اس پر رجم کا حکم دیا سو تو اس کو رجم کر دے یا میں نے اس کے ہاتھ کاٹنے کا حکم دیا سو تو اس کا ہاتھ کاٹ دے یا میں نے اس پر کوڑے مارنے کا حکم دیا سو تو اس کو کوڑے ماردے تو تیرے لئے ایسا کرنا جائز ہے۔ اور امام محمد سے روایت ہے کہ انہوں نے اس قول سے رجوع کیا ہے اور کہا کہ تو اس کا قول مت قبول کر یہاں تک کہ حجت کا مشاہدہ کر لے۔ کیونکہ قاضی کا قول غلطی اور خطاء کا احتمال رکھتا ہے۔ اور تدارک غیر ممکن ہے۔ اور اس روایت کی بنا پر قاضی کا خط قبول نہ ہونا چاہیئے ۔ اور مشائخ نے اس روایت کو مستحسن قرار دیا۔ کیونکہ ہمارے زمانہ میں اکثر قاضیوں کی حالت بگڑی ہوئی ہے۔ سوائے قاضی کے خط کے۔ اس لئے کہ اس کی ضرورت ہے اور ظاہر الروایہ کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اس نے ایسے امر کی خبر دی ہے جس کی ایجاد کا وہ مالک ہے۔ پس تہمت سے خالی ہونے کی وجہ سے قاضی کا حکم قبول ہوگا ۔ اور اس لئے کہ حکام کی فرمانبرداری کرنا واجب ہے۔ اور اس کی تصدیق کرنے میں فرمانبرداری ہے۔ اور امام ابو منصور نے کہا کہ اگر قاضی عالم اور عادل ہو تو اس کا قول قبول کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ خطا اور خیانت کی تہمت معدوم ہے۔ اور اگر قاضی عادل، جاہل ہو تو اس سے استفسار کیا جائے گا۔ پس اگر اس نے اچھی تفسیر بیان کی تو اس کی تصدیق کرنا واجب ہے۔ ورنہ تو نہیں ۔ اور اگر قاضی جاہل فاسق یا عالم فاسق ہو تو اس کا قول قبول نہ ہو گا مگر یہ کہ سبب حکم کا مشاہدہ کرے کیونکہ اس صورت میں خطا اور خیانت کی تہمت ہے۔
Another section: If the judge says, 'I have sentenced this one to stoning, so stone him,' or 'to amputation, so amputate [his hand],' or 'to flogging, so flog [him],' it is permissible for you to do so. And it is narrated from Muhammad that he retracted this and said: Do not accept his word until you see the evidence, because his word is subject to error and mistake, and rectification is impossible. According to this narration, his letter is not accepted. The mashayikh preferred this narration due to the corrupt condition of most judges in our time, except for the judge's letter out of necessity. The reasoning of the apparent narration is that he informed about a matter which he has the authority to create, so it is accepted because it is free from suspicion, and because obedience to those in authority is obligatory, and in affirming him there is obedience. Imam Abu Mansur said: If he is just and knowledgeable, his word is accepted because there is no suspicion of error and betrayal. If he is just but ignorant, he is asked to explain; if he gives a good explanation, his statement must be believed; otherwise not. If he is ignorant and sinful, or knowledgeable and sinful, his word is not accepted unless he witnesses the reason for the judgment, due to the suspicion of error and betrayal.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute from Kitab al-Adab al-Qadi. It deals with the authority of a judge's oral statement that he has passed a specific punishment (stoning, amputation, flogging) on someone. The question is whether another person (e.g., an executioner) can carry out the punishment based solely on the judge's word. According to the Zahir al-Riwaya (the apparent narrated position), it is allowed because the judge has the authority to issue such orders, and trusting him is an act of obedience to those in authority (ulu'l-amr). However, Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani reportedly retracted this view, stating that one should not accept the judge's statement until seeing the evidence (hujja) because the judge's word is fallible and the punishment, once executed, cannot be undone. The later scholars (mashayikh) preferred Imam Muhammad's retracted view due to the corruption of judges at their time, except for a judge's written letter (kitab al-qadi), which is accepted out of necessity. Imam Abu Mansur further classified: a just and knowledgeable judge's word is accepted; a just but ignorant judge must explain and if he explains well, his word is accepted; a sinful or ignorant judge's word is not accepted unless one personally witnesses the basis of the judgment. This classification balances the need for authority with caution against error.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The apparent and most well-known narrated position within the Hanafi school, typically from Imam Muhammad's six books.
حجت (hujja): Evidence or proof that establishes the judgment; here, it refers to written documentation or witnesses confirming the judge's sentence.
كتاب القاضي (kitab al-qadi): A written letter from a judge to another judge or official conveying a judgment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view (as chosen by the mashayikh), when can a judge's oral instruction to carry out a punishment be acted upon?
A) Always, because obedience to authority is wajib
B) Only if the judge is just and knowledgeable
C) Only if the judge provides evidence (hujja) or a written letter
D) Never, under any circumstances

Key Takeaway
The preferred Hanafi position requires written evidence or a judge's letter before carrying out a punishment, protecting against irreversible errors from oral orders.
